Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Intention for Tawaf vs Wuquf: Qurbat Mustaqilla
Distinguishing tawaf and wuquf regarding intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim that tawaf is an independent act of worship (qurbat mustaqilla) to distinguish it from wuquf, and determine when intention is required for each.

Core Idea
Tawaf needs its own intention; wuquf is covered by ihram intention because tawaf is independent worship.

This passage examines a nuanced point in Hajj rituals: why tawaf performed without worshipful intention (e.g., while chasing a debtor) is invalid, but the same scenario at wuquf is valid. The answer lies in the nature of each act—tawaf is an independent act of worship (qurbat mustaqilla), while wuquf is subsumed under the broader ihram intention. Understanding this distinction helps muftis correctly evaluate intention-related issues in Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings for tawaf and wuquf
Note the two cases: performing tawaf while pursuing a debtor (invalid) vs. standing at Arafat while pursuing a debtor (valid). Recognize that both seem analogous, yet rulings differ.
The 'debtor' example is a concrete illustration; the principle applies to any worldly purpose.
2
Analyze the first distinction: independent worship
Understand that Hanafi scholars classify tawaf as qurbat mustaqilla—an independent act requiring its own intention. Wuquf is not independent; it is part of Hajj, already intended via ihram. Thus, tawaf fails without specific intention, wuquf succeeds with ihram intention.
This is the primary distinguishing factor.
3
Examine Zaylai's second distinction: timing relative to tahlul
Zaylai notes that ihram intention covers all acts performed entirely within the state of ihram. Tawaf occurs after partial tahlul (release from ihram), so it is not fully covered. Wuquf occurs entirely within ihram, so the original intention suffices.
This secondary distinction reinforces the first.
4
Apply the maxim to a new scenario
Consider a pilgrim who performs tawaf while distracted, without any conscious intention of worship. Apply the qawida: tawaf requires intention, so it is invalid. Then consider the same pilgrim performing wuquf similarly; it remains valid due to ihram intention.
Test your understanding by varying the scenarios.
5
State the governing qawida and its scope
Formulate the maxim: 'Tawaf is an independent act of worship, unlike wuquf.' Recognize that this is a dabt (sub-maxim) within the chapter of Hajj, and it complements broader qawaid like 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' and 'insihab al-niyyah.'
Memorize the qawida in Arabic: الطَّوَافُ قُرْبَةٌ مُسْتَقِلَّةٌ، بِخِلَافِ الْوُقُوْفِ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالُوا الْطَوَافَ طَالِباً لِغَرِيْمٍ لَا يُجْزِتُهُ، وَلَوْ وَقَفَ كَذَالِكَ بِعَرَفَاتٍ أَجْزَاهُ وَقَدَّمْنَاهُ وَالْفَرْقَ أَنَّ الطَّوَافَ عَهْدُ قُرْبَةٍ مُسْتَقِلَّةٍ، بِخِلَافِ الْوُقُوْفِ وَفَرَّقَ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ بَيْنَهُمَا بِفَرْقٍ آخَرَ، وَهُوَ أَنَّ النِّيَّةَ عِندَ الإِحْرَامِ تَضَمَّنَتْ جَمِيعَ مَا يُفْعَلُ فِي الْأَحْرَامِ، فَلَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى تَجْدِيدِ النِّيَّةِ، وَالطَّوَافُ يَقَعُ بَعْدَ التَّحَلَّلِ، وَفِي الْإِحْرَامِ مِنْ وَجْهِ، فَاشْتَرِطَ فِيْهِ أَصْلُ النِّيَّةِ لَا تَعْيِينُ الْجِهَةِ، إنتهى.
ترجمه: فقہاء کرام فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے قرضدار کا پیچھا کرتے ہوئے طواف کیا تو وہ اس کے لئے کافی نہیں ہے اور اگر اسی طرح عرفات میں ٹھہرا تو وہ اس کے لئے کافی ہے اور اسے ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں اور فرق یہ ہے کہ طواف کو قربت مستقلہ جانا گیا ہے برخلاف وقوف کے اور زیلعی نے ان دونوں کے مابین ایک دوسرا فرق کیا ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ احرام کے وقت کی نیت ان تمام امور کو شامل ہے جو احرام کی حالت میں انجام دیئے جاتے ہیں تو تجدید نیت کی ضرورت نہیں اور طواف من وجہ حلال ہونے کے بعد ہوتا ہے اور من وجہ حالت احرام میں اس لئے اس میں اصل نیت شروط ہے نہ کہ جہت کی تعیین زیلعی کا کلام پورا ہوا۔
تشریح: یہ دونوں مسئلے ماقبل میں گذر چکے ہیں یہاں ان کے درمیان فرق بیان کیا جارہا ہے جن کا حکم الگ الگ ہے اور قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ دونوں مسئلوں کا حکم ایک ہی ہونا چاہئے اور وہ مسئلے یہ ہیں کہ اگر اس نے اپنے مقروض کو تلاش کرنے کی غرض سے وقوف عرفہ کیا تو وقوف عرفہ بیج ہو جائے گا۔ ان دونوں کے مابین ایک فرق تو یہ ہے کہ طواف قربت مستقلہ ہے جس میں تحصیل ضروری ہے لہذا اس کے لئے مستقل نیت کی ضرورت ہے۔ جکہ وقوف عرفہ قربت مستقلہ نہیں بلکہ اس کا حصول ضروری ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے مستقل نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ (۲) دوسرا فریق علامہ زیلعی نے ذکر کیا ہے جو در حقیقت اس کی وضاحت ہے کہ احترام کے وقت کی نیت ان تمام افعال کو شامل ہوتی ہے جو بندہ احرام کے اندر کرتا ہے لہذا تجد ید نیت کی اسے ضرورت نہیں رہتی اور طواف حلال ہونے کے بعد ہوتا ہے اور احترام میں من وجہ ہوتا ہے اس لئے احرام کے وقت کی نیت اس جگہ پورے طور پر موجود نہ رہی جس کی وجہ سے احرام میں اصل نیت کو تو ضروری قرار دیا گیا ہے، تعیین جہت نہیں تو خوان بدون نیت کے ہوا طواف احترام والی نیت کے ضمن میں نہیں ہے۔
They said: If one performs tawaf while pursuing a debtor, it does not suffice him; but if he stands (wuquf) similarly at Arafat, it suffices him, and we have presented this earlier. The difference is that tawaf is considered an independent act of worship, unlike wuquf. Zaylai made another distinction between them: that the intention at the time of ihram encompasses all actions done during ihram, so there is no need to renew intention; but tawaf occurs after the partial release (tahlul) and is only from one aspect in ihram, so for tawaf the basic intention is required, not specification of the direction. End. Translation: The noble jurists say: If someone performed tawaf while pursuing a debtor, it is not sufficient for him; but if he stood at Arafat in the same manner, it is sufficient, and we have explained this earlier. The difference is that tawaf is considered an independent act of worship, contrary to wuquf. Zaylai made another difference between them: that the intention at the time of ihram includes all actions performed during ihram, so there is no need for renewal of intention; and tawaf occurs after the partial release and is from one aspect in ihram, so in it the basic intention is required, not specification of direction. Zaylai's words are complete. Explanation: These two issues have passed earlier; here the difference between them is being explained, whose ruling is different, and analogy would require that the ruling of both issues be the same. The issues are: if he stood at Arafat with the purpose of searching for his debtor, the standing at Arafat will be valid. One difference between them is that tawaf is an independent act of worship, where realization (of intention) is necessary; therefore, a separate intention is needed for it. But wuquf at Arafat is not an independent act of worship; rather, its realization is necessary, so a separate intention is not needed. (2) The second difference is mentioned by Allama Zaylai, which is actually an explanation: the intention at the time of ihram includes all actions that the servant performs during ihram, so he does not need to renew the intention; and tawaf occurs after the partial release and is only from one aspect in ihram, so the intention at the time of ihram does not fully remain there. Therefore, in tawaf, the basic intention is declared necessary, not specification of direction; so tawaf without intention is not included within the intention of ihram.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents a specific legal distinction between two Hajj-related acts: tawaf (circumambulation) and wuquf (standing at Arafat). The scholars rule that if a person performs tawaf while chasing a debtor (i.e., without intending tawaf as worship), it does not count as valid tawaf. However, if one stands at Arafat with the same intention (chasing a debtor), the wuquf is valid. The initial explanation (the first distinction) is that tawaf is an independent act of worship (qurbat mustaqilla), so it requires its own intention, whereas wuquf is part of the Hajj, which is already intended via the ihram. Zaylai provides a second distinction: the intention at ihram covers all actions performed while in the state of ihram. Since tawaf occurs after the tahlul (partial release from ihram), it is not fully covered by the original ihram intention; hence a separate intention is needed. Wuquf, however, occurs entirely within the state of ihram, so the initial intention suffices. The commentary emphasizes that both distinctions are valid and explain why the same logical expectation (qiyas) would have suggested a similar ruling, but the actual ruling differs due to the different natures of the acts.

Key Terms
قربت مستقلہ (qurbat mustaqilla): An act of worship that is independent and self-standing, not merely a part of another worship.
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, initiated by a specific intention.
تحلل (tahlul): Partial or full release from the state of ihram; the first tahlul occurs after stoning and shaving/trimming.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does tawaf require a separate intention while wuquf at Arafat does not, according to the passage?
A) Tawaf is obligatory and wuquf is voluntary.
B) Tawaf is an independent act of worship (qurbat mustaqilla), while wuquf is covered by the ihram intention.
C) Wuquf is longer in duration, so it needs less intention.
D) Tawaf must be performed on foot, requiring intention.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf requires its own intention because it is an independent act of worship, while wuquf is covered by the ihram intention.

The Spreading of Intention Over Pillars: Nafl Tawaf for Fard
Ruling and qawida with two furuat and an exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'niyyat al-ibada tansahabu ala arkaniha' to determine when nafl intention can substitute for fard in acts of worship, and identify the exception when deliberate omission invalidates.

Core Idea
Intention spreads over all pillars; nafl tawaf fulfills fard.

This passage presents a key Hanafi qawida: the intention of worship spreads over all its pillars. The jurists apply it to Hajj: performing tawaf with nafl intention during the days of Nahr suffices for the obligatory tawaf, and similarly for the farewell tawaf. Al-Qunyah then clarifies that if one deliberately omits intention for a non-essential part, the worship is valid but reward is lost; if for an essential pillar, it becomes invalid. For a mufti, understanding this qawida resolves cases of mixed intentions and prevents unnecessary invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Principle
Read the Arabic sentence: 'نِيَّةَ الْعِبَادَةِ تنسحبُ عَلَى أَرْكَائِهَا'. This is the qawida. Understand its meaning: the intention of worship spreads over its pillars, meaning it covers all essential parts once made at the beginning.
This is a sughra qawida, but widely applicable.
2
Analyze the First Fur': Tawaf During Nahr
The passage states that if someone performs tawaf with nafl intention during the days of Nahr, it counts for the obligatory tawaf. Apply the qawida: the intention of worship (even if labeled nafl) spreads over all seven circuits, fulfilling the fard.
This works because the entire tawaf is a single act of worship.
3
Analyze the Second Fur': Tawaf al-Sadr
Similarly, if one performs tawaf after the departure (al-nafr) with nafl intention, it suffices for tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf). Again, the spread of intention covers the obligatory nature.
Tawaf al-sadr is wajib, not fard, but the principle holds.
4
Examine the Exception from al-Qunyah
Al-Qunyah adds that if someone deliberately does not intend worship for some parts of prayer, they lose reward. If that part is essential (a rukn), the worship becomes invalid; if not, it remains valid but sinful. This refines the qawida: the spread covers all parts, but deliberately excluding intention for a rukn breaks the unity.
The key distinction: essential (arkan) vs. non-essential (wajibat/sunan).
5
Connect to Fatwa Practice
As a mufti, when faced with a case of mixed or changed intentions, first identify the act of worship and its pillars. Then apply the qawida to see if the initial intention can cover later actions. Always check if there was a deliberate omission of intention for an essential pillar.
This principle prevents hardship (mashaqqa) for pilgrims who may have intended nafl but actually fulfilled obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالُوا: لَوْ طَافَ بِنِيَّةِ التَّطَوُّعِ فى أيَّامِ النَّحْرِ، وَقَعَ عَنِ الْفَرْضِ، وَلَوْ طَافَ بَعْدَ مَا حَلَ النَّفْرُ، وَنَوَى أَجْزَاهُ عَنِ الصَّدْرِ، كَمَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ وَهُوَ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَىٰ أَنَّ نِيَّةَ الْعِبَادَةِ تنسحبُ عَلَى أَرْكَائِهَا، وَاسْتَفِيدُ مِنْهُ أنَّ نِيَّةَ التَّطَوُّعِ فِي بَعْضِ الْأَرْكَانِ لَا تُبْطِلُهُ. وَفِي القنية : وَإِنْ تَعَمَّدَ أَنْ لا يَنْوِي الْعِبَادَةَ بِبَعْض مَا يَفْعَلُهُ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ لَا يَسْتَحِقُ الثَّوَابَ، ثُمَّ إِنْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ فِعْلَا لَا تَتِمُ الْعِبَادَةُ بِدُوْنِهِ فَسَدَتْ، وَإِلَّا فَلَا، وَقَدْ أَسَاءَ، إِنْتَهَى.
ترجمہ: اور فقہار فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے ایام نحر میں نفل کی نیت سے طواف کیا تو وہ فرض کی طرف سے ہوگا اور اگر او گوں کے احترام سے نکل جانے کے بعد طواف کیا اور نفل کی نیت کی تو وہ اس کے لئے طواف صدر کی طرف ست کافی ہے فتح القدیر میں ایسا ہی ہے اور وہ اس پر مبنی ہے کہ عبادت کی نیت اس کے ارکان پر پھیل جاتی ہے اس سے پتہ چلا کہ بعض ارکان میں تطوع کی نیت اسے باطل نہیں کرتی اور قنیہ میں ہے کہ اگر جان کر ایسا کیا کہ جو نماز وہ پڑھ رہا ہے اس کے بعض افعال میں عبادت کی نیت نہ کرے تو اسے ثواب نہیں ملے گا، پھر اگر وہ فعل ایسا ہو جس کے بغیر عبادت مکمل نہیں ہوتی تو عبادت فاسد ہو جائے گی، ورنہ نہیں، اور اس نے برا کیا، انتہی۔
And they said: If one performed tawaf with the intention of voluntary (nafl) during the days of Nahr, it counts for the obligatory (fard); and if he performed tawaf after the departure (al-nafr) was permitted, and intended, it suffices for tawaf al-sadr, as in Fath al-Qadir. And it is built upon the fact that the intention of worship spreads over its pillars. From this it is understood that the intention of voluntary in some pillars does not invalidate it. And in al-Qunyah: If one deliberately does not intend worship for some of what he does of prayer, he does not deserve reward; then if that action is one without which the worship is not complete, it becomes invalid; otherwise not, and he has done wrong. End. Translation: The jurists say: If someone performed tawaf with the intention of voluntary during the days of Nahr, it will be on behalf of the fard; and if he performed tawaf after the days of departure from Ihram and intended voluntary, it is sufficient for tawaf al-sadr, as in Fath al-Qadir. And it is based on the fact that the intention of worship spreads over its pillars. From this it is learned that the intention of voluntary in some pillars does not invalidate it. And in Qunyah: If one deliberately does not intend worship for some actions of the prayer he is performing, he does not earn reward; then if that action is one without which the worship is not complete, it becomes invalid; otherwise not, and he has done wrong.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about substituting nafl tawaf for fard tawaf, based on the principle that the intention of worship spreads over all its pillars. The Hanafi jurists state that if a person performs tawaf with the intention of nafl during the days of Nahr (the days of sacrifice, i.e., 10th-12th Dhul Hijjah), it fulfills the fard tawaf (the obligatory circumambulation of Hajj). Similarly, if one performs tawaf after the tahlul (partial release) and intended nafl, it suffices for tawaf al-sadr (the farewell tawaf). The underlying rule is that once a valid intention for an act of worship is made, it applies to all its essential parts. Therefore, even if one intends nafl for some pillars, it does not nullify the overall worship. The passage then cites al-Qunyah to clarify a related point: if a person deliberately omits the intention of worship for some parts of the prayer, they forfeit reward. If the omitted part is essential (a pillar), the prayer becomes invalid; otherwise it remains valid but is disliked (makruh). This shows that intentional absence of niyya for non-essential parts does not invalidate the whole act, but it is sinful. The principle reinforces the idea that niyya at the beginning covers the entire act, but deliberate renunciation of niyya for specific parts has consequences.

Key Terms
نية التطوع (niyya al-tatawwu'): Intention to perform a voluntary (nafl) act of worship.
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell circumambulation performed before leaving Mecca after Hajj. Also called tawaf al-wada'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim performs tawaf with the intention of nafl during the days of Nahr, what is the ruling according to the text?
A) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated
B) It counts for the obligatory tawaf due to the spreading of intention
C) It counts only if the pilgrim explicitly intended fard later
D) It is valid but no reward is given

Key Takeaway
The intention of worship spreads over its pillars, allowing nafl intention to fulfill fard in acts like tawaf, unless a deliberate omission of intention for an essential pillar occurs.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

Oaths Based on Wording: Intention vs Expression
Explains the maxim and its application to divorce and emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'Oaths are based on wording, not on intentions' to explicit statements in divorce and emancipation, and distinguish between qada' (court) and diyana (before God) rulings.

Core Idea
Explicit wording determines court rulings; intention matters only before God.

The Hanafi school places great weight on explicit wording in oaths, divorce, and emancipation. This passage introduces a foundational maxim that outward expression governs legal rulings in court, while a person's hidden intention is only considered in the court of Allah. Understanding this distinction is crucial for both qadis (judges) and muftis, as it affects how fatwas are given and how disputes are resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim and its Scope
Locate the qawida 'الأيمان مبنية على الألفاظ لا على الأغراض' in the passage. Understand that it applies to explicit (sarih) statements in oaths, divorce, and emancipation where the wording is clear and unambiguous.
The maxim is cited from Radd al-Mukhtar, with the nuance that it refers to literal wording, not hidden intentions.
2
Distinguish Qada' and Diyana
Note the two levels of ruling: qada'an (in court, based on apparent evidence) and diyanatan (before God, based on true intention). The passage repeatedly uses this distinction.
In Hanafi fiqh, qada' is binding in this world; diyana is a matter of conscience.
3
Apply to Divorce Cases
Examine the first furu': a man says 'anti taliq' intending 'release from a bond' (talaq min withaq). The court rules divorce occurs because the wording is explicit; before God, he is believed if truthful.
This shows the maxim in action: court enforces the apparent meaning.
4
Apply to Emancipation Cases
Similarly, a master says 'anta hurr' intending freedom from a task. The court declares the slave free; diyanatan, not free. Another example: if he intended to say 'subhanallah' but 'anti taliq' came out, she is divorced because the wording is explicit.
The principle applies equally to emancipation.
5
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Disputes
The passage includes two disputes: the preacher story (Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf/Ghazali) and the Qadi Khan case (Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad). Note the different rulings and the author's preferred view.
In the preacher case, the preferred view is that divorce does not occur. In the Qadi Khan case, Abu Yusuf's view (slave not free) is stronger based on the author's reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کر گئی تو کفارہ لازم ہو جائے گا یا اس کا ارادہ کسی شئی کی قسم کھانے کا تھا اس کی زبان سے کچھ اور نکل گیا تو اس کا اختیار ہو گا بشر طیکہ اس نے اللہ کی قسم کھائی ہو۔
الايمان مبنية على الالفاظ لا على الاغراض وتحتہ في رد المختار اى على المقاصد والنيات احترز به عن القول ببنائها على النية (شامل زكريا ج ۵ ص : ۵۳۸)
وَأَمَّا فِي الطَّلَاقِ وَالْعَتَاقِ فَيَقَعُ قَضَاءُ لَا دِيَانَةٌ، وَمِنْ فُرُوعِهِ إِنْ فَصَدَ بِلَفْظِ غَيْرَ مَعْنَاهُ الشَّرْعِيِّ، وَأَمَّا إِنْ قَصَدَ مَعْنِي آخَرُ كَلَفْظِ الطَّلَاقِ إِذَا أَرَادَ بِهِ الطَّلَاقَ مِنْ وَثَاقٍ لَمْ يُقْبَلُ قَضَاءً وَيُدَيَّنُ، وَفِي الْخَانِيَةِ : قَالِ لِعَبْدِهِ : أَنْتَ حُرِّ، وَقَالَ قَصَدْتُ بِهِ عَنْ عَمَلٍ كَذَا، لَمْ يُصَدَّقَ قَضَاءً. :ترجمہ اور بہر حال طلاق وعتاق میں تو وہ قضاء واقع ہوگی دیانی نہیں اور اس کی جزئیات میں سے ہے کہ اگر لفظ سے اس کے معنی شرعی کے علاوہ کا ارادہ کیا اور بہر حال اگر دوسرے معنی کا ارادہ کیا جیسے لفظ طلاق اگر اس سے طلاق من وثاق کا ارادہ کیا ہے تو قضاء قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور دیانہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا اور خانیہ میں ہے کہا اپنے غلام سے انت حر اور اور اس نے کہا میں نے اس سے فلاں کام سے آزاد کرنے کا ارادہ کیا تو اس کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ تشریح : نیت کا محل اصل قلب ہے، اس پر تفریح ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق کے علاوہ کچھ اور کہے کا ارادہ کیا اور زبان سے طلاق نکل گیا یا اپنے غلام کو کسی نام سے پکارنے کا ارادہ کیا اور زبان سے انت حر نکل گیا تو اس صورت میں ویانی یعنی فیما بیند و بین اللہ عورت مطلقہ اور غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا بشرطیکہ معاملہ ایسا ہی ہو۔ البتہ قضاء طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور غلام بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا چوں کہ قضاء ظاہر پر نافذ ہوتی ہے دل کا حال اللہ بہتر جانتا ہے۔ ان اراد التكلم بغير الطلاق فجرى على لسانه الطلاق و تحته في الشامية بان اراد ان يقول سبحان الله فجرى على لسانه انت طالق تطلق لانه صريح لا يحتاج إلى النية ومن فروعه ان قصد بلفظ : اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی کو انت طالق کہا اور اس نے طلاق من وثاق مراد لیانو چونکہ قضا ظاہر پر نافذ ہوتی ہے اس لئے قضاء طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی البتہ دیائی طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی چونکہ کل نیت قلب ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کسی نے اپنے غلام سے انت حر کہا اور مراد اس کی اس سے حرعن العمل تھی تو قضاء غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا چونکہ قضاء کا نفاذ ظاہر پر ہوتا ہے اور دیانہ غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ او یا خرا او یا عتيق ولو قال اردت الكذب او حريته من العمل دين و تحته في الشامية اى فيما بينه و بین الله تعالى اما القاضى فلا یصدقه (شامی ج ۵ : ۳۸۵)

وَقَدْ حُكِي فِي شَرْحِ الْبَسِيط: أَنَّ بَعْضَ الْوُ عَاظِ طَلَبَ مِنَ الْحَاضِرِيْنَ شَيْئًا، فَلَمْ يُعْطَوْهُ، فَقَالَ مُتَضَجّراً مِنْهُمْ : طَلَقَتَكُمْ ثَلاثاً ، وَكَانَتْ زَوْجَتُهُ فِيْهِمْ، وَهُوَلَا يَعْلَمُ فَأَفْتَى إِمَامِ الْحَرَمَيْنِ بِوُقُوْعِ الطَّلَاقِ ثَلَاثَاً، قَالَ الْعَزَالِيُّ: وَفِي الْقَلْبِ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ، إِنْتَهَى ترجمه : اور شرح البسیط میں منقول ہے کہ کسی واعظ نے حاضرین سے کسی چیز کا مطالبہ کیا اورانہوں نے اس کونہ دیا تو اس نے ان کو زجر و توبیخ کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ میں نے تمہیں تین طلاق دیدی حالانکہ اس کی بیوی انہیں میں تھی اور اسے معلوم نہیں تھا تو امام الحرمین نے تین طلاق واقع ہونے کا فتویٰ دیا امام غزائی نے فرمایا کہ اس سے دل میں کچھ تردد ہے شرح بسیط کی بات پوری ہوئی۔
تشریح: شرح بسیط میں ایک مسئلہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے کہ اگر کسی واعظ نے حاضرین سے کچھ کہا اور حاضرین نے اس کی بات پر توجہ نہ دی اس نے زجر و توبیخ کے طور پر کہا تم کو تین طلاق حالانکہ اس کی بیوی بھی اس مجمع میں موجود تھی لیکن واعظ صاحب کو معلوم نہیں تھا تو آیا اس کی بیوی پر طلاق واقع ہوگی یا نہیں تو امام الحرمین نے تین طلاق کے وقوع کا فتویٰ دیا ہے امام محمد بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں لیکن یہ قول غیر مفتی یہ ہے جبکہ امام غزائی عدم وقوع طلاق کے قائل ہیں امام یوسف کا بھی یہی مسلک ہے اور دلائل کے اعتبار سے یہی قول قومی معلوم ہوتا ہے۔
قلْتُ يَتَخَرُجُ عَلَى مَا فِي فَتَاوَى قَاضِي حَانُ مِنْ الْعِلْقِ، قَالَ رَجُلٌ: عَبِيدُ أهْلِ بَلْخَ أحْرَارٌ، أوْقَالَ: عَبَيْدُ أهْلِ بَغْدَادَ أَحْرَارٌ، أَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ عَبْدِ فِي الْأَرْضِ ، أَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ عَبْدِ فِى الدُّنْيَا، قَالَ أَبُوْ يُوْسُفَ لَا يَعْتِقُ عَبْدُهُ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ : يَعْتِقُ. ترجمہ میں کہتا ہوں کہ اس کی تخریج اس پر کی جاسکتی ہے جو فتاوی قاضی خاں کے کتاب العتق میں ہے کہ کسی آدمی نے کہا کہ بلخ والوں کے غلام آزاد ہیں یا کہا کہ بغداد والوں کے غلام آزاد ہیں اور اپنے غلام کی نسبت نہیں کی حالانکہ و وبغداد والوں میں سے تھایا کہا کہ بلخ والوں کا ہر غلام یا کہا بغداد والوں کا ہر غلام آزاد ہے یا کہا کہ ہر وہ غلام جو زمین پر ہے یا کہا کہ ہر وہ غلام جو دنیا میں ہے تو امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کا غلام آزاد نہیں ہوگا اور امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کا غلام آزاد ہو گا۔ تشریح اب جب اوپر والا مسئلہ فقہاء حنفی کے یہاں آیا تو انہوں نے اس کا حکم بیان کرنے کے لئے کچھ نظیریں بیان کی ہیں قاضی خاں نے عشق کے مسائل کے تحت ذکر کیا ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے یہ کہا کہ بلخ والوں کے غلام آزاد میں یا کہا بغداد والوں کے غلام آزاد ہیں اور وہ خود بھی بغداد کا ہے مگر اپنے غلام کی نیت نہیں کی یا کہا کہ بیچ والوں کے تمام غلام آزاد ہیں یا زمین کے تمام غلام آزاد ہیں تو اس کے غلام کی آزادی کا کیا حکم ہوگا۔ اس کے جواب میں امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کا غلام آزاد نہیں ہوگا، امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کا غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اس اختلاف پر
If she did it, expiation becomes obligatory. Or if his intention was to swear by something but his tongue uttered something else, he has choice provided he swore by Allah. Oaths are based on wording, not on intentions. And under it in Radd al-Mukhtar: i.e., on purposes and intentions; he avoided the statement that they are based on intention (Shami Zakariya vol. 5 p. 538). As for divorce and emancipation, they occur in court (qada'an) but not before God (diyanatan). Among its sub-rulings: if he intended by the word a meaning other than its legal meaning, and if he intended another meaning like the word 'talaq' when he intended release from a bond, it is not accepted in court but he is believed before God. In al-Khaniya: someone said to his slave 'you are free' and said 'I intended thereby freedom from such work,' he is not believed in court. Translation: And in any case, in divorce and emancipation, it occurs qada'an not diyanatan. Among its sub-rulings: if he intended by the word something other than its legal meaning, and if he intended another meaning like the word 'talaq' intending release from a bond, it is not accepted qada'an but is accepted diyanatan. In al-Khaniya: he said to his slave 'you are free' and he said 'I intended thereby freedom from such work,' his statement is not accepted qada'an. Explanation: The place of intention is the heart. Based on this, if someone intended to say something other than divorce to his wife and the word 'talaq' came out, or intended to call his slave by a name and 'anta hurr' came out, then diyanatan (between him and Allah) the wife is not divorced and the slave is not free, provided the situation is as such. However, qada'an the divorce occurs and the slave becomes free, because the court acts on the apparent, and Allah knows best the state of the heart. If he intended to speak other than divorce and divorce flowed on his tongue, and under it in al-Shamiyya: if he intended to say 'subhanallah' and 'anti taliq' flowed on his tongue, she is divorced because it is explicit and does not need intention. Among its sub-rulings: if he intended by the word... If someone said to his wife 'anti taliq' and he intended release from a bond, because the court acts on the apparent, therefore qada'an divorce occurs, but diyanatan divorce does not occur because the intention is in the heart. Similarly, if someone said to his slave 'anta hurr' and he intended freedom from work, then qada'an the slave is free because the court acts on the apparent, and diyanatan the slave is not free. Or if he said 'you are free' or 'you are a freedman' and said 'I intended lying' or 'his freedom from work,' he is believed before God. Under it in al-Shamiyya: i.e., between him and Allah Almighty; as for the judge, he does not believe him (Shami vol. 5 p. 385). It has been narrated in Sharh al-Basit: a preacher asked the attendees for something, they did not give it to him, so he said in anger: 'I have divorced you three times,' and his wife was among them, and he did not know. So Imam al-Haramayn gave a fatwa of the occurrence of three divorces. Al-Ghazali said: 'There is something in my heart about it.' End. Translation: In Sharh al-Basit it is narrated that a preacher asked the attendees for something, they did not give it to him, so he rebuked them saying: 'I have given you three divorces,' although his wife was among them and he did not know. So Imam al-Haramayn gave a fatwa of the occurrence of three divorces. Imam Ghazali said: 'There is some hesitation in my heart about it.' The matter of Sharh al-Basit is complete. Explanation: In Sharh al-Basit, a case is mentioned: if a preacher asked the attendees for something and they did not pay attention, he said in rebuke: 'You are thrice divorced,' even though his wife was present in that gathering but the preacher did not know. Will the divorce occur to his wife or not? Imam al-Haramayn gave a fatwa of occurrence of three divorces. Imam Muhammad also holds this view, but this is not the preferred view. Imam Ghazali holds non-occurrence; Imam Yusuf also has this opinion, and based on evidence this opinion is stronger. I say: This can be derived from what is in Fatawa Qadi Khan regarding emancipation: a man said: 'The slaves of the people of Balkh are free,' or said: 'The slaves of the people of Baghdad are free,' or said: 'Every slave on earth,' or said: 'Every slave in the world,' Abu Yusuf said: 'His slave does not become free,' and Muhammad said: 'He becomes free.' Translation: I say that this can be derived from what is in Fatawa Qadi Khan in the Book of Emancipation: if a man said: 'The slaves of the people of Balkh are free,' or said: 'The slaves of the people of Baghdad are free,' and did not specify his own slave, although he was from among the people of Baghdad, or said: 'Every slave of the people of Balkh,' or said: 'Every slave of the people of Baghdad is free,' or said: 'Every slave on earth,' or said: 'Every slave in the world,' then Abu Yusuf says: 'His slave does not become free,' and Muhammad says: 'His slave becomes free.' Explanation: Now that the above issue came before Hanafi jurists, they mentioned some precedents to state its ruling. Qadi Khan mentioned under the issues of emancipation: if a person said: 'The slaves of the people of Balkh are free,' or said: 'The slaves of the people of Baghdad are free,' and he himself is from Baghdad but did not intend his own slave, or said: 'All slaves of the people of such place are free,' or 'All slaves on earth are free,' then what is the ruling on his slave's freedom? In response, Abu Yusuf says: 'His slave does not become free,' Muhammad says: 'His slave becomes free,' upon this difference.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the qawida (maxim) 'الأيمان مبنية على الألفاظ لا على الأغراض' (Oaths are based on wording, not on intentions). The author begins by citing this maxim from the Hanafi tradition, specifically from Radd al-Mukhtar, emphasizing that in explicit statements the literal wording is the basis for legal rulings, not the hidden intention. However, he immediately introduces an important distinction between qada' (court ruling) and diyana (before God). In the case of divorce (talaq) and emancipation (itaq), if the wording is explicit (sarih), the court will enforce the apparent meaning even if the person intended something else. But before God, the person's intention is taken into account. Several sub-rulings (furu') are given: if someone uses the word 'talaq' intending release from a bond (talaq min withaq), the court does not accept his claim (divorce occurs), but he is believed before God. Similarly, if a master says 'anta hurr' to his slave intending freedom from a specific task, the court declares the slave free, but he is not believed before God. The author then quotes a famous story from Sharh al-Basit: a preacher, angry at the congregation, says 'I have divorced you three times' while his wife is present. Imam al-Haramayn ruled that three divorces occur because the wording is explicit and directed at the wife (she was included). Imam al-Ghazali expressed doubt. The Hanafi position, according to Imam Muhammad, supports occurrence, but the author notes that Imam Abu Yusuf and al-Ghazali hold the opposite view, which the author considers stronger. Finally, the author draws an analogy from Fatawa Qadi Khan: if someone makes a general statement freeing all slaves of a certain city, does his own slave become free? Abu Yusuf says no (since he did not intend his own slave), Muhammad says yes (because the general wording includes his slave). This illustrates the same principle: in court, the apparent wording prevails, but intention matters before God.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'an): Ruling by a judge based on apparent evidence; legally binding in this world.
ديانة (diyanatan): Before God; based on the person's true intention; matters of conscience.
صريح (sarih): Explicit wording that clearly indicates the intended meaning without need for intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says to his wife 'You are divorced' (anti taliq) but inwardly intends 'release from a bond'. What is the ruling in court (qada'an)?
A) Divorce occurs because the wording is explicit, regardless of intention.
B) Divorce does not occur because the intention was different.
C) Divorce occurs only if the man had witnesses.
D) Divorce does not occur because the intention matters before God.

Key Takeaway
Explicit wording in divorce and emancipation determines court rulings (qada'), while intention is considered only before God (diyana); the maxim 'الأيمان مبنية على الألفاظ لا على الأغراض' governs, with exceptions for accidental or non-specific statements.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
12 min
General Statements Including the Speaker's Own Property: Talaq, Itq, and Yamin
Analyzing a case of a preacher's divorce pronouncement and analogous rulings on manumission and oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim about general statements that include the speaker's own property, distinguishing rulings for talaq, itq, and yamin based on context and intention.

Core Idea
General statements that include your own property or spouse require context and intention to determine the ruling.

This lesson explores a famous case from Sharh al-Basit where a preacher, angered by an audience's refusal, declared 'I divorce you three times' while his wife was among them. This incident triggers a deep investigation into how general statements affect the speaker's own property and spouse. We will examine the Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on manumission and see how it extends to talaq and oaths, guided by the maxim that context and intention are decisive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
First, understand the underlying qawida: general statements that encompass the speaker's own property or spouse do not automatically apply to them; context and intention (qarina and niyya) determine the ruling. This maxim governs talaq, itq, and yamin.
The maxim is derived from the furuat presented in the passage.
2
Analyze the preacher incident
Focus on the narrated incident: the preacher says 'I divorce you three times' to the audience, unaware his wife is present. Imam al-Haramayn ruled three divorces occurred; al-Ghazali expressed doubt. Note that this incident sets up the problem of general statements.
The preacher's anger and lack of knowledge are key contextual factors.
3
Examine the itq cases and the internal ikhtilaf
Move to the manumission examples. If someone says 'all slaves of Balkh are free' or 'every slave in this alley is free', does his own slave become free? Abu Yusuf says no (context does not indicate intent), Muhammad says yes (literal generality). Note the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view.
This ikhtilaf is the core of the lesson.
4
Note the consensus cases
Identify the two consensus cases: 'every slave in this house is free' (own slaves freed) and 'all children of Adam are free' (own slaves not freed). These define the boundaries of the maxim.
The 'house' case shows that a specific location explicitly including one's property triggers inclusion.
5
Apply the oath analogy
Finally, see how the text analogizes to an oath: if one swears not to speak to Zayd and then greets a group containing Zayd, he is sinful (religious judgment) but not legally guilty (judicial judgment) if he intended only the others. This reinforces the role of intention (dinan vs qada).
The oath analogy helps resolve the preacher's case: if he was in a house, divorce; if in a mosque/alley, the ikhtilaf applies.

وَقَدْ حُكِي فِي شَرْحِ الْبَسِيط: أَنَّ بَعْضَ الْوُعَاظِ طَلَبَ مِنَ الْحَاضِرِيْنَ شَيْئًا، فَلَمْ يُعْطَوْهُ، فَقَالَ مُتَضَجّراً مِنْهُمْ : طَلَقَتَكُمْ ثَلاثاً ، وَكَانَتْ زَوْجَتُهُ فِيْهِمْ، وَهُوَ لَا يَعْلَمُ فَأَفْتَى إِمَامِ الْحَرَمَيْنِ بِوُقُوْعِ الطَّلَاقِ ثَلَاثَاً، قَالَ الْغَزَالِيُّ: وَفِي الْقَلْبِ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ، إِنْتَهَى. وَعَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ الطَّلَاقَ، وَبِقَوْلِ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ أَخَذَ عِصَامُ بِنْ يُوْسُفَ، وَبِقَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ أَخَذَ شَدَّادُ وَالْفَتْوَى عَلَى قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوسُفَ. وَلَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ عَبْدِ فِي هَذِهِ السِّكَةِ وَعَبْدُهُ فِي السِّكَةِ، أَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ عَبْدِ فِي المَسْجِدِ الجَامِعِ حُرُّ، وَهُوَ فِيْهِ، فَهُوَ عَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ. وَلَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ عَبْدٍ فِي هَذِهِ الدَّارُ حُرُّ وَعَبِيدُهُ فِيْهَا يَعْتِقُ عَبِيدُهُ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعاً. وَلَوْ قَالَ: وُلْدَ آدَمَ كُلُّهُمْ أَحْرَارٌ لَا يَعْتِقُ عَبِيدُهُ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعاً. فَمُقْتَضَاهُ أَنَّ الْوَاعِظَ إِنْ كَانَ فِي دَارِ طُلِّقَتْ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الْجَامِعِ أَوِ السِّكَّةِ فَعَلَى الْخِلَافِ، وَالأوْلى تَخْرِيْجُهَا عَلَىٰ مَسْأَلَةِ الْيَمِيْنِ لَوْ حَلَفَ أن لا يُكَلَّمَ زَيْداً، فَسَلَّمَ عَلى جَمَاعَةٍ هُوَ فِيْهِمْ، قَالُوا يَحْنَثُ، وَإِنْ نَوَاهُمْ دُوْنَهُ دَيْنَ دِيَانَةٌ لَا قَضَاء إِنْتَهى.
It has been narrated in Sharh al-Basit that a certain preacher asked the attendees for something, and they did not give it to him. So he said angrily to them: 'I divorce you three times,' while his wife was among them and he did not know. Imam al-Haramayn gave a fatwa that three divorces occurred. Al-Ghazali said: 'There is something in my heart about it.' End. And upon this ikhtilaf is talaq. Isam ibn Yusuf adopted the saying of Abu Yusuf, and Shaddad adopted the saying of Muhammad, and the fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf. If he said: 'Every slave in this alley' while his slave is in the alley, or said: 'Every slave in the congregational mosque is free' while he is in it, then it is on this ikhtilaf. If he said: 'Every slave in this house is free' and his slaves are in it, his slaves are freed by consensus of all. If he said: 'All children of Adam are free,' his slaves are not freed by consensus of all. End. So its implication is that if the preacher was in a house, she is divorced; if he was in the mosque or alley, then it is on the ikhtilaf. And the more appropriate is to derive it upon the case of the oath: if one swore not to speak to Zayd, then greeted a group in which he was present, they said he is sinful; but if he intended only them without him, it is accepted religiously (dinan diyanatan) not judicially (qada).
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a qawida (maxim) with furuat (applications) regarding the effect of general statements that encompass the speaker's own property or spouse. It begins with a narrated incident from Sharh al-Basit: a preacher, angered by the audience's refusal, declared 'I divorce you all three times,' unaware that his wife was among them. Imam al-Haramayn (a prominent Shafi'i scholar) ruled that three divorces occurred, but al-Ghazali expressed doubt. The author then connects this to a Hanafi dispute in Fatawa Qadi Khan about manumission: if someone says 'all slaves of Balkh are free' or similar general statements, does his own slave become free? Abu Yusuf holds no, Muhammad holds yes. The same ikhtilaf applies to talaq. It is then noted that Isam ibn Yusuf followed Abu Yusuf, Shaddad followed Muhammad, and the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view. The passage then provides further furuat: for statements like 'every slave in this alley' or 'in the mosque,' the same ikhtilaf applies; for 'every slave in this house,' consensus that his slaves are freed; for 'all children of Adam,' consensus that his slaves are not freed. From these, the author deduces that if the preacher was in a house, divorce occurs; if in a mosque or alley, it is subject to ikhtilaf. Finally, the author prefers to analogize the preacher's case to an oath case: if one swears not to speak to Zayd and then greets a group including Zayd, he breaks his oath religiously (dinan) but not judicially (qada) if he intended only the others. This illustrates the subtlety of intention in general statements.

Key Terms
الطلاق (al-talaq): Divorce; specifically the pronouncement of divorce by the husband
العتق (al-itq): Manumission; freeing a slave
اليمين (al-yamin): Oath; specifically a vow not to do something

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (fatwa) position in the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding a general manumission statement that includes the speaker's own slave?
A) The slave is freed according to both
B) The slave is not freed according to Muhammad
C) The slave is not freed according to Abu Yusuf
D) The slave is freed only if the speaker explicitly names him

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, a general statement that includes the speaker's own property does not affect that property unless the context indicates intent, as adopted from Abu Yusuf.

General Oaths and Inclusion of the Speaker: A Qawida with Furu'at
Qawida with furu'at on general oaths including the speaker

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'al-yaminu 'ala niyyati al-halif' to determine when a general oath includes the speaker, and state the fatwa position (Abu Yusuf) on the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
In general oaths, the speaker is included by default unless the expression is universally impossible.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: when a person makes a general oath such as 'every slave in this alley is free' and his own slave is present, does the oath affect his slave? The answer depends on whether the expression is truly general or hyperbolic. We will work through several furu'at to see the pattern, and then apply it to a preacher's divorce declaration. The fatwa follows Imam Abu Yusuf's position that the general includes the speaker, absent a clear contrary intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing qawida
The relevant qawida is that oaths are interpreted by the intention of the swearer, but also by the literal meaning when intention is absent. For general expressions, the default is that they include all individuals unless context indicates otherwise.
See the qawida: اليمين على نية الحالف
2
Classify the expression's specificity
Determine whether the location is specific enough to necessarily include the speaker (e.g., 'this house') or more general (e.g., 'this alley', 'the mosque'). The ruling changes accordingly.
House: consensus on inclusion; alley/mosque: ikhtilaf.
3
Apply to the preacher scenario
A preacher says 'every woman in this house/mosque/alley is divorced' while his wife is present. If he is in the house, divorce occurs by consensus. If he is in the mosque or alley, the ikhtilaf applies.
The fatwa (Abu Yusuf) holds that divorce occurs even in the mosque/alley.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf argues the general includes the speaker; Imam Muhammad argues the speaker is excluded by default. Both derive from principles of language and intention.
The thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in whether the slave is freed or wife divorced.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view because it is more cautious and prevents individuals from circumventing oaths by claiming lack of intention.
This is the relied-upon position in the later Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ عَبْدٍ فِي هَذِهِ السِّكَّةِ وَعَبِيدُهُ فِي السِّكَّةِ، أَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ عَبْدٍ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الْجَامِعِ حُرٌّ، وَهُوَ فِيهِ، فَهُوَ عَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ. وَلَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ عَبْدٍ فِي هَذِهِ الدَّارِ وَعَبِيدُهُ فِيهَا يَعْتِقُ عَبِيدُهُ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعًا. وَلَوْ قَالَ: وُلْدُ آدَمَ كُلُّهُمْ أَحْرَارٌ لَا يَعْتِقُ عَبِيدُهُ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعًا. إِنْتَهَى. فَمُقْتَضَاهُ أَنَّ الْوَاعِظَ إِنْ كَانَ فِي دَارِ طُلِّقَتْ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الْجَامِعِ أَوِ السِّكَّةِ، فَعَلَى الْخِلَافِ، وَالْأَوْلَى تَخْرِيجُهَا عَلَى مَسْأَلَةِ الْيَمِينِ: لَوْ حَلَفَ أَنْ لَا يُكَلِّمَ زَيْدًا، فَسَلَّمَ عَلَى جَمَاعَةٍ هُوَ فِيهِمْ، قَالُوا: يَحْنَثُ، وَإِنْ نَوَاهُمْ دُونَهُ دَيِّنَ دِيَانَةً لَا قَضَاءً. إِنْتَهَى. فَعِنْدَ عَدَمِ نِيَّةِ الْوَاعِظِ يَقَعُ الطَّلَاقُ عَلَيْهَا، فَإِنَّ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْيَمِينِ لَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ كَوْنِهِ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّ زَيْدًا فِيهِمْ أَوْ لَا.
And if he said: Every slave in this alley and his slaves in the alley, or said: Every slave in the congregational mosque is free, and he is in it, then it is upon this disagreement. And if he said: Every slave in this house and his slaves in it, his slaves are freed by their consensus. And if he said: The children of Adam all are free, his slaves are not freed by their consensus. End. So its implication is that the preacher if he was in a house, his wife is divorced; and if he was in the mosque or alley, then upon disagreement. And the better is to extrapolate it upon the oath issue: If he swore that he would not speak to Zayd, and then he greeted a group in which Zayd was, they said he breaks his oath; and if he intended them excluding him, he is believed in religious matter not in judicial. End. So when the preacher has no intention, divorce falls upon her, because in the oath case there is no difference between his knowing that Zayd is among them or not.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents a qawida with multiple furuat concerning general expressions in oaths. The author first reiterates the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the effect of a general statement when the speaker is included. For the cases of 'every slave in this alley' or 'every slave in this mosque', there is disagreement: according to Abu Yusuf, the general includes the speaker, so his own slave is freed (or in the divorce analogy, his wife is divorced); according to Muhammad, the general does not include the speaker. The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's position. In contrast, when the location is specific like 'this house', there is consensus that the speaker's slave is freed because the house is a specific container that includes the speaker. When the expression is universal like 'all children of Adam', there is consensus that the speaker's slave is not freed because the universal cannot be intended for a specific. The author then extrapolates to the case of a preacher who says 'every woman in this house is divorced' while his wife is present: if he was in the house, divorce occurs by consensus; if he was in the mosque or alley, it is subject to the same ikhtilaf. The preferred view (al-awla) is to analogize it to the oath case where a person swears not to speak to Zayd and then greets a group including Zayd: he breaks his oath even if he did not intend Zayd, and he is not believed judicially. Therefore, even if the preacher had no intention to divorce his wife, the divorce falls because intention is not required for the legal effect when the expression is general and includes her.

Key Terms
إخْتِلَاف (ikhtilāf): Disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding inclusion of speaker in general oaths.
فَتْوَى (fatwā): The preferred position (Abu Yusuf) used for issuing legal verdicts.
يَمِين (yamīn): Oath; a solemn declaration that carries legal consequences.
نِيَّة (niyya): Intention of the speaker; relevant in oaths but does not override clear general expressions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fatwa, if a preacher standing in the mosque (a public place) says 'every woman in this mosque is divorced' without intending his wife, did the divorce take effect?
A) Yes, because the general includes her irrespective of intention.
B) No, because he did not intend her.
C) Only if he knew she was there.
D) It depends on the size of the mosque.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa holds that a general oath includes the speaker unless the expression is so universal as to be impossible; intention is irrelevant for the legal effect in clear general statements.

The Maxim of Default Freedom and Its Application to Oaths
Commentary on a maxim with analogical extension to oath and divorce rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim 'All children of Adam are free', identify its applications in emancipation and oaths, and apply the istithna' regarding intention.

Core Idea
Freedom is the default for humans; but general utterances may be particularized by intention.

This lesson examines the foundational maxim 'All children of Adam are free' and how it interacts with intention. The maxim sets a default, but its application in concrete cases like a manager's declaration or an oath shows where intention is required and where it is not. We will work through the two main exemplars (furu') provided in the text.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Identify the Arabic text of the maxim and note that it establishes a default presumption of freedom for all humans.
This is a sughra (minor) kulliya maxim governing contracts and oaths.
2
Analyze the manager (منظم) case
Apply the maxim: when a manager says 'every slave in this house is free', his own slave is freed only if he intended to free him. This is an exception (istithna') based on intention.
The intention requirement is due to the complementary maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
3
Analyze the oath case
Consider someone who swore not to speak to Zaid and then greeted a group containing Zaid. Even if he did not intend Zaid, he is guilty (ḥānith) judicially; religiously his intention is considered.
In oaths, generalized utterances take effect judicially regardless of specific intent.
4
Apply the analogy to the preacher (واعظ)
The preacher who says 'you are divorced' without intending divorce is treated like the oath case: divorce occurs judicially because the utterance is general and he is aware of its meaning.
This shows that intention is not required for judicial effect when the utterance is not particularized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولد آدم كلهم احرار : اس میں بالاتفاق منتظم کا نظام آزاد نہ ہوگا الا یہ کہ منظم اپنے نام کے آزاد کرنے کی نیت کرلے۔
كل عبد في هذه الدار ان میں بالا تفاق منتظم کا غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اور باقی جزئیات تیسرے درجہ کی ہیں جن میں من وجہ تخصیص اور من وجہ قسیم ہے ان تمام میں امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان اختلاف ہے۔ فمقتضاه ان الواعظ : علامہ ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ یمین کے ایک مناہ کونظیر بنانا اولی ہوگا کہ اگر کسی نے زید سے بات نہ کرنے کی قسم کھائی تھی پھر اس نے کبھی کسی جماعت کو سلام کیا جس میں زید بھی تھا تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا لیکن اگر سلام کرتے وقت اس نے زید کی نیت نہیں کی تھی تو دیانت اس کی بات معتبر ہوگی ، قضاء نہیں لہذا اس مسئلہ کے اعتبار سے واعظ کی نیت نہ ہونے پر بھی طلاق پڑ جائے گی کیونکہ یمین کے مسئلہ میں زید کے مجمع میں ہونے کے علم ہونے یا نہ ہونے میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے ۔
فَعِنْدَ عَدَمِ نِّيَّةِ الْوَاعِظِ يَقَعُ الطَّلَاقِ عَلَيْهَا، فَإِنْ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْيَمِيْنِ لَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ كَوْ نِهِ يَعْلَمُ ان زيداً فِيهِمْ أَوْلَا. ترجمه تو واعظ کی نیت نہ ہونے کی صورت میں اس پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ مسئلہ یمین میں اس کا کوئی فرق نہیں ہے کہ وہ جانتا ہو کہ زید اسی جماعت میں ہے یا نہ جانتا ہو۔
تشریح مطلب اس عبارت کا گذر چکا ہے۔
ويَتَفَرُّعُ على هذا فُرُوْعَ، لَوْ قَالَ لَهَا: يَا طَالِقُ وَهُوَ اسْمُهَا، وَلَمْ يَقْصُدِ الطَّلَاقِ، قَالُوا: لَا يَقَعُ كَيَاحُرِّ، وَهُوَ أَسْمُهُ، كَمَا فِي الْخَانِيَةِ . وَفَرْقُ الْمَحْبُوبِى فِي التَّلْقِيْحِ بَيْنَ الطَّلَاقِ فَلَا يَقَعُ، وَبَيْنَ الْعِتْقَ فَيَقَعُ خِلَافِ الْمَشْهُورِ ، وَلَوْنَجْزَ الطَّلَاقَ، وَقَالَ: أَرَدْتُ بِهِ التَّعْلِيْقَ عَلَى كَذَا، لَمْ يُقْبَلْ قَضَاء وَيُدَيَّنُ.
ترجمہ: اور اس پر چند جزئیات متفرع ہیں اگر شوہر نے اس سے کہا یا طالق حالانکہ وہ اس کا نام تھا اور اس نے طلاق کا ارادہ نہیں کیا ہے تو فقہاء فرماتے ہیں طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی جیسے یا حر حالانکہ وہ اس کا نام ہے جیسا کہ خانیہ میں ہے محبوبی نے تلقیح میں طلاق اور عشق کے درمیان فرق بیان کیا ہے کہ طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی اور عتق واقع ہو جائے گا تو یہ مشہور کے خلاف ہے اور اگر اس نے بدون تعلیق کے طلاق دی اور کہا کہ میں نے فلاں چیز پر اسے معلق کرنے کا ارادہ کیا تھا تو قضاء اس کا قول قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور دیانہ تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ تشریح: لا يكفى التلفظ باللسان دون القلب پر چند تفریعات بیان کی جارہی ہیں کسی آدمی کی بیوی کا نام طالق تھا اس نے طالق کہہ کر پکارا اور طلاق کا ارادہ اس نے نہیں کیا تھا تو اس کی بیوی پر طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی اسی طرح اگر کسی کے غلام کا نام حر تھا اور اس نے یا حر سے پکارا تو وہ آزاد نہیں ہوگا۔ علامہ ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ اس سلسلہ میں محبوبی نے طلاق و عناق کے درمیان فرق کرنے کے بعد جو یہ بات کہی ہے کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور غلام آزاد نہیں ہوگا ، وہ فقہاء کے قول مشہور کے خلاف ہے۔ وكذا في الطلاق و تحته فى الشامية قال فى البحر و فى اكثر الكتب لم يفرق بينهما لان العلم لم يشترط فيه ان يكون معهوداً والكلام فيما اذا اشهد وقت التسمية فيهما فالظاهر عدم الفرق (شامی زکریاج ۵ : ۳۸۵)
علامہ محبوبی نے دونوں مسئلوں میں جو فرق کیا ہے کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور محقق واقع نہ ہوگی کیونکہ تر نام رکھا جاتا ہے اور مطلقہ یا طالق نام نہیں رکھا جاتا ہے۔ تو محبوبی کا یہ فرق کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ علم میں معبود ہونا شرم نہیں اور انہوں نے فرق کی بنیاد اسی کو قرار دیا ہے۔ ولـو نـجـز الطلاق و قال اردت به : اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق منجز ( بدون تعلیق ) دی پھر وہ ان الفاظ کو تعلیق پر محمول کرنا چاہتا ہے تو دیا یہ اس کی بات قبول کی جائے گی مگر قضاء قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اور طلاق پڑ جائے گی۔ ولو قال ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق يقع الحال الا اذا قال عينت به الطلاق فحينئذ يدين فيما بينه و بين الله تعالى ولايدين فى القضاء ( تارتار خامیة ج ۳ ص ۵۰۲)
وَلَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ إمْرَاقِ لِى طَالِقٌ، وَقَالَ : أَرَدْتُ غَيْرَ فُلَانَةٍ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ كَذَالِكَ، وَفِي الكنْ لَوْ قَالَتْ: تَزَوَّجُتَ عَلَى فَقَالَ: كُلُّ إِمْرَأَةٍ لِى طَالِقٌ طُلْقَتِ الْمُحَلِّفَةُ ، وَفِي شَرْحِ الْجَامِعِ لِقَاضِي حَانَ، وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوْسُفَ أَنَّهَا لَا تُطَلَّقُ، وَبِهِ أَخَذَ مَشَائِحُنَا، وَفِي الْمَبْسُوط وَقَوْلُ أبي يُوْسُفَ أَصَحُ عِنْدِي.
ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے کہا کہ میری ہر بیوی کو طلاق اور کہا کہ میں نے فلاں بیوی کے علاوہ کا ارادہ کیا تھاتو اس طرح کا قول قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور کنز الدقائق میں ہے کہ اگر بیوی نے (شوہر سے) کہا کیا تو نے میرے علاوہ کسی سے شادی کی ہے تو اس پر اس نے کہا کہ میری ہر بیوی کو طلاق تو حلف دلانے والی پر بھی طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور قاضی خاں کی شرح الجامع میں ہے کہ امام یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ اسے طلاق نہیں ہوگی اور ہمارے مشائخ نے اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے اور مبسوط میں ہے کہ ابو یوسف کا قول میرے نزدیک اصح ہے۔
تشریح کسی آدمی کی کئی بیویاں تھیں اس نے کل امراہ لی طالق کہا تو اس کی ہر بیوی مطلقہ ہو جائے گی اور اس کی استثناء کی نیت کسی بیوی کے بارے میں معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ و فی الکنز : کسی کی بیوی نے اپنے شوہر سے دریافت کیا کہ تو نے میرے علاوہ کسی سے شادی کی ہے؟ شوہر نے کہا میری ہر بیوی کو طلاق تو اب قسم کھلانے والی بھی چونکہ اس کی بیوی ہے اس پر طلاق ہوگی یا نہیں اس سلسلہ میں
All children of Adam are free: in this, by consensus, the manager's system will not be free unless the manager intends to free his name. Every slave in this house: by consensus, the manager's slave will be freed, and the remaining details are of the third level, which are partially specific and partially general; in all these, there is a difference between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. So its implication is the preacher: Allama Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says that making an analogy of an oath is better: if someone swore not to speak to Zaid, then he greeted a group including Zaid, he would be guilty of oath-breaking, but if at the time of greeting he did not intend Zaid, his statement would be valid religiously, not judicially. Therefore, by this issue, even without the preacher's intention, divorce will occur because in the oath issue, there is no difference between knowing that Zaid is in the group or not. So when the preacher has no intention, divorce occurs upon her, for in the case of an oath, there is no difference between his knowing that Zaid is among them or not. Explanation of this has passed. And there branch from this several sub-issues: If he said to her, 'O Taliq' – and that is her name – and he did not intend divorce, they said: It does not occur, like 'O Free' – and that is his name – as in al-Khaniyya. And al-Mahbubi in al-Talqih made a distinction between divorce – it does not occur – and emancipation – it occurs – contrary to the famous view. And if he gave a definite divorce and said, 'I intended by it a conditional upon such-and-such,' it is not accepted judicially but is accepted religiously. Explanation: Several branches are being stated on 'utterance with the tongue without the heart is insufficient.' A man's wife was named Taliq; he called her 'Taliq' without intending divorce; divorce would not occur. Similarly, if someone's slave was named Free and he called him 'O Free', he would not be freed. Allama Ibn Nujaym says that al-Mahbubi's distinction that divorce occurs but emancipation does not is contrary to the famous view. And likewise in divorce, under it in al-Shamiyya, it is said in al-Bahr and in most books that there is no distinction between them because knowledge does not require that it be customary; the discussion is about when he witnesses at the time of naming; the apparent is no distinction. Al-Mahbubi's distinction that divorce occurs but emancipation does not because a slave is given that name but a divorced woman or Taliq is not named – his distinction is incorrect because knowledge of being customary is not required, and he based the distinction on that. And if he gave a definite divorce and said, 'I intended by it to be conditional,' then religiously his statement is accepted but not judicially, and divorce will occur. And if he said, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' it occurs immediately unless he said, 'I intended by it the divorce,' then he is believed between himself and Allah, not in court. And if he said, 'Every wife of mine is divorced' and said, 'I intended other than so-and-so,' it is not accepted likewise. And in al-Kanz: if she said, 'Did you marry another?' and he said, 'Every wife of mine is divorced,' the one who made him swear will also be divorced. And in Sharh al-Jami' li Qadi Khan, from Abu Yusuf that she is not divorced, and our mashayikh adopted this. And in al-Mabsut: Abu Yusuf's view is more correct in my opinion. Explanation: A man had several wives; he said 'Every wife of mine is divorced,' so all his wives become divorced, and his intention to exclude a particular wife is not accepted. And in al-Kanz: A man's wife asked him, 'Did you marry someone besides me?' The husband said, 'Every wife of mine is divorced.' Now whether the one who made him swear, since she is his wife, divorce occurs upon her or not – this is discussed.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on legal maxims and their exceptions, focusing on the role of intention (niyya) in oaths and divorce. It begins with the maxim 'All children of Adam are free' (ابن آدم كلهم أحرار), which establishes that default freedom is presumed. The first application: if someone says 'every slave in this house is free,' the manager's own slave becomes free by consensus only if the manager intends to free him; otherwise not. Subsequent details involve differences between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The passage then discusses the preacher (واعظ) case: if a preacher says 'you are divorced' without intending divorce, does it take effect? Using analogy to an oath, the author compares to a case where someone swore not to speak to Zaid and then greeted a group including Zaid without intending Zaid – he is guilty judicially but not religiously. Similarly, the preacher's divorce occurs even without intention, because in oaths, knowledge of Zaid's presence is irrelevant. The text then lists several furū' (branches): calling one's wife 'O Taliq' if that is her name, and calling a slave 'O Free' – in both, the intended effect (divorce or emancipation) does not occur if no intention, contrary to a view of al-Mahbubi who distinguished between divorce and emancipation. The relied-upon view is no distinction. Then, if one gives a definite divorce and later claims he intended it as conditional, this claim is accepted religiously but not judicially. Finally, the case of 'every wife of mine is divorced' – a general statement cannot be excepted by a later intention; all wives are divorced. However, there is a difference of opinion in the case where a wife asks if he married another, and he responds 'every wife is divorced' – Abu Yusuf says the questioning wife is not divorced, and this is adopted by later scholars.

Key Terms
نِيَّة (niyya): Intent in the heart, which may affect legal consequences of utterances
واعظ (wā'iẓ): A preacher who says 'you are divorced' without intending divorce in a hypothetical teaching context

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a manager says 'every slave in this house is free' without intending his own slave, what is the ruling regarding his own slave?
A) The slave is freed by the general statement
B) The slave is not freed because intention is lacking
C) The slave is freed only if the manager knew his slave was in the house
D) The slave is freed but the manager must pay compensation

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'All children of Adam are free' establishes default freedom, but intention can particularize general utterances in emancipation, while in oaths general words take effect judicially regardless of specific intent.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
advanced
10 min
Intention in Divorce Utterances: The Taliq Case and General Statements
Commentary on furu' of divorce with distinctions of intention and general utterances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on divorce when a husband uses a word that is his wife's name (e.g., Taliq) without intending divorce, identify the disputed view of al-Mahbubi, and apply the rule regarding general divorce statements.

Core Idea
In divorce, uttering a word that sounds like divorce does not cause divorce without intention; but a general statement like 'every wife of mine is divorced' cannot be restricted by a later exception.

This lesson explores several contemporary-sounding fatwa issues: what happens if a husband calls his wife by a nickname that is also a word for divorce? The classical discussion revolves around the name 'Taliq'. We also examine the case where a husband claims a definite divorce was actually conditional, and the general statement 'every wife of mine is divorced'. These illustrate the boundaries of intention (niyya) in divorce law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core branch: calling wife 'O Taliq'
If a husband says to his wife 'O Taliq' and that is her name, and he does not intend divorce, the famous view is that no divorce occurs. This is analogous to saying 'O Free' to a slave named Free.
The key is that the word is being used as a name, not as a declaration.
2
Analyze al-Mahbubi's distinction
Al-Mahbubi distinguished between divorce and emancipation: he argued that divorce occurs even without intention in the 'Taliq' case because women are not named Taliq (it is only a word for divorce), whereas slaves are named 'Free' so the word is a name.
This distinction is rejected by the majority as contrary to the famous view.
3
Examine the claim of conditional intention
If a husband gives a definite (munajjaz) divorce and later claims he intended it as conditional, his claim is accepted religiously (dayānah) but not judicially (qaḍā'an). The divorce is effective in court.
This shows the default: immediate judicial effect of plain words.
4
Analyze general statements: 'Every wife of mine is divorced'
A husband says 'Every wife of mine is divorced' and later claims he intended to exclude a particular wife. This is not accepted; all wives are divorced. Even a later intention to exclude is ineffective.
Exception: Abu Yusuf's view on the questioning wife is considered more sound by later scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولد آدم كلهم احرار : اس میں بالاتفاق منتظم کا نظام آزاد نہ ہوگا الا یہ کہ منظم اپنے نام کے آزاد کرنے کی نیت کرلے۔
كل عبد في هذه الدار ان میں بالا تفاق منتظم کا غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اور باقی جزئیات تیسرے درجہ کی ہیں جن میں من وجہ تخصیص اور من وجہ قسیم ہے ان تمام میں امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان اختلاف ہے۔ فمقتضاه ان الواعظ : علامہ ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ یمین کے ایک مناہ کونظیر بنانا اولی ہوگا کہ اگر کسی نے زید سے بات نہ کرنے کی قسم کھائی تھی پھر اس نے کبھی کسی جماعت کو سلام کیا جس میں زید بھی تھا تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا لیکن اگر سلام کرتے وقت اس نے زید کی نیت نہیں کی تھی تو دیانت اس کی بات معتبر ہوگی ، قضاء نہیں لہذا اس مسئلہ کے اعتبار سے واعظ کی نیت نہ ہونے پر بھی طلاق پڑ جائے گی کیونکہ یمین کے مسئلہ میں زید کے مجمع میں ہونے کے علم ہونے یا نہ ہونے میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے ۔
فَعِنْدَ عَدَمِ نِّيَّةِ الْوَاعِظِ يَقَعُ الطَّلَاقِ عَلَيْهَا، فَإِنْ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْيَمِيْنِ لَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ كَوْ نِهِ يَعْلَمُ ان زيداً فِيهِمْ أَوْلَا. ترجمه تو واعظ کی نیت نہ ہونے کی صورت میں اس پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ مسئلہ یمین میں اس کا کوئی فرق نہیں ہے کہ وہ جانتا ہو کہ زید اسی جماعت میں ہے یا نہ جانتا ہو۔
تشریح مطلب اس عبارت کا گذر چکا ہے۔
ويَتَفَرُّعُ على هذا فُرُوْعَ، لَوْ قَالَ لَهَا: يَا طَالِقُ وَهُوَ اسْمُهَا، وَلَمْ يَقْصُدِ الطَّلَاقِ، قَالُوا: لَا يَقَعُ كَيَاحُرِّ، وَهُوَ أَسْمُهُ، كَمَا فِي الْخَانِيَةِ . وَفَرْقُ الْمَحْبُوبِى فِي التَّلْقِيْحِ بَيْنَ الطَّلَاقِ فَلَا يَقَعُ، وَبَيْنَ الْعِتْقَ فَيَقَعُ خِلَافِ الْمَشْهُورِ ، وَلَوْنَجْزَ الطَّلَاقَ، وَقَالَ: أَرَدْتُ بِهِ التَّعْلِيْقَ عَلَى كَذَا، لَمْ يُقْبَلْ قَضَاء وَيُدَيَّنُ.
ترجمہ: اور اس پر چند جزئیات متفرع ہیں اگر شوہر نے اس سے کہا یا طالق حالانکہ وہ اس کا نام تھا اور اس نے طلاق کا ارادہ نہیں کیا ہے تو فقہاء فرماتے ہیں طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی جیسے یا حر حالانکہ وہ اس کا نام ہے جیسا کہ خانیہ میں ہے محبوبی نے تلقیح میں طلاق اور عشق کے درمیان فرق بیان کیا ہے کہ طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی اور عتق واقع ہو جائے گا تو یہ مشہور کے خلاف ہے اور اگر اس نے بدون تعلیق کے طلاق دی اور کہا کہ میں نے فلاں چیز پر اسے معلق کرنے کا ارادہ کیا تھا تو قضاء اس کا قول قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور دیانہ تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ تشریح: لا يكفى التلفظ باللسان دون القلب پر چند تفریعات بیان کی جارہی ہیں کسی آدمی کی بیوی کا نام طالق تھا اس نے طالق کہہ کر پکارا اور طلاق کا ارادہ اس نے نہیں کیا تھا تو اس کی بیوی پر طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی اسی طرح اگر کسی کے غلام کا نام حر تھا اور اس نے یا حر سے پکارا تو وہ آزاد نہیں ہوگا۔ علامہ ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ اس سلسلہ میں محبوبی نے طلاق و عناق کے درمیان فرق کرنے کے بعد جو یہ بات کہی ہے کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور غلام آزاد نہیں ہوگا ، وہ فقہاء کے قول مشہور کے خلاف ہے۔ وكذا في الطلاق و تحته فى الشامية قال فى البحر و فى اكثر الكتب لم يفرق بينهما لان العلم لم يشترط فيه ان يكون معهوداً والكلام فيما اذا اشهد وقت التسمية فيهما فالظاهر عدم الفرق (شامی زکریاج ۵ : ۳۸۵)
علامہ محبوبی نے دونوں مسئلوں میں جو فرق کیا ہے کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور محقق واقع نہ ہوگی کیونکہ تر نام رکھا جاتا ہے اور مطلقہ یا طالق نام نہیں رکھا جاتا ہے۔ تو محبوبی کا یہ فرق کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ علم میں معبود ہونا شرم نہیں اور انہوں نے فرق کی بنیاد اسی کو قرار دیا ہے۔ ولـو نـجـز الطلاق و قال اردت به : اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق منجز ( بدون تعلیق ) دی پھر وہ ان الفاظ کو تعلیق پر محمول کرنا چاہتا ہے تو دیا یہ اس کی بات قبول کی جائے گی مگر قضاء قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اور طلاق پڑ جائے گی۔ ولو قال ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق يقع الحال الا اذا قال عينت به الطلاق فحينئذ يدين فيما بينه و بين الله تعالى ولايدين فى القضاء ( تارتار خامیة ج ۳ ص ۵۰۲)
وَلَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ إمْرَاقِ لِى طَالِقٌ، وَقَالَ : أَرَدْتُ غَيْرَ فُلَانَةٍ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ كَذَالِكَ، وَفِي الكنْ لَوْ قَالَتْ: تَزَوَّجُتَ عَلَى فَقَالَ: كُلُّ إِمْرَأَةٍ لِى طَالِقٌ طُلْقَتِ الْمُحَلِّفَةُ ، وَفِي شَرْحِ الْجَامِعِ لِقَاضِي حَانَ، وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوْسُفَ أَنَّهَا لَا تُطَلَّقُ، وَبِهِ أَخَذَ مَشَائِحُنَا، وَفِي الْمَبْسُوط وَقَوْلُ أبي يُوْسُفَ أَصَحُ عِنْدِي.
ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے کہا کہ میری ہر بیوی کو طلاق اور کہا کہ میں نے فلاں بیوی کے علاوہ کا ارادہ کیا تھاتو اس طرح کا قول قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور کنز الدقائق میں ہے کہ اگر بیوی نے (شوہر سے) کہا کیا تو نے میرے علاوہ کسی سے شادی کی ہے تو اس پر اس نے کہا کہ میری ہر بیوی کو طلاق تو حلف دلانے والی پر بھی طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور قاضی خاں کی شرح الجامع میں ہے کہ امام یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ اسے طلاق نہیں ہوگی اور ہمارے مشائخ نے اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے اور مبسوط میں ہے کہ ابو یوسف کا قول میرے نزدیک اصح ہے۔
تشریح کسی آدمی کی کئی بیویاں تھیں اس نے کل امراہ لی طالق کہا تو اس کی ہر بیوی مطلقہ ہو جائے گی اور اس کی استثناء کی نیت کسی بیوی کے بارے میں معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ و فی الکنز : کسی کی بیوی نے اپنے شوہر سے دریافت کیا کہ تو نے میرے علاوہ کسی سے شادی کی ہے؟ شوہر نے کہا میری ہر بیوی کو طلاق تو اب قسم کھلانے والی بھی چونکہ اس کی بیوی ہے اس پر طلاق ہوگی یا نہیں اس سلسلہ میں
All children of Adam are free: in this, by consensus, the manager's system will not be free unless the manager intends to free his name. Every slave in this house: by consensus, the manager's slave will be freed, and the remaining details are of the third level, which are partially specific and partially general; in all these, there is a difference between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. So its implication is the preacher: Allama Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says that making an analogy of an oath is better: if someone swore not to speak to Zaid, then he greeted a group including Zaid, he would be guilty of oath-breaking, but if at the time of greeting he did not intend Zaid, his statement would be valid religiously, not judicially. Therefore, by this issue, even without the preacher's intention, divorce will occur because in the oath issue, there is no difference between knowing that Zaid is in the group or not. So when the preacher has no intention, divorce occurs upon her, for in the case of an oath, there is no difference between his knowing that Zaid is among them or not. Explanation of this has passed. And there branch from this several sub-issues: If he said to her, 'O Taliq' – and that is her name – and he did not intend divorce, they said: It does not occur, like 'O Free' – and that is his name – as in al-Khaniyya. And al-Mahbubi in al-Talqih made a distinction between divorce – it does not occur – and emancipation – it occurs – contrary to the famous view. And if he gave a definite divorce and said, 'I intended by it a conditional upon such-and-such,' it is not accepted judicially but is accepted religiously. Explanation: Several branches are being stated on 'utterance with the tongue without the heart is insufficient.' A man's wife was named Taliq; he called her 'Taliq' without intending divorce; divorce would not occur. Similarly, if someone's slave was named Free and he called him 'O Free', he would not be freed. Allama Ibn Nujaym says that al-Mahbubi's distinction that divorce occurs but emancipation does not is contrary to the famous view. And likewise in divorce, under it in al-Shamiyya, it is said in al-Bahr and in most books that there is no distinction between them because knowledge does not require that it be customary; the discussion is about when he witnesses at the time of naming; the apparent is no distinction. Al-Mahbubi's distinction that divorce occurs but emancipation does not because a slave is given that name but a divorced woman or Taliq is not named – his distinction is incorrect because knowledge of being customary is not required, and he based the distinction on that. And if he gave a definite divorce and said, 'I intended by it to be conditional,' then religiously his statement is accepted but not judicially, and divorce will occur. And if he said, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' it occurs immediately unless he said, 'I intended by it the divorce,' then he is believed between himself and Allah, not in court. And if he said, 'Every wife of mine is divorced' and said, 'I intended other than so-and-so,' it is not accepted likewise. And in al-Kanz: if she said, 'Did you marry another?' and he said, 'Every wife of mine is divorced,' the one who made him swear will also be divorced. And in Sharh al-Jami' li Qadi Khan, from Abu Yusuf that she is not divorced, and our mashayikh adopted this. And in al-Mabsut: Abu Yusuf's view is more correct in my opinion. Explanation: A man had several wives; he said 'Every wife of mine is divorced,' so all his wives become divorced, and his intention to exclude a particular wife is not accepted. And in al-Kanz: A man's wife asked him, 'Did you marry someone besides me?' The husband said, 'Every wife of mine is divorced.' Now whether the one who made him swear, since she is his wife, divorce occurs upon her or not – this is discussed.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on legal maxims and their exceptions, focusing on the role of intention (niyya) in oaths and divorce. It begins with the maxim 'All children of Adam are free' (ابن آدم كلهم أحرار), which establishes that default freedom is presumed. The first application: if someone says 'every slave in this house is free,' the manager's own slave becomes free by consensus only if the manager intends to free him; otherwise not. Subsequent details involve differences between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The passage then discusses the preacher (واعظ) case: if a preacher says 'you are divorced' without intending divorce, does it take effect? Using analogy to an oath, the author compares to a case where someone swore not to speak to Zaid and then greeted a group including Zaid without intending Zaid – he is guilty judicially but not religiously. Similarly, the preacher's divorce occurs even without intention, because in oaths, knowledge of Zaid's presence is irrelevant. The text then lists several furū' (branches): calling one's wife 'O Taliq' if that is her name, and calling a slave 'O Free' – in both, the intended effect (divorce or emancipation) does not occur if no intention, contrary to a view of al-Mahbubi who distinguished between divorce and emancipation. The relied-upon view is no distinction. Then, if one gives a definite divorce and later claims he intended it as conditional, this claim is accepted religiously but not judicially. Finally, the case of 'every wife of mine is divorced' – a general statement cannot be excepted by a later intention; all wives are divorced. However, there is a difference of opinion in the case where a wife asks if he married another, and he responds 'every wife is divorced' – Abu Yusuf says the questioning wife is not divorced, and this is adopted by later scholars.

Key Terms
صارح (ṣarīḥ): Clear, unambiguous words for divorce (e.g., 'anti ṭāliq') which require no intention for judicial effect
مُنجَّز (munajjaz): Definite, unconditional divorce utterance

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband says to his wife 'O Taliq' (which is her name) without intending divorce, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling?
A) Divorce occurs because the word was uttered
B) Divorce does not occur because intention is lacking
C) Divorce occurs if the wife was aware of the meaning
D) Divorce occurs only if the husband knew her name was Taliq

Key Takeaway
In divorce, using a woman's name that sounds like divorce does not cause divorce without intention; general statements cannot be restricted by later claims; claims of conditional intention after a definite divorce are accepted only religiously, not judicially.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Intention to Restrict General Statements in Oaths
Applying the qa'idah of takhsis al-amm vs takhsis al-wasf to freedom oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qa'idah distinguishing takhsis al-amm from takhsis al-wasf to evaluate the validity of a speaker's intention when making general statements in oaths and manumissions.

Core Idea
Intention can restrict a general term but not an accidental attribute — takhsis al-amm works, takhsis al-wasf fails.

A common scenario in ifta' is a person making a sweeping statement like 'Every slave of mine is free' and later claiming they only meant a specific subset. How do we evaluate such claims? This lesson presents a critical Hanafi qa'idah: the distinction between specifying the general term itself (which may be accepted in din) and specifying an accidental attribute (which is never accepted). We will work through the furuat from divorce and manumission to see this principle in action.

Guided Path
1
State the core qa'idah
Extract the key rule from the passage: 'takhsis al-amm' is specification of the general, 'takhsis al-wasf' is specification of an attribute. The former can be valid in din; the latter never.
The qa'idah is a dabt governing oaths and general statements in legal contexts.
2
Analyse the divorce furu'
Consider the case: a man is asked 'Do you have a wife other than this one?' and he replies 'Every wife of mine is divorced.' Here, the present wife is not divorced because the question excludes her; his statement is implicitly restricted by context.
This is takhsis by context, not by intention alone.
3
Analyse the manumission furu' (gender)
If a man says 'Every slave of mine is free' and later claims he intended only males, he is believed in din (between him and Allah) but not in qada'. This is takhsis al-amm because 'mamluk' is general and can be narrowed.
The word 'mamluk' is masculine but includes females in usage; narrowing to males is plausible.
4
Analyse the manumission furu' (color and similar attributes)
If he claims he intended only black slaves or only white, his intention is not accepted at all. This is takhsis al-wasf because color is an accidental attribute not covered by the word 'mamluk'.
There is no generality over attributes, so intention cannot restrict them.
5
Determine the fatwa outcome
For takhsis al-amm: the person is believed in din but not in court. For takhsis al-wasf: the intention is completely ignored; all slaves are freed.
The mufta bihi is based on the dīn/qaḍā distinction and the principle that attributes have no generality.
