ات ہیں۔ (۱) نالہ پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ (۲) دوسری روایت جو امام ابو یوسف کی ہے کہ طلاق واقع نہ ہو گی کرا مشائخ نے اس کو لیا ہے اور علامہ شمس الائمہ سر سی نے مبسوط میں اس کو اسح کہا ہے۔
طلاق غيرها فيتقيد به واختار شمس الائمه السرخسى وكثير من المشائخ رواية ابي يوسف وعن أبي يوسف انها لاتطلق لانه اخرجه جوابا فينطبق عليه ولان غرضه ارضاءها وهو ا رفى جامع قاضی خان و به اخذ مشائخنا (البحر الرائق ج ۲ ش: ۳۵۵)
وَلَوْقِيلَ لَهُ: الْكَ إمْرَأَةٌ غَيْرَ هَذِهِ الْمَرْأَةِ، فَقَالَ: كُلَّ امْرَأَةٍ لي طَالِقَ فَلَا تُطَلَّقَ هَذِهِ، وَالْفَرْقُ حُرُ عَتِقَ عَبِيدُهُ الْقِنُ، وَأُمَّهَاتُ أوْلَادِهِ، وَمُدَبَّرُوْهُ ، وَفِي شَرْحِهِ لِلزَّيْلَعِيُّ، وَلَوْ قَالَ: أَرَدْتُ يَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ مَسْأَلَةِ الْكُفْرِ مَذْكُورٌ فِي الْوَلْوَ الْجِيَّةِ . وَفِي الْكُفْرِ : كُلُّ مَمْلُوكِ لي بِهِ الرِّجَالَ دُونَ النِّسَاءِ دُيّنَ. وَكَذَا لَوْ نَوَى غَيْرَ الْمُدَبَّرِ، وَلَوْ قَالَتْ : نَوَيْتِ السَّوْدَ هُوَنَ ض أَوْعَكْسَهُ لَا يُدَيَّنُ؛ لأنَّ الأَوَّلَ تَخْصِيْصُ الْعَام وَالثَّانِي تَخْصِيْصُ الْوَصْفِ وَلَا عُمُوْمَ لِغَيْرِ اللَّفْظِ فَلَا تَعْمَلُ فِيْهِ نِيَّةُ التَّخْصِيْصِ وَلَوْ نَوَى النِّسَاءَ دُوْنَ الرِّجَالَ لَمْ يُدَيَّنُ. ترجمہ: اور اگر اس سے کہا گیا اس بیوی کے علاوہ تیری اور کوئی بیوی ہے تو اس نے کہا میری ہر بیوی کوطلاق رای طلاق نہیں ہوگی اس کے اور مسئلہ کنز کے درمیان فرق ولوالجیہ میں مذکور ہے اور کنز میں ہے کہ میرا ہر ملوک آزاد ہے اس کے خالص غلام اور ام ولد اور مد بر سب آزاد ہو جائیں گے اور زیلعی کی شرح کنز میں ہے کہ اگر اس نے یہ کہا ہ میں نے مردو کا ارادہ کیا تھا عورتوں کا ارادہ نہں کیا تھا تودیانہ اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی اور یہی حکم اس صورت ٹا ہے جب اس نے مدبر کے علاوہ کی نیت کی ہو اور اگر اس نے کہا کہ میں نے کالوں کی نیت کی تھی گوروں کی نیت نہیں ک تھی اس کے برعکس تو اس کی تصدیق دیا نہ بھی نہیں کی جائے گی اس لئے کہ اول صورت میں عام کی تخصیص ہے اور انی میں وصف کی تخصیص ہے اور لفظ کے علاوہ میں عموم نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس میں تخصیص کی نیت عمل نہیں کرے گی اور اران نے عوتوں کی نیت کی ہو مردوں کی نسبت نہ کی ہو تو دیانہ بھی اس کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ تشریح کسی آدمی نے کسی سے پوچھا کہ اس کے علاوہ تمہاری کوئی بیوی ہے؟ اس نے کہا میری ہر بیوی کو خالق ہے تو اس کے یہ جملہ کہنے پر اس کی بیوی کو طلاق نہیں پڑے گی کنز کا جو مسئلہ اوپر بحر کے حوالہ سے نقل کیا گیا ہے اس میں اور اس مسئلہ میں ولوالجیہ میں جو فرق ذکر کیا ہے وہ ہمیں ولوالجیہ میں تلاش کے بعد بھی نہیں ملا۔ علامہ موٹی کے حوالہ سے نقل کیا جاتا ہے کہ پہلے میں تزوجت علی اِمرأۃ کے اندر ا ا مراۃ کا لفظ اس عورت اور یر کی عورت دونوں کو شامل ہے جبکہ یہاں الک امرأۃ غیر ہذہ کے اندر اس عورت کے دخول کا احتمال نہیں ہے کیونکہ وئیر کے ذریعہ تلی ہوئی ہے۔
فقولها انک قد تزوجت على إمرأة اسم المرأة يتناولها كما يتناول غيرها فتدخل و اما هنا قوله غير هذه المرأة لا يحتمل هذه المرأة فلا يدخل تحت قول الزوج. (حاشیر میموی ص: ۸۷) کل مملوک لی حر حر : اگر کسی کے پاس بہت سارے غلام، مدبر ، مکاتب اور ام ولد ہیں اس نے کہا کل مملوک لی حر تو اب ہر طرح کے مملوک داخل ہوں گے خواہ وہ من کامل ہوں ، مدبر ہوں یا امہات اولاد ہوں۔ کل مملوک لی حر عتق عبیده و مدبره و ويدين فى نية الذكور لا الاناث و امهات اولاده. تنوير مع الدرج ۵، ص : ۶۲۰)
کل مملوک لی حد میں صرف مرد غیر مدبرکی نیست : کسی نے کل مملوک لی حر کہا اب بعد میں وہ یہ کہے کہ میں نے صرف مرد غلام مراد لئے تھے اسی طرح میری نیست غیر مدیر کی تھی تو دیا ہے اس کی بات مان لی جائے گی قضاء سب آزاد ہوں گے۔ كل مملوک لی حر عتق عبيده القن و امهات اولاده و مدبره و مکاتبه. (برج ۴ ص: ۳۳۵)
کل مملوک لی حر سے صرف حبشی یا گورے غلاموں کی نیت معتبر نہیں : سی کے پاس حبشی اور گورے دونوں طرح کے غلام تھے اس نے کل مملوک لی حر کیا اور بعد میں کیا کہ میری نیت صرف حبشی غلاموں کی تھی یا گورے غلاموں کی تھی تو دیا یہ بھی اس کی یہ نیت نہیں مانی جائے گی اور اوپر کے مسئلہ میں اور اس میں فرق یہ ہے کہ اس میں عام کی تخصیص تھی اور دوسرے میں وصف کی تخصیص ہے اور الفاظ کے علاوہ میں عموم کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا لہذا تخصیص کی نیت کا وصف میں کچھ فائد نہ ہوگا۔
کل مملوک لی حر سے صرف باندیاں مراد لینا معتبر نہیں:
کوئی شخص کل مملوک لی حر کہے اور پھر صرف باندیاں مراد لے مردوں کو مراد نہ لے تو قضاء اس کی تصدیق ہی نہیں کی جائے گی بلکہ دیانے بھی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی لیکن اوپر کے مسئلہ میں جب صرف مرد کی نیت کی تھی تو دیانت اس کی نیت کا اعتبار تھا دونوں میں علامہ حموی نے یہ فرق ذکر کیا ہے کہ مملوک کا لفظ حقیقیہ مذکر کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے مؤنث کے لئے نہیں لیکن اختلاط کے موقع پر بطریق تبعیہ ان کے لئے بھی تذکیر کا لفظ عادہ استعمال کر دیا جاتا ہے تنہا عورتوں کے لئے یہ لفظ استعمال نہیں ہوتا لہذا اس کی نیت لغو قرار پائے گی اور دریائے بھی اس کی تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ ولونوى النساء وحدهن لا يصدق اصلا. (شای ج ۵ ص: ۱۳۰)
وَفِي الْكَبْرِ إِنْ لَبِسْتُ اوْا كَلْتُ اوْ شَرِبْتُ، وَنَوَى مُعَيَّنَا لَمْ يُصَدَّقَ اصْلَا، وَلَوْ زَادَ ثَوَاباً، أَوْ طَعَاماً، أَوْ شَرْا بادينَ. وَفِي الْمُحِيْطِ لَوْنَوَى جَمِيعَ الأَطْعِمَةِ، فِي
There are two issues: (1) Divorce will occur on crying. (2) The second narration from Imam Abu Yusuf that divorce will not occur, and the mashayikh took it, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi in al-Mabsut considered it correct. Divulging other than her, so it is restricted by it, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi and many of the mashayikh chose the narration of Abu Yusuf. And from Abu Yusuf that she does not divorce because he uttered it as a response, so it applies to that, and because his purpose is to please her, and it is in Jami' al-Qadi Khan, and our mashayikh adopted it. (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, vol. 2, p. 355) And if it is said to him: 'Do you have a wife other than this woman?' and he said: 'Every wife of mine is divorced,' then this one is not divorced. The difference between it and the issue of freedom: his qinn slaves, his ummahat al-awlad, and his mudabbar slaves are freed. And in its commentary by al-Zayla'i: and if he said: 'I intended between her and the issue of disbelief mentioned in al-Walwajiyyah.' And in al-Kanz: 'Every slave of mine is free' — he intends the men without the women, so he is believed (dinan). Similarly if he intended other than the mudabbar. And if he said: 'I intended black [slaves]' or the opposite, he is not believed; because the first is takhsis of the general, and the second is takhsis of the attribute, and there is no generality for other than the wording, so the intention of takhsis does not apply to it. And if he intends women without men, he is not believed. Translation: ... [Urdu paraphrases the ruling and explains the distinction between takhsis al-amm and takhsis al-wasf, and the difference between diyanah and qada'.] Explanation: The passage discusses that if a person says 'kullu mamlookin li hurr', all types of slaves are freed, but if he intends only male slaves, he is believed in din (between him and Allah) but in qada (court) all are freed. If he intends only female slaves, he is not believed at all. If he intends black or white, his intention is not accepted because it is takhsis of attribute, not of the general. The text compares with the divorce case where the question 'Do you have a wife other than this one?' and he replies 'Every wife of mine is divorced' — the present wife is not included because the question excludes her, so his statement is interpreted accordingly.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of a central qa'idah in Hanafi fiqh: when a person utters a general statement (like 'every slave of mine is free' or 'every wife of mine is divorced'), the effectiveness of their intention to restrict that general statement depends on the nature of the restriction. The author first presents the case of divorce: a man is asked 'Do you have a wife other than this one?' and he replies 'Every wife of mine is divorced.' Here, the wife present is not divorced because the question itself eliminates her from consideration — his answer is understood in the context of the question. This is contrasted with the case of manumission: if a man says 'Every slave of mine is free,' all his slaves (qinn, mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab) are freed. If he later claims he intended only male slaves or only non-mudabbar, he is believed in din (between him and Allah) because the qualification is takhsis of the general (takhsis al-amm) — the word 'mamluk' is general, so restricting it by intention is plausible. However, if he claims he intended only black slaves or only white slaves, his intention is not accepted even in din, because that is takhsis of an attribute (takhsis al-wasf) — the wording 'mamluk' does not imply any color, so there is no generality regarding attributes to be restricted. The same applies if he intends only female slaves: the word 'mamluk' is masculine in its true usage; females are included only secondarily. Therefore, an intention to restrict to females alone is invalid. The passage also cites a similar principle from al-Kanz regarding oaths of eating, drinking, etc., where intention to specify a particular type is not accepted unless the wording is general enough. In short, the qa'idah is: intention can restrict a general expression only when the restriction is on the general itself (e.g., selecting a subset of individuals covered by the term), not when it restricts an accidental description that the term does not explicitly cover.

Key Terms
تخصيص العام (takhsīṣ al-‘āmm): Specification of the general: restricting a general term to a subset of its individuals.
تخصيص الوصف (takhsīṣ al-waṣf): Specification of an attribute: restricting a term by an accidental quality not part of its meaning.
دين (dīnan): In religious/conscience matters: a ruling that is between the person and Allah, not enforced by a judge.
قضاء (qaḍā’an): In court/judicial matters: a ruling enforceable by a judge based on apparent evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says 'Every slave of mine is free' and later claims he only meant his male slaves (excluding females). What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He is believed in both din and qada', so only male slaves are freed.
B) He is believed in din but not in qada'; in court all slaves are freed.
C) He is not believed at all; all slaves are freed.
D) His intention is accepted only if he has female slaves.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, intention can narrow a general term (takhsis al-amm) but not an accidental attribute (takhsis al-wasf); this distinction governs the acceptance of a speaker's claimed intention in oaths and manumissions.

Oaths Without a Generic Term: Intention Not Credited at All
Ruling on general oath without specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when someone swears 'if I eat' without specifying and later claims a specific intention, and identify the governing qawida.

Core Idea
Without a generic term, the oath applies to all instances; intention is irrelevant.

When someone swears a conditional oath like 'if I eat' and later claims they meant a particular food, the Hanafi school does not accept that claim at all. This lesson establishes the default rule: general wording binds the oath absolutely. The principle 'al-yamin tunazzalu 'ala niyyat al-halif' applies, but here the intention contradicts the apparent general meaning, so it is rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath wording
Look at the wording: 'if I eat' (إن أكلت) – no generic term like 'food' was added. The oath is general and covers any act of eating.
2
State the claim of intention
The swearer later claims he meant a specific food (e.g., only bread). This is a restriction of the general meaning.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
According to al-Kanz and the majority, such an intention is not credited at all (لم يصدق أصلا). The general wording remains fully operative.
The qawida 'al-yamin tunazzalu 'ala niyyat al-halif' is overridden because the intention contradicts the literal scope.
4
Determine the consequence
Any act of eating, regardless of the specific item, breaks the oath. The swearer is liable for the penalty (e.g., freeing slaves).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي الْكَبْرِ إِنْ لَبِسْتُ اوْا كَلْتُ اوْ شَرِبْتُ، وَنَوَى مُعَيَّنَا لَمْ يُصَدَّقَ اصْلَا، وَلَوْ زَادَ ثَوَاباً، أَوْ طَعَاماً، أَوْ شَرْا بادينَ. وَفِي الْمُحِيْطِ لَوْنَوَى جَمِيعَ الأَطْعِمَةِ، فِي لا يَا كُلُ طَعَاماً وَجَمِيعَ مِيَاهِ الْعَالَمِ فِي لَا يَشْرَبُ شَرَاباً يُصَدَّقُ قَضَاءُ، إِنْتَهَى وَ فِى الْكَشْفِ الْكَبِيْرِ يُصَدَّقُ دِيَا نَةٌ لَا قَضَاءً وَقِيْلَ : قَضَاءً أَيْضاً. ترجمہ: اور کنز میں ہے اگر کسی نے کہا ان لبست یا ان اکلت یا ان شربت اور اس نے معین کی نیت کی تو بالکلیہ اس کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی اور اگر اس نے تو بایا طعاماً یا شرابا کا اضافہ کر دیا تو دیائیے اس کی تصدیق کی جائیگی اور محیط میں ہے کہ اگر " لا یا کل طعاماً " میں تمام ہی کھانوں کی اور لا یشرب شرابا میں ہر قسم کی پانی کی نیت کر لی تو قضاء اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی کنز کا کلام پورا ہوا اور الکشف الکبیر میں ہے کہ دیانہ تصدیق کی جائے گی قضا نہیں اور کہا گیا کہ قضاء بھی تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے کہا کہ اگر میں پہنوں یا کھاؤں یا پیوں تو میرے سارے غلام آزاد ہیں پھر بعد میں وہ کسی معین کھانے یا معین کپڑا پہنے یا معین مشروب کی نیت کرے تو اس کی یہ نیت اصلا معتبر ہی نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر کہتے وقت تو یا طعاما یا شرابا کا اضافہ بھی کر دیا تھا تو دیانے اس کی بات مان لی جائے گی۔
قال ان اکلت او شربت او لبست ونوى معينا لم يصدق اصلا فیحنث بای شیاکل او شرب (تنوير مع الدرج ۵، ص: ۵۸۱)
لا يأكل طعاماً : اگر کسی نے لا يأكل طعاماً يا لايشرب شراباً کہا اور ہر طرح کا کھانا و پینا مرا دلیا تو اس سلسلہ میں تین قول ہیں: (۱) قضاء اس کی نیت کی تصدیق کی جائے گی (۲) دوسرا قول جو الکشف الکبیر کے اندر ہے کہ دیانہ تصدیق کی جائے گی (۲) تیسرا قول یہ ہے کہ دیانیہ اور قضاء دونوں اعتبار سے رتصدیق کی جائے گی۔ علامہ شامی نے اس قول کو راجح قرار دیا ہے۔ ویلزم منه ان يصدق قضاء وديانةً اذا نوى الكل (شامى مع الدرج ۵، ص: ۵۲۸).
And in al-Kanz: If he said 'if I wear' or 'if I eat' or 'if I drink' and intended a specific thing, he is not credited at all. And if he added 'a garment' or 'food' or 'drink' then he is credited diyanatan. And in al-Muhit: If he intended all foods in 'I will not eat food' and all waters of the world in 'I will not drink any drink' then he is credited judicially. End. And in al-Kashf al-Kabir: He is credited diyanatan, not judicially; and it was also said: judicially as well. Translation: And in Kanz: If someone said 'if I wear' or 'if I eat' or 'if I drink' and intended a specific thing, then his intention is not credited at all. And if he added 'a garment' or 'food' or 'drink' then he is credited diyanatan. And in al-Muhit: If in 'I will not eat food' he intended all foods and in 'I will not drink any drink' he intended all waters, then he is credited judicially. End of Kanz's statement. And in al-Kashf al-Kabir: He is credited diyanatan, not judicially; and it was said: judicially as well. Explanation: If someone said 'if I wear or eat or drink, then all my slaves are free' and later intends a specific food, specific garment, or specific drink, then his intention is not valid at all. And if at the time of speaking he added 'a garment' or 'food' or 'drink' then he is credited diyanatan. He said: if he said 'if I eat or drink or wear' and intended a specific thing, he is not credited at all, so he breaks his oath with anything he eats or drinks (Tanwir with al-Durr vol.5 p.581). 'He will not eat food': If someone said 'I will not eat food' or 'I will not drink any drink' and intended all types of food and drink, then there are three opinions: (1) He is credited judicially. (2) The second opinion in al-Kashf al-Kabir: He is credited diyanatan, not judicially. (3) The third opinion: He is credited both diyanatan and judicially. Shami declared this opinion as preponderant. And it follows from this that he is credited judicially and diyanatan when he intends all (Shami with al-Durr vol.5 p.528).
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage discusses rulings on oaths (ayman) where a person swears a conditional oath (e.g., 'if I eat, then my slaves are free') and later claims he meant a specific item (e.g., 'only bread'). According to al-Kanz, such an intention is not accepted at all, because the wording is general. However, if he added a general term like 'food' or 'drink' (e.g., 'if I eat any food'), then his intention to specify a particular item is accepted diyanatan (in conscience) but not judicially. Al-Muhit presents a different case: if the oath is in the negative (e.g., 'I will not eat food') and he intended all foods, then he is credited judicially (he is not considered a breaker until he eats all foods). Al-Kashf al-Kabir limits this to diyanatan only, while another opinion extends it to judicially. Imam Shami preferred the opinion that he is credited both ways. The lesson illustrates how the generality of the wording and the addition of 'food' or 'drink' affect the acceptance of intention. The key principle: without an added word, the general remains general; with an added word, the intention is only plausible diyanatan.

Key Terms
معین (mu'ayyan): Specified particular item (e.g., a specific food or garment)
تصدیق (tasdiq): Acceptance of a person's claim or intention

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Kanz, if someone says 'if I eat' and later intends a specific food, his intention is:
A) Accepted both diyanatan and qada'an.
B) Accepted diyanatan only.
C) Not accepted at all.
D) The oath becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
General oath without a generic term: no intention to specify is accepted; the oath applies to all instances.

Adding a Generic Term: Diyanatan Acceptance Only
Ruling on oath with added generic term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qada'an and diyanatan acceptance of intention when a generic term (like 'food') is added in a conditional oath.

Core Idea
Adding a generic term allows the swearer's specific intention to be credited diyanatan, not judicially.

When someone says 'if I eat food' (adding the generic 'food') and later claims he meant a specific food, his intention is accepted in conscience (diyanatan) but not in court (qada'an). This lesson explains why the added term creates ambiguity that makes the intention plausible, but the law still holds the general meaning as default for litigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath with an added generic term
The wording includes a category word like 'food' (طعاماً), 'garment' (ثوباً), or 'drink' (شراباً). This is different from bare 'if I eat'.
The generic term is the key differentiator.
2
State the swearer's claimed intention
He later claims he meant a specific item within that category (e.g., only bread as 'food').
3
Apply the ruling: diyanatan acceptance
The Hanafi sources (al-Kanz and others) rule that he is credited diyanatan (فديانةً), meaning in his religious conscience the oath is restricted, but the court applies the general meaning.
Diyanatan: acceptable before Allah; qada'an: enforceable in court.
4
Understand the rationale
The added term makes the scope ambiguous; the intention can clarify it inwardly, but outwardly the general word remains the standard for legal enforcement.
This balances between literal wording and subjective intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي الْكَبْرِ إِنْ لَبِسْتُ اوْا كَلْتُ اوْ شَرِبْتُ، وَنَوَى مُعَيَّنَا لَمْ يُصَدَّقَ اصْلَا، وَلَوْ زَادَ ثَوَاباً، أَوْ طَعَاماً، أَوْ شَرْا بادينَ. وَفِي الْمُحِيْطِ لَوْنَوَى جَمِيعَ الأَطْعِمَةِ، فِي لا يَا كُلُ طَعَاماً وَجَمِيعَ مِيَاهِ الْعَالَمِ فِي لَا يَشْرَبُ شَرَاباً يُصَدَّقُ قَضَاءُ، إِنْتَهَى وَ فِى الْكَشْفِ الْكَبِيْرِ يُصَدَّقُ دِيَا نَةٌ لَا قَضَاءً وَقِيْلَ : قَضَاءً أَيْضاً. ترجمہ: اور کنز میں ہے اگر کسی نے کہا ان لبست یا ان اکلت یا ان شربت اور اس نے معین کی نیت کی تو بالکلیہ اس کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی اور اگر اس نے تو بایا طعاماً یا شرابا کا اضافہ کر دیا تو دیائیے اس کی تصدیق کی جائیگی اور محیط میں ہے کہ اگر " لا یا کل طعاماً " میں تمام ہی کھانوں کی اور لا یشرب شرابا میں ہر قسم کی پانی کی نیت کر لی تو قضاء اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی کنز کا کلام پورا ہوا اور الکشف الکبیر میں ہے کہ دیانہ تصدیق کی جائے گی قضا نہیں اور کہا گیا کہ قضاء بھی تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے کہا کہ اگر میں پہنوں یا کھاؤں یا پیوں تو میرے سارے غلام آزاد ہیں پھر بعد میں وہ کسی معین کھانے یا معین کپڑا پہنے یا معین مشروب کی نیت کرے تو اس کی یہ نیت اصلا معتبر ہی نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر کہتے وقت تو یا طعاما یا شرابا کا اضافہ بھی کر دیا تھا تو دیانے اس کی بات مان لی جائے گی۔
قال ان اکلت او شربت او لبست ونوى معينا لم يصدق اصلا فیحنث بای شیاکل او شرب (تنوير مع الدرج ۵، ص: ۵۸۱)
لا يأكل طعاماً : اگر کسی نے لا يأكل طعاماً يا لايشرب شراباً کہا اور ہر طرح کا کھانا و پینا مرا دلیا تو اس سلسلہ میں تین قول ہیں: (۱) قضاء اس کی نیت کی تصدیق کی جائے گی (۲) دوسرا قول جو الکشف الکبیر کے اندر ہے کہ دیانہ تصدیق کی جائے گی (۲) تیسرا قول یہ ہے کہ دیانیہ اور قضاء دونوں اعتبار سے رتصدیق کی جائے گی۔ علامہ شامی نے اس قول کو راجح قرار دیا ہے۔ ویلزم منه ان يصدق قضاء وديانةً اذا نوى الكل (شامى مع الدرج ۵، ص: ۵۲۸).
And in al-Kanz: If he said 'if I wear' or 'if I eat' or 'if I drink' and intended a specific thing, he is not credited at all. And if he added 'a garment' or 'food' or 'drink' then he is credited diyanatan. And in al-Muhit: If he intended all foods in 'I will not eat food' and all waters of the world in 'I will not drink any drink' then he is credited judicially. End. And in al-Kashf al-Kabir: He is credited diyanatan, not judicially; and it was also said: judicially as well. Translation: And in Kanz: If someone said 'if I wear' or 'if I eat' or 'if I drink' and intended a specific thing, then his intention is not credited at all. And if he added 'a garment' or 'food' or 'drink' then he is credited diyanatan. And in al-Muhit: If in 'I will not eat food' he intended all foods and in 'I will not drink any drink' he intended all waters, then he is credited judicially. End of Kanz's statement. And in al-Kashf al-Kabir: He is credited diyanatan, not judicially; and it was said: judicially as well. Explanation: If someone said 'if I wear or eat or drink, then all my slaves are free' and later intends a specific food, specific garment, or specific drink, then his intention is not valid at all. And if at the time of speaking he added 'a garment' or 'food' or 'drink' then he is credited diyanatan. He said: if he said 'if I eat or drink or wear' and intended a specific thing, he is not credited at all, so he breaks his oath with anything he eats or drinks (Tanwir with al-Durr vol.5 p.581). 'He will not eat food': If someone said 'I will not eat food' or 'I will not drink any drink' and intended all types of food and drink, then there are three opinions: (1) He is credited judicially. (2) The second opinion in al-Kashf al-Kabir: He is credited diyanatan, not judicially. (3) The third opinion: He is credited both diyanatan and judicially. Shami declared this opinion as preponderant. And it follows from this that he is credited judicially and diyanatan when he intends all (Shami with al-Durr vol.5 p.528).
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage discusses rulings on oaths (ayman) where a person swears a conditional oath (e.g., 'if I eat, then my slaves are free') and later claims he meant a specific item (e.g., 'only bread'). According to al-Kanz, such an intention is not accepted at all, because the wording is general. However, if he added a general term like 'food' or 'drink' (e.g., 'if I eat any food'), then his intention to specify a particular item is accepted diyanatan (in conscience) but not judicially. Al-Muhit presents a different case: if the oath is in the negative (e.g., 'I will not eat food') and he intended all foods, then he is credited judicially (he is not considered a breaker until he eats all foods). Al-Kashf al-Kabir limits this to diyanatan only, while another opinion extends it to judicially. Imam Shami preferred the opinion that he is credited both ways. The lesson illustrates how the generality of the wording and the addition of 'food' or 'drink' affect the acceptance of intention. The key principle: without an added word, the general remains general; with an added word, the intention is only plausible diyanatan.

Key Terms
معین (mu'ayyan): Specified particular item (e.g., a specific food or garment)
تصدیق (tasdiq): Acceptance of a person's claim or intention

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'I will not drink any drink' and later claims he meant 'only water', how is he credited?
A) Not credited at all.
B) Credited diyanatan only.
C) Credited qada'an only.
D) Credited both.

Key Takeaway
Adding a generic term permits religious acceptance of specific intention but not judicial enforcement.

Negative Oaths Intending All Types: Three Opinions and Shami's Tarjih
Dispute on negative oath with intention to include all

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi opinions on whether a swearer's intention to include all types in a negative oath (e.g., 'I will not eat food') is credited, and state Shami's preferred view.

Core Idea
Intending all types in a negative oath is credited judicially and religiously according to Shami's tarjih.

When someone says 'I will not eat food' and later claims he intended all foods (so that only eating every possible food breaks the oath), there are three scholarly opinions within the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks each opinion, their proofs, and why Imam Shami preferred the view that credits the swearer both judicially and religiously.

Guided Path
1
Understand the case
The oath is in the negative: 'I will not eat food' (لا آكل طعاماً). The swearer later claims he intended 'all foods' (جميع الأطعمة).
This is different from positive oaths; here the intention expands the scope rather than restricts.
2
List the three opinions
Opinion 1 (from al-Muhit): Credited judicially (قضاءً). Opinion 2 (from al-Kashf al-Kabir): Credited diyanatan only (ديانةً لا قضاءً). Opinion 3: Credited both judicially and religiously (قضاءً وديانةً).
3
Analyse the proofs
Al-Muhit argues that the word 'food' is general; intending all is consistent with its literal meaning, so it should be accepted legally. Al-Kashf al-Kabir argues that the intention is unnecessary because the word already covers all, so it is only religious. The third view combines: intention is valid and consistent, so accept both ways.
4
Identify Shami's tarjih
Shami preferred the third opinion: credited both judicially and religiously. His reasoning: if the swearer genuinely intends all, his oath is not violated until he eats all types of food.
This is the mufta bihi position according to Shami.

Divorce by 'Ant Talik li al-Sunnah' and the Role of Intention
Ruling on divorce by 'li al-sunnah' with intention effect and internal ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention when pronouncing 'Ant Talik li al-Sunnah' and explain the ikhtilaf between Kanz and Hidayah regarding intention for immediate triple divorce.

Core Idea
Intention can override the default meaning of a divorce phrase when the wording is ambiguous.

This passage examines a nuanced issue in Hanafi divorce law: the effect of the husband's intention when he uses the phrase 'You are divorced according to the Sunna'. The default understanding is that this phrase implies one divorce per tuhr (purity period), but what if he intends three divorces immediately? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute between the author of al-Hidayah and later scholars like the author of al-Kanz. Understanding this sharpens your ability to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' in divorce matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
According to al-Kanz, when a husband says 'You are divorced three according to the Sunna' to his wife, the default is that one divorce occurs at each purity period (tuhr). This is the sunna method.
The wife must be in a non-menstrual state without recent intercourse for the phrase to apply.
2
Locate the role of intention
If the husband intends that the three divorces occur immediately (all at once) or one per month, his intention is valid and the divorces occur accordingly. Intention can change the timing and number.
The phrase 'li al-sunnah' does not explicitly specify timing; intention supplies that.
3
Understand the ikhtilaf
The author of al-Hidayah (Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani) holds that if the husband intends all three immediately, the intention is invalid because it contradicts the declared 'sunnah' method which requires spacing. The later view (Kanz, its commentary) accepts the intention.
The dispute is about whether the phrase itself implies timing or only method.
4
Trace the tarjih
The position of al-Kanz and later scholars (including the commentator) prevails in fatwa. Thus, the husband's intention is accepted, and if he intended triple immediately, all three occur.
This is an example of later Hanafi authorities overruling earlier ones when the later view is more practical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي الْكَفْرِ: وَلَوْ قَالَ لِمَوْطُوْعَ تِهِ: أَنْتَ طَالِقٌ ثَلَاثَاً لِلسُّنَّةِ وَقَعَتْ عِنْدَ كُلِّ طُهْرٍ طَلَقَةٌ، وَإِنْ نَوى أنْ يُقَعَ الثَّلَاتُ السَّاعَةَ، أَوْ عِنْدَ كُلِّ شَهْرِ وَاحِدَةً صَحَتْ نِيَّتُهُ، إِنْتَهَى، وَفِي شَرْحِهِ : أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ لِلسُّنَّةِ، وَنَوَى ثَلَاثَاً جُمْلَةً أَوْ مُتَفَرِّقَةٌ عَلَى الأَطْهَارِ صَحْ، خِلَافَالِصَاحِبِ الْهَدَايَةِ فِي بية الجُمْلَةِ وَفِي الْخَانِيَةِ وَلَوْ جَمَعَ بَيْنَ مَنْكُوحَتِهِ وَرَجُلٍ، فَقَالَ : أَحَدُ كُمَا طَالِقٌ لَا يَقَعُ الطَّلَاقُ عَلَى إِمْرَأَتُهُ فِي قَوْلِ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ أَنَّهُ يَقَعُ. ترجمہ: اور کنز میں ہے کہ اگر اس نے موطوء ہ سے کہا انت طالق للسنة تو ہر طہر کی ایک طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور اگر اس نے فی الفور تین طلاق کے وقوع کی نیت کر لی یا ہر مہینہ ایک کی تو اس کی نیت صحیح ہے کنز کا کلام پورا ہوا اور اس کی شرح میں ہے اگر شوہر نے انت طالق للسنة کہا اور ایک ساتھ یا الگ الگ طہروں میں تین طلاق
And in al-Kanz: If he said to his wife (whom he has had intercourse with) 'You are divorced three according to the Sunna', then one divorce occurs at each purity period. And if he intended that the three occur immediately, or one at each month, his intention is valid. End. And in its commentary: He said 'You are divorced according to the Sunna' and intended three together or separately over purity periods, it is valid, contrary to the author of al-Hidayah in [the matter of] intention of the collective [three]. And in al-Khaniya: If he combined his wife and a man and said 'One of you two is divorced', divorce does not occur on his wife according to Abu Hanifa, and from Abu Yusuf that it does occur. Translation: And in Kanz: If he said to his wife 'You are divorced according to the Sunna', then one divorce occurs at each purity period. And if he intended immediate occurrence of three, or one each month, his intention is valid. End of Kanz's statement. And in its commentary: If the husband said 'You are divorced according to the Sunna' and intended three together or separately over purity periods, it is valid, contrary to the author of al-Hidayah in [the matter of] intention of the collective [three]. And in al-Khaniya: If he combined his wife and a man and said 'One of you two is divorced', divorce does not occur on his wife according to Abu Hanifa, and from Abu Yusuf that it does occur.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of intention when pronouncing a divorce phrase 'You are divorced according to the Sunna' (انت طالق للسنة). According to al-Kanz, the default ruling is that one divorce falls in each purity period (tuhr) if the wife is in a state in which intercourse has occurred (i.e., not during menstruation). However, if the husband intends that the three occur immediately (i.e., all at once at the current purity) or one at each month, his intention is valid and the divorces happen as he intended. The commentary adds that if he says 'You are divorced according to the Sunna' and intends three together (i.e., three divorces in one utterance) or separately over purity periods, it is valid. This contradicts the author of al-Hidayah (Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani) in the case of intending three together. The Hidayah held that pronouncing 'according to the Sunna' necessarily implies spacing; intending simultaneity contradicts the phrase. However, the later position (supported by Kanz and its commentary) upholds the validity of such intention. Also, a brief note from al-Khaniya: if a man addresses his wife and another man saying 'One of you two is divorced', then according to Abu Hanifa no divorce occurs on the wife because the word is ambiguous, but Abu Yusuf says divorce does occur. That part is tangential.

Key Terms
الطلاق للسنة (al-talaq li al-sunnah): Divorce pronounced following the prophetic sunna: one divorce during a tuhr (non-menstrual period) without intercourse
نية (niyyah): Intention regarding the timing and number of divorces
موطوءة (mawtu'ah): Wife with whom the husband has had intercourse

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says to his wife 'You are divorced according to the Sunna' and intends that three divorces occur immediately. According to the mufta bihi position, what is the ruling?
A) His intention is invalid; only one divorce occurs at each purity.
B) His intention is valid; three divorces occur immediately.
C) The divorce does not occur because it contradicts the sunna.
D) It depends on whether the wife has had intercourse during her purity.

Key Takeaway
Intention can override the default meaning of a divorce phrase, and muftis follow the later Hanafi view that accepts intention for immediate triple when saying 'li al-sunnah'.

Intention in Oaths: The Qawida 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha'
Ruling on the effect of intention in oaths about food, drink, and clothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to cases of intention in oaths and identify the distinction between qada' and diyanah.

Core Idea
Intention in oaths is accepted diyanatan but not qada'an unless the wording supports it.

This passage explores how the foundational maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' operates in the context of oaths. The key challenge is determining when a person's specific intention is legally accepted. The Hanafi school distinguishes between an absolute oath (e.g., 'if I eat') and one that explicitly mentions the genus (e.g., 'if I eat food'). The passage also documents an intra-madhhab disagreement on whether the person is believed judicially, religiously, or both.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
The governing maxim is 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions). It applies widely, including in oaths, but its operation is modified by the wording of the oath.
The qawida is kulliya (universal) but subject to restrictions (dabt).
2
Distinguish absolute vs. genus-containing oaths
An absolute oath uses words like 'in akaltu' (if I eat) without specifying a genus. A genus-containing oath adds the category, e.g., 'la aakulu ta'aman' (I will not eat food). The acceptance of intention differs.
The presence of 'ta'aman' or 'sharaban' changes the ruling.
3
Apply the maxim to each scenario
For absolute oaths: the person's specific intention (e.g., intended one food) is not accepted at all. For genus oaths: if the person intends a specific item, he is believed diyanatan. If he intends the entire genus, he is believed both diyanatan and qada'an per the preponderant view.
This reflects the difference between particularizing and universalizing intention.
4
Identify the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
When someone says 'la aakulu ta'aman' and intends all food, there are three views: believed qada'an (in Kanz), believed diyanatan only (in Kashf), or believed both (favored by Shami).
The ikhtilaf is legitimate within the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Allamah Shami considered the view of belief in both diyanatan and qada'an as preponderant. Thus, in fatwa, if the person intended the entirety, both his conscience and the court accept his claim.
This tarjih is based on the strength of the dalil and the harmony with the maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يأكل طعاماً وجميع مياه العالم في لا يشرب شراباً يصدق قضاءً، انتهى. وفي الكشف الكبير يصدق ديانةً لا قضاءً، وقيل: قضاءً أيضاً.

ترجمہ: اور کنز میں ہے اگر کسی نے کہا ان لبست او ان اکلت او ان شربت اور اس نے معین کی نیت کی تو بالکلیہ اس کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی اور اگر اس نے طعاماً یا شراباً کا اضافہ کر دیا تو دیانۃً اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ اور محیط میں ہے کہ اگر "لا يأكل طعاماً" میں تمام ہی کھانوں کی اور "لا يشرب شراباً" میں ہر قسم کی پانی کی نیت کر لی تو قضاءً اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ کنز کا کلام پورا ہوا۔ اور الکشف الکبیر میں ہے کہ دیانةً تصدیق کی جائے گی قضاءً نہیں۔ اور کہا گیا کہ قضاءً بھی تصدیق کی جائے گی۔

تشریح: اگر کسی نے کہا کہ اگر میں پہنوں یا کھاؤں یا پیوں تو میرے سارے غلام آزاد ہیں پھر بعد میں وہ کسی معین کھانے یا معین کپڑا پہنے یا معین مشروب کی نیت کرے تو اس کی یہ نیت اصلاً معتبر ہی نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر کہتے وقت یا طعاماً یا شراباً کا اضافہ بھی کر دیا تھا تو دیانۃً اس کی بات مان لی جائے گی۔

قال إن أكلت أو شربت أو لبست ونوى معيناً لم يصدق أصلاً فيحنث بأي شيء أكل أو شرب (تنوير مع الدرج 5، ص: 581)

لا يأكل طعاماً: اگر کسی نے لا يأكل طعاماً یا لا يشرب شراباً کہا اور ہر طرح کا کھانا و پینا مراد لیا تو اس سلسلہ میں تین قول ہیں: (1) قضاءً اس کی نیت کی تصدیق کی جائے گی (2) دوسرا قول جو الکشف الکبیر کے اندر ہے کہ دیانةً تصدیق کی جائے گی (3) تیسرا قول یہ ہے کہ دیانةً اور قضاءً دونوں اعتبار سے تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ علامہ شامی نے اس قول کو راجح قرار دیا ہے۔

ويلزم منه أن يصدق قضاءً وديانةً إذا نوى الكل (شامى مع الدرج 5، ص: 528)
He will not eat food' and 'all the waters of the world' in 'he will not drink any drink' – he is believed judicially, end. And in al-Kashf al-Kabir: he is believed religously, not judicially. And it was said: judicially as well. Translation: In Kanz: if someone said 'if I wear' or 'if I eat' or 'if I drink' and intended a specific thing, his intention is not accepted at all. And if he added 'food' or 'drink' to his statement, then he is believed religously. In al-Muhit: if he said 'la aakulu ta'aman' intending all foods, and 'la ashrabu sharaban' intending all drinks, he is believed judicially. End of Kanz. In al-Kashf al-Kabir: he is believed religously, not judicially. And some said: judicially as well. Explanation: If someone said: 'If I wear or eat or drink, then all my slaves are free', and later intends a specific food, garment, or drink, his intention is not accepted at all. But if he had added 'food' or 'drink' when speaking, then he is believed religously. Said: If he intended a specific thing, he is not believed at all, so he breaks his oath by anything he eats or drinks (Tanwir with al-Durr, 5:581). 'He will not eat food': If someone said 'he will not eat food' or 'he will not drink any drink' and meant all kinds of food and drink, there are three opinions: (1) he is believed judicially; (2) in Kashf Kabir, he is believed religously, not judicially; (3) he is believed both religously and judicially. Allamah Shami deemed the third opinion preponderant. And it follows that he is believed judicially and religously if he intended the entirety (Shami with al-Durr, 5:528).
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage discusses the application of the maxim 'al-umoor bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions) in the context of oaths. The author presents multiple rulings from Kanz, Kashf Kabir, and Muhit regarding whether a person who swears an oath about eating, drinking, or wearing is believed when he specifies a particular type. The key distinction is between qada'an (judicially, in court) and diyanatan (religiously, in conscience). When the oath is absolute (e.g., 'if I eat') and the person later intends a specific food, his intention is not accepted at all—he breaks the oath by eating anything. However, if he explicitly mentions the genus (e.g., 'if I eat food') and intends all of that genus, he is believed both judicially and religously according to the preponderant view. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi disagreement: some say he is believed only diyanatan, others only qada'an, but Imam Shami favored the view that combines both. This illustrates how intention interacts with the wording of oaths.

Key Terms
نوى معيناً (nawaa mu'ayyanan): Intended a specific instance of the genus (e.g., a particular food)
قضاءً (qada'an): Judicially, i.e., in a court of law
ديانةً (diyanatan): Religiously, i.e., according to one's conscience before Allah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view, if someone swears 'La aakulu ta'aman' intending all types of food, how is he believed?
A) Only diyanatan
B) Only qada'an
C) Both diyanatan and qada'an
D) Not believed at all

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' applies to oaths, but the acceptance of intention depends on the wording: absolute oaths reject specific intention, while genus-based oaths accept it at least diyanatan, and if the entirety is intended, both diyanatan and qada'an.

The Rule of Niyyah without Talfaz and Its Exceptions
Defining the ruling on verbal utterance with intention and listing exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi principle that verbal utterance is not required with intention in worship, IDENTIFY the disputed opinions on uttering intention, and APPLY the exceptions for nadhr, waqf, and shuru'.

Core Idea
Intention is of the heart; verbal utterance is not required for worship, except for vows, endowments, and commencement of prayer or hajj.

This lesson examines a foundational Hanafi qa'ida: that intention (niyyah) is purely an act of the heart and does not require verbal expression (talfaz) for any act of worship. While this is a matter of consensus among the four schools, there is an inter-madhhab difference with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that utterance is necessary. Additionally, within the Hanafi school, there are varying positions on whether uttering the intention is recommended or disliked. The passage then lists three well-known exceptions where verbal utterance is indispensable: nadhr (vow), waqf (endowment), and the commencement (shuru') of salah and ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qa'ida and its scope
State the principle that verbal utterance is not required with intention in all acts of worship. Note its universal scope within ibadat.
The principle is from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair.
2
Analyze the dalil (evidence)
Examine the claim that uttering intention is not transmitted from the Prophet or his Companions. This serves as a dalil naqli (transmitted evidence) for the principle.
Fath al-Qadir and Ibn Amir al-Hajj emphasize the lack of transmission.
3
Map the opinions on talfaz
Identify the three positions: mustahabb, sunnah, and makruh. Note the preferred view in al-Hidayah and al-Qunyah.
Al-Hidayah recommends talfaz for those with weak resolve; al-Qunyah declares it mustahabb.
4
List the exceptions
State the three cases where verbal utterance is required: nadhr, waqf, and the commencement of salah/ihram. Explain the reason for each exception.
These exceptions are from the text: nadhr requires lafz, waqf requires lafz, and shuru' requires dhikr (takbir/talbiyah).
5
Apply the qa'ida and exceptions
Given a scenario, decide whether the principle applies or an exception overrides. Practice with the furuat provided.
For example, if someone intends to give a verbal vow but does not speak, the vow is not binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأَصْلُ الثَّانِي مِنَ التَّاسِعَ : وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ لَا يُشْتَرَطُ مَعَ نِيَّةِ الْقَلْبِ التَّلَفُظُ فِي جَميعَ الْعِبَادَات وَلِذَاقَالَ فِي الْمَجْمَعِ : وَلَا مُعْتَبَرَ بِاللسَانِ، وَهَلْ يَسْتَحِبُّ التَّلَفُظُ، أَوْ يَسُنُ، أَوْ يَكْرَهُ أَقْوَالٌ إخْتَارَ فِي الْهَدَايَةِ الْأَوَّلْ لِمَنْ لَمْ تَجْتَمِعْ عَزِيْمَتَهُ. وَفِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ: لَمْ يُنقَلْ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ الله وَ أَصْحَابِهِ التَّلَفْظُ بِالنِّيَّةِ لَا فِي حَدِيثٍ صَحِيحٍ، وَلَا فِي ضَعِيْفِ وَزَادَا إِبْنُ أَمِيرِ الْحَاجِّ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يُنْقَلْ عَنِ الأَئِمَّةِ الأَرْبَعَةِ. وَفِي الْمُقِيدِ كَرِهَ بَعْضُ مَشَائِحِنَا النُّطْقَ با اللسان، وَرَآهُ الْآخَرُونَ سُنَّة. تشریح: تمام علماء کا اس پر اتفاق و اجماع ہے کہ اگر کسی کے دل میں نیت ہے اور اس نے زبان سے نیت نہیں کی تو اس کی نماز درست ہو جائے گی معلوم ہوا کہ قلب میں نیت ہوتے ہوئے زبان سے ادا کر نالازم نہیں ہے اور نا ہی میں جو بی ذ کر کیا ہے کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک زبان سے بولنا ضروری ہے اس کو صاحب بحر نے مردود کیا ہے۔ وَقَالُوا اجْمَعَ الْعُلَمَاءُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَوْ نَوَى بِقَلْبِهِ وَلَمْ يَتَكَلَّمْ فَإِنَّهُ يَجُوزُ كَمَا حَكَاهُ غَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ (برج ص: ۴۸۳) وهل يستحب : تلفظانیت کے بارے میں متعدد اقوال ہیں مدینہ المصلی میں اسے مطلقاً مستحب کہا گیا ہے مجتبی میں اس قول کی تصحیح کی گئی ہے صاحب بحر نے اس کو وہ واشیح کہا ہے جبکہ ہدایہ کافی اور تبیین میں جس شخص کے دل میں اس کے بغیر عزیمت نہ ہوتی ہو اس کے لئے مستحب قرار دیا ہے۔ ويحسن ذلك اى الذكر باللسان لاجتماع عزيمته (بدا يا اشرفی ، ص:۹۲) صححه في المجتبى و في الهداية والكافى و التبيين انه يحسن لاجتماع عزيمته (البحرن، ص: ۴۸۳) و فتح القدير لم ينقل : تلفظ نیت کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے بعض نے اسے بدعت حسنہ کہا ہے اور بعض نے مطاتنا بدعت کہا ہے اس لئے بعض حفاظ حدیث نے کہا ہے کہ تلفظ نیت کسی بھی صحیح طریق یا ضعیف طریق سے حضور صحابہ اور تابعین سے ثابت نہیں ہے صاحب فتح القدیر کا رجحان بھی یہی ہے۔ وَفِي الْمُحِيطِ أَذْكُرُ بِا اللسان سُنَّةٌ، فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَقُوْلَ اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أُرِيْدُ صَلَاةَ كَذَا، فَيَسْرُهَا لِي وَتَقَبَّلُهَا مِنِّي، وَنَقَلُوْا فِي كِتَابِي الْحَجِّ أَنَّ طَلَبَ التَّيْسِيْرَ لَمْ يُنْقَلْ إِلَّا فِي الْحَجِّ، بِخِلَافِ بَقِيَّةِ الْعِبادَاتِ، وَقَدْ حَقَّقْنَاهُ فِي شَرْحِ الْكَنْرِ" . وَفِي الْقِنْيَةِ وَ الْمُجْتَبى": الْمُخْتَارُ أَنَّهُ مُسْتَحَتْ، وَخَرَجَ عَنْ هَذَا الْأَصْلِ مَسَائِلُ. ترجمہ: اور امحیط میں ہے کہ ذکر باللسان سنت ہے تو مناسب ہے کہ کہے اے اللہ میں فلاں نماز پرھنا چاہتا ہوں اس کو میرے لئے آسان فرما اور اس کو میری طرف سے قبول فرما اور فقہاء نے کتاب الحج میں نقل کیا ہے کہ تیسیر کی طلب صرف حج ہی میں منقول ہے برخلاف بقیہ عبادات کے اور اس کی تحقیق ہم نے کنز کی شرح میں کی ہے اور قلیہ اور نقیبی میں ہے کہ مستحب ہے اور اس اصل سے چند مسائل مستقلی ہیں۔ تشریح اور محیط میں ذکر باللسان کو سنت قرار دیا گیا ہے اور اس طرح کہنا چاہئے کہ اے اللہ میں فلاں نماز پڑھنا چاہتا ہوں اس کو میرے لئے آسان فرما اور قبول فرما، جبکہ بعض فقہاء سے منقول ہے کہ طلب تیسیر صرف حج میں منقول ہے بقیہ عبادات میں نہیں ہے اور اس قاعدہ سے بہت سے مسائل مستثنیٰ ہیں کہ جن میں نطق باللسان قلب کی نیت کے ساتھ ضروری ہے جس کی تفصیل آرہی ہے۔ مِنْهَا النَّذْرُ لَا تَكْفِي فِي إيْجَابِهِ النِّيَّةُ بَلْ لَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّلَفْظِ بِهِ صَرَّ حُوْابِهِ فِي بَابِ الْإِعْتِكَافِ وَمِنْهَا : الْوَقْفُ وَلَوْ مَسْجِدًا لَا بُدَّ مِنَ اللَّفْظِ الدَّالّ عَلَيْهِ، وَأَمَّا تَوَقُفُ شُرُوْعِهَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَالْإحْرَام عَلَى الذِّكْرِ ، وَلَا تَكْفِى النِّيَّةُ، فَلِأَنَّهُ مِنَ الشَّرَائِطِ لِلشُّرُوْع.
The second principle of the ninth [chapter]: that verbal utterance is not required along with intention of the heart in all acts of worship. Therefore it is said in al-Majma': 'No consideration is given to the tongue.' And as to whether verbal uttering is recommended (mustahabb), or sunnah, or disliked (makruh) – there are different sayings. Al-Hidayah chose the first for one whose resolve is not firm. In Fath al-Qadir: 'It is not transmitted from the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions – neither in a sound hadith nor in a weak one – that they uttered the intention.' Ibn Amir al-Hajj added that it is not transmitted from the four Imams. In al-Muqid: 'Some of our mashayikh disliked pronouncing with the tongue, while others considered it sunnah.' ... Exceptions from this principle: from them is nadhr (vow): intention alone is not sufficient for making it obligatory; rather verbal utterance is necessary, as clarified in the chapter on i'tikaf. And from them is waqf (endowment), even if a mosque: the word indicating it is necessary. As for the commencement of prayer and ihram being dependent on utterance (dhikr), and intention not sufficing, that is because it is among the conditions for commencement.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage discusses a fundamental principle in Hanafi fiqh: that intention (niyyah) is an act of the heart and does not require verbal expression (talfaz) for acts of worship. The author presents the consensus (ijma) of scholars on this, noting that if a person intends in the heart without speaking, the worship is valid. However, there is a well-known difference with Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires verbal utterance for the validity of worship – the author of al-Bahr rejects this view. The passage then reviews various opinions on whether uttering the intention is mustahabb, sunnah, or makruh. Al-Hidayah recommends it for those whose resolve is not firm. Fath al-Qadir and many hadith scholars note that uttering the intention is not transmitted from the Prophet, his Companions, or even the four Imams, leading some to consider it a reprehensible innovation (bid'ah). Finally, the passage lists exceptions to this rule: nadhr (vow) and waqf (endowment) require explicit verbal expression. Also, the commencement (shuru') of prayer and ihram requires the takbir (or talbiyah), not merely intention, because these are conditions for entering the act.

Key Terms
نِيَّة (niyyah): Intent of the heart; the determination to perform an act of worship for Allah.
تَلَفُظ (talfaz): Verbal utterance; pronouncing the intention with the tongue.
شُرُوْع (shuru'): Commencement of an act of worship, such as the first takbir in salah or talbiyah in hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for a vow (nadhr) to be valid?
A) Only intention in the heart
B) Intention and verbal utterance
C) Verbal utterance alone without intention
D) Written contract

Key Takeaway
Intention is an act of the heart; verbal utterance is not required for any act of worship, except for vows, endowments, and the commencement of prayer or hajj.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
When Intention Alone Is Not Enough
Expanding the maxim of niyyah sufficiency with its exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi principle that intention suffices without verbalization, identify the key exceptions, and apply the maxim to new furu’ cases.

Core Idea
Intention suffices—except where the Law commands utterance.

We have learned that in the Hanafi school, the heart's intention (niyyah) is normally sufficient for acts of worship and transactions, without needing to speak it. But every rule has its exceptions. This lesson explores the important cases where verbalization (talfiz) is required, and even some exceptions within those exceptions. Understanding these boundaries is crucial for a mufti to give correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
Start with the maxim: al-aṣl anna al-niyyah takfī wa lā yushtaraṭ al-talfiz – intention suffices and verbalization is not required. This governs most fiqh chapters.
The principle is a wusta (intermediate) maxim; it is not absolute.
2
Note the Internal Dispute on Talfiz al-Niyyah
The passage mentions differing views on whether to verbalize intention itself (e.g., saying 'I intend to pray'). Some Hanafis deem it mustahabb; others, citing lack of Salaf proof, avoid it. The relied-upon view is mustahabb for those who need it.
This is a sub-issue, not one of the exceptions – it concerns the act of verbalizing intention, not the necessity of verbalization for validity.
3
List the Exceptions from the General Principle
The passage specifies four cases where intention alone does not suffice: (1) nadhr (vows), (2) waqf (endowments), (3) commencing salah and ihram, (4) talaq (divorce) and itq (manumission). For each, verbal expression is required.
For salah and ihram, the required verbal remembrance (takbir, talbiyah) is a condition for starting the act, not a substitute for niyyah.
4
Analyze the Sub-Exceptions
Even among these exceptions, there are further exceptions: (a) reviving dead land with intention to make it a mosque – becomes a mosque by mere intention, no verbal waqf formula needed. (b) In an ambiguous divorce scenario from Fatawa Qadi Khan, intention can determine on which wife the divorce falls.
These sub-exceptions show that the general maxim interacts with other qawaid like al-‘ādah muḥakkamah and al-umūr bi-maqāṣidihā.
5
Apply the Maxim to New Cases
Given a novel scenario, ask: is this an act where the Law typically requires utterance (like vows, endowments, divorce) or is it one where intention alone has been deemed sufficient? Check for any specific text or qiyas that might create an exception.
The mufti must weigh the general principle against the known exceptions and any relevant sub-maxims.

مِنْهَا النَّذْرُ لَا تَكْفِي فِي إيْجَابِهِ النِّيَّةُ بَلْ لَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّلَفْظِ بِهِ صَرَّ حُوْابِهِ فِي بَابِ الْإِعْتِكَافِ وَمِنْهَا : الْوَقْفُ وَلَوْ مَسْجِدًا لَا بُدَّ مِنَ اللَّفْظِ الدَّالّ عَلَيْهِ، وَأَمَّا تَوَقُفُ شُرُوْعِهَ
فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَالْإحْرَام عَلَى الذِّكْرِ ، وَلَا تَكْفِى النِّيَّةُ، فَلِأَنَّهُ مِنَ الشَّرَائِطِ لِلشُّرُوْع. ترجمه : ان میں سے نذر ہے کہ اس کے واجب کرنے میں نیت کافی نہیں بلکہ اس کا تلفظ ضروری ہے فقہاء نے باب الاعتکاف میں اس کی تصریح کی ہے اور ان ہی میں سے وقف ہے اگر چہ مسجد ہو ضروری ہے لفظ جو اس پر دلالت کرے اور بہر حال نماز اور احترام کا ذکر پر موقوف ہونا اور یہ کہ اس کے لئے نیت کافی نہیں ہے تو وہ اس کے شروع کرنے کی شرائط میں سے ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے۔

اقول و يستثنى من الوقف وقف المسجد لما في فتح القدير اذا حيا ارضا مواتاً بنية جعلها مسجداً كانت مسجداً بمجرد النية ولا يحتاج الى لفظ (حاشيه الموى ص:۸۹) و اما توقف شروعه في الصلاة والاحرام: اس جگہ اشکال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ آپ اصل ثانی سے متقی اور مستی منہ کی بات کر رہے ہیں حالانکہ ہم تو یہ دیکھتے ہیں کہ نماز اور احرام کا شروع کرنا بھی تلفظ (ذکر ) پر موقوف ہے اور نیت اس کے لئے کافی نہیں ہوتی اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نیت سے ان اذکار کا کوئی تعلق نہیں ہے ان کا تعلق نماز اور احرام شروع کرنے سے ہے لہذاوہ شروع کرنے کے شرائط میں سے ہے اشکال کی کوئی وجہ نہیں رہتی۔
وفى وروده تامل اذا الكلام فى التلفظ بالمنوى لابشي آخر.
وَأَمَّا الطَّلَاقُ وَالْعِتَاقُ : فَلَا يَقَعَانِ بِالنِّيَّةِ، بَلْ لَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّلَفُّظِ إِلَّا فِي مَسْأَلَةِ فِي فَتَاوَى قَاضِي خان ، هِيَ رَجُلٌ لَهُ إِمْرَأَتَانِ غَمْرَةٌ ، وَزَيْنَبُ، فَقَالَ : يَا زَيْنَبُ فَأَجَابَتْهُ عُمْرَةً، فَقَالَ: أنتَ طَالِقٌ ثلاثاً، وَقَعَ الطَّلَاقُ عَلَى الَّتِي أَجَابَتْ إِنْ كَانَتْ إِمْرَأَتُهُ، وَإِنْ لَّمْ تَكُنْ إِمْرَأَتُهُ بَطَلَ لأَنَّهُ أَخْرَجَ الْجَوَابَ جَوَاباً لكلام الَّتِي أَجَابَتْهُ، وَإِنْ قَالَ: نَوَيْتُ زَيْنَبَ طُلَّقَتْ زَيْنَبُ إنتهى فَقَدْ وَقَع الطلاق عَلى زَيْنَبَ بِمُجَرَّدِ النية.
In al-Mujtaba this statement is authenticated; the author of al-Bahr called it clear, while in al-Hidaya, al-Kafi, and al-Tabyin, it is declared mustahabb for one whose resolve does not strengthen without it. 'And that is good, i.e., verbal remembrance, due to the gathering of his resolve.' (Bada'i' al-Ashrafi, p. 92) It is authenticated in al-Mujtaba, and in al-Hidaya, al-Kafi, and al-Tabyin that it is good due to the gathering of his resolve. (al-Bahr, p. 483) And Fath al-Qadir did not narrate: There is disagreement about verbalizing intention; some call it a good innovation, and others call it a reprehensible innovation. Therefore some hadith scholars said that verbalizing intention is not established from the Prophet, the Companions, or the Followers through any authentic or weak chain. The inclination of the author of Fath al-Qadir is also this. 'And in al-Muhit: I remember with the tongue is sunnah, so it is appropriate that he say: O Allah, I intend to pray such and such prayer, so make it easy for me and accept it from me. And they narrated in the books of Hajj that seeking ease is only reported in Hajj, contrary to other acts of worship, and we have verified it in Sharh al-Kanz.' And in al-Qunya and al-Mujtaba: The chosen view is that it is mustahabb, and from this principle there are exceptions. Translation: In al-Muhit, verbal remembrance is considered sunnah, and one should say: O Allah, I intend to pray such and such prayer, make it easy for me and accept it. Some jurists narrated that seeking ease is reported only in Hajj, not in other acts of worship. And this principle has several excepted cases. Among them: nadhr: intention alone is not sufficient for its obligation, rather verbalization is necessary, as they explicitly stated in the chapter of i'tikaf. And among them: waqf, even if a mosque, must have the expression indicating it. As for the dependence of beginning prayer and ihram on verbal remembrance, and intention alone is not sufficient, it is because it is among the conditions for commencement. Translation: Among them is nadhr: intention alone is not sufficient for making it obligatory; verbalization is necessary. Jurists have explicitly stated this in the chapter of i'tikaf. And among them is waqf: even if it is a mosque, a verbal expression indicating it is necessary. In any case, the commencement of prayer and ihram depends on remembrance, and intention is not sufficient because it is among the conditions for commencement. Commentary: So far the author, under the principle of al-Asl al-Thani min al-Tasi', mentioned all acts of worship and non-worship where the intention in the heart sufficed and verbalization was not necessary. But since every principle has exceptions, the author now mentions these excepted matters in sequence. The first issue is that for nadhr, the intention in the heart is not sufficient; verbalization is necessary. If someone intends in his heart: 'If my such-and-such work is done, I will pray four rak'ahs,' this intention alone does not make the nadhr binding; verbalization is required. 'And it becomes binding on him by the nights with a vow of i'tikaf of days, like his saying with his tongue: For Allah upon me that I perform i'tikaf for three days, we made it a vow by his tongue because mere intention of the heart does not make anything binding upon him.' (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, vol. 2, pp. 532-533) And from them: waqf: The second issue excepted from this principle is that of waqf: for waqf, mere intention of the heart is not sufficient; verbalization of intention is necessary. However, 'Allamah al-Hamawi made an exception from this exception: if someone revives dead land with the intention of making it a mosque, it becomes a mosque by mere intention; verbalization is not needed. I say: And an exception from waqf is the waqf of a mosque, as in Fath al-Qadir: If someone revives dead land with the intention of making it a mosque, it becomes a mosque by mere intention and does not need verbal expression. (Hashiyah al-Mawi, p. 89) As for the dependence of commencement in prayer and ihram: Here an objection arises: you are speaking from al-Asl al-Thani about those matters that are excepted, whereas we see that commencing prayer and ihram also depends on verbal remembrance, and intention is not sufficient for it. The answer is that these remembrances have no connection with intention; they relate to the commencement of prayer and ihram. Therefore they are among the conditions of commencement; there is no room for objection. There is consideration in its occurrence, for the talk is about verbalizing what is intended, not something else. And as for divorce and manumission: they do not occur by intention, rather verbalization is necessary, except in one case in Fatawa Qadi Khan: a man has two wives, 'Amrah and Zaynab. He said, 'O Zaynab,' and 'Amrah answered him. He said, 'You are divorced three times.' The divorce falls upon the one who answered if she was his wife; if she was not his wife, it is invalid because he made the answer a response to the one who answered him. If he says, 'I intended Zaynab,' then Zaynab is divorced. So divorce occurs on Zaynab by mere intention.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage expands a fundamental Hanafi rule: the general principle (al-asl) is that in acts of worship and legal transactions, the intention (niyyah) of the heart is sufficient, and verbalization (talfiz) is not required. However, the author now presents several exceptions where intention alone is insufficient. The passage begins with a discussion on the verbalization of intention (talfiz al-niyyah) in prayer, noting a difference of opinion: some consider it a good innovation (bid'ah hasanah), others a reprehensible one, and some hadith scholars state it is not established from the Salaf. The relied-upon Hanafi view, as in al-Muhit and other works, is that verbalizing the intention is sunnah or mustahabb, especially for those whose resolve is strengthened by it. From this general principle of intention sufficing, several cases are excepted: 1) Nadhr (vows): A vow is not binding by mere intention; one must verbally declare it. 2) Waqf (endowments): A verbal expression is needed to establish a waqf, even for a mosque. However, an exception to this exception exists: if someone revives dead land with the intention of making it a mosque, it becomes a mosque by mere intention, as per Fath al-Qadir. 3) Commencing prayer and entering ihram: These acts require a verbal remembrance (takbir for prayer, talbiyah for ihram) as conditions for commencement; intention alone is not sufficient because these are conditions of the act, not substitutes for intention. 4) Divorce (talaq) and manumission ('itq): Generally, these do not occur by intention alone; a verbal pronouncement is necessary. The passage notes one exception from Fatawa Qadi Khan: if a man with two wives says to one by name but the other responds, and he pronounces divorce ambiguously, his subsequent claim of intention determines which wife is divorced. This shows that in certain ambiguous cases, intention can be decisive. The passage underscores the Hanafi methodological principle that general rules have exceptions, and the mufti must be aware of these furu' to apply the law correctly.

Key Terms
نِيَّة (niyyah): The intention in the heart that determines the nature of an act of worship or legal transaction.
تلفظ باللسان (talfiz bi al-lisan): Speaking verbally to express the intended act.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship that becomes obligatory upon verbal declaration.
وقف (waqf): Endowment of property for charitable purposes, requiring verbal expression.
طلاق (talaq): Divorce, which normally requires verbal pronouncement to take effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following acts cannot be performed by intention alone?
A) Making a vow (nadhr) to fast three days
B) Endowing a house as a waqf
C) Commencing the prayer with takbir
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Intention suffices as a general rule, but verbalization is mandatory for vows, endowments, beginning prayer/ihram, divorce, and manumission; a mufti must know these exceptions to avoid incorrect fatwas.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

Five Stages of Inner Thoughts and Their Accountability
Defining the five stages of inner thoughts and their legal accountability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five stages of inner thoughts (hajis, khatir, hadith al-nafs, hamm, 'azm) and apply the Hanafi qawida 'hadith al-nafs la yu'akhadhu bihi' to determine when a person becomes legally accountable for an intention.

Core Idea
Inner thoughts are not held against you until you speak or act upon them.

This lesson examines the classical Hanafi qawida that distinguishes between fleeting thoughts and firm intentions. By understanding the five psychological stages, you will learn how Islamic law precisely allocates accountability. The source text, drawn from the Hanafi legal maxims, provides both the rule and its supporting evidence from Sahih Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Define the five stages
List and define each stage: hajis (fleeting thought), khatir (continued thought), hadith al-nafs (internal hesitation), hamm (inclination to act), 'azm (firm determination). Use the Arabic terms from the source.
Memorize the order and key characteristics.
2
Apply the rule of non-accountability
State the qawida: one is not accountable for inner thoughts until speaking or acting upon them. Identify which stages fall under this rule based on the hadith.
The first three stages are explicitly not punishable by consensus.
3
Identify the exception
Note that 'azm (firm determination) when accompanied by a preparatory action becomes punishable. This is derived from the complementary qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
The hadith about two Muslims meeting with swords illustrates this exception.
4
Evaluate practical cases
Apply the maxim and its exception to scenarios: mere thought of sin (not sinful), firm intention to sin without action (not sinful), but if preparatory steps are taken (accountable).
Use the furuat from the toolbox to test understanding.

وَمِنْهَا: حَدِيْتُ النَّفْسِ لَا يُؤاخَذُ بِهِ مَالَمْ يَتَكَلَّمْ، أَوْ يَعْمَلْ بِهِ، كَمَا فِي حَدِيْثِ مُسْلِمٍ، وَحَاصِلَ مَا قَالُوْهُ: إِنَّ الَّذِي يَقَعُ فِى النَّفْسِ مِنْ قَصْدِ الْمَعْصِيَةِ أَوِ الطَّاعَةِ عَلَى خَمْسِ مَرَاتِبَ : أَلْهَا جِسُ : وَهُوَ مَايُلْقَى فِيْهَا ثُمَّ جَرَيَانُهُ فِيْهَا : وَهُوَ الْخَاطِرُ، ثُمَّ حَدِيْتُ النَّفْسِ: وَهُوَ مَا يَقَعُ فِيْهَا مِنَ التَّرَدُّدِ، هَلْ يَفْعَلُ أَوْلَا، ثُمَّ الهُمَّ : وَهُوَ تَرْجِيْحُ قَصْدِ الْفِعْلِ، ثُمَّ الْعَرْمِ، وَهُوَ قُوَّةً ذَلِكَ الْقَصْدِ وَالْجَزْمُ بِهِ. فَالْهَاجِسُ لَا يُؤاخَذُ بِهِ إِجْمَاعَاً؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ مِنْ فعله، وَإِنَّمَا هُوَ شَيْءٌ وَرَدَعَلَيْهِ لَا قَدْ رَةَ لَهُ، وَلَا صُنْع.
And among them is hadith al-nafs (inner thought); one is not held accountable for it as long as he does not speak or act upon it, as in the hadith of Muslim. The sum of what they said: that which occurs in the soul of intending an act of disobedience or obedience is of five stages: (1) al-hajis: that which is cast into it; then (2) its running within it: that is al-khatir; then (3) hadith al-nafs: that which occurs in it of hesitation, whether to do it or not; then (4) al-hamm: the preference of the intend to act; then (5) al-'azm: the strength of that intention and the determination to do it. So the hajis is not held accountable by consensus, because it is not his action; rather, it is something that comes upon him over which he has no power and no making.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage defines a legal qawida (maxim) from Islamic jurisprudence: 'Inner thoughts are not punishable unless spoken or acted upon.' It is based on a hadith in Sahih Muslim. The Hanafi jurists have analyzed the internal psychological process into five distinct stages: (1) Hajis: the initial fleeting thought; (2) Khatir: the thought continues to run; (3) Hadith al-nafs: hesitation and internal debate; (4) Hamm: the inclination to act becomes dominant; (5) 'Azm: firm determination and resolution. The first three stages (hajis, khatir, hadith al-nafs) are not punishable by consensus because they are involuntary. The hamm and 'azm may be punishable if they lead to action or verbal expression. The mufti should understand this gradation when issuing fatwas about accountability for intentions.

Key Terms
حديث النفس (hadith al-nafs): Inner thoughts that occur in the mind, ranging from fleeting ideas to firm intentions.
هاجس (hajis): The initial fleeting thought that comes to mind without any control.
خاطر (khatir): The continuation of a thought in the mind, still without firm intention.
همّ (hamm): The inclination or preponderance of intention towards an act, but still not firm.
عزم ('azm): Firm determination and resolution to perform an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At which stage does a person become fully accountable for an intended sin according to this text?
A) Hajis
B) Khatir
C) Hamm
D) 'Azm with action or speech

Key Takeaway
Inner thoughts are not punishable until spoken or acted upon, but firm determination ('azm) may incur accountability if it leads to preparatory actions.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
15 min
Five Stages of Intention and Accountability
Qa'ida with furu': five stages of intention and their legal effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qa'ida of intention stages to determine accountability for internal thoughts and resolve.

Core Idea
Only firm resolve ('azm) on sin incurs sin; mere thoughts and wavering intentions are not punished until action.

As a mufti, you will frequently encounter questions about the legal status of internal thoughts and intentions. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi maxim on the five stages of intention (qasd), distinguishing between mere passing thoughts and firm resolve. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for issuing accurate fatwas on issues ranging from sinful thoughts to conditional contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its rank
Identify the five stages of intention: hajis, khatir, hadith al-nafs, hamm, and 'azm. Note that the first three are not punishable; hamm of evil is not punished until action; 'azm of evil is sinful but not fully punishable unless the act is completed by intention alone (e.g., disbelief). Classify this as a sughra (minor) qa'ida within the larger kubra 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
The maxim is summarized in the poem: مراتب القصد خمس هاجس فخاطر فحديث النفس فهم فعزم.
2
Identify the scope and exception
The maxim governs all actions where intention is relevant, especially in ibadat and muamalat. The key exception is when the intention itself completes the act (e.g., apostasy), where both 'azm and action are sinful. Also, for good deeds, hamm is recorded as a reward.
Use the hadith: 'Allah has forgiven my ummah for what they whisper to themselves as long as they do not act or speak.' (Muslim)
3
Apply to the furu' case
Consider the case: a man says to his wife, 'If I permanently quit wine, I am divorced.' He does not drink but intends to drink. The Hanafi ruling: divorce does not occur because the condition is actual drinking, not intention. However, his 'azm to drink is sinful, but not the full sin of drinking unless he acts.
This demonstrates that 'azm does not count as doing for conditional oaths.
4
Analyse the dispute on 'azm
Some scholars (based on the hadith 'the killer and the killed are in the Fire') hold that 'azm upon sin is fully punishable. The Hanafi response distinguishes: 'azm is sinful, but the full sin of the act requires external action unless the act is completed by mere intention (like disbelief). The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in the divorce case, the Hanafi view spares the divorce; the opposing view might trigger it.
5
Identify the istithna' and its dalil
The exception to the general forgiveness of thoughts is 'azm that completes the act by itself. Evidence: the hadith about the killer, and the principle that firm resolve in such cases is treated as doing. The Hanafi response limits this exception to acts like disbelief, where intention alone suffices.
Thus, for acts requiring external action, 'azm alone does not incur the full sin.

(۲) ذہن میں کوئی تصور آیا تھوڑی دیر ر ہا پھر غائب ہو گیا تو یہ خاطر کہلاتا ہے۔
(۳) حدیث النفس آیا تھوڑی دیر کے لئے جم گیا تو ہ حدیث النفس کہلاتا ہے کیونکہ نفس تھوڑی دیر تک اس خیال میں لگا رہتا ہے۔ (۴) ہم حدیث النفس سے بڑھ کر کرنیکا ارادہ شروع ہو جائے لیکن پھر ڈھیلا پڑ جائے تو یہ ہم کہلاتا ہے۔ (۵) عزم دل میں کوئی خیال آگیا جم گیا اور اس کو کرنے کا بھی پختہ ارادہ ہو گیا تو یہ عزم کہلاتا ہے پہلی امتوں پر ان میں سے شروع کے تینوں معاف تھے آخر کے دو یعنی ہم اور عزم پر مواخذہ تھا لیکن اس سلسلہ میں شریعت محمدیہ یہ تخفیف کی گئی ہے کہ اگر نیکی کا ہم ہے تو نیکی کے رجسٹر میں اس کا اندراج ہو جاتا ہے لیکن ہم برائی کا ہے تو جب تک قولنا یا فعلا بندہ اسکو انجام نہ دیدے اس وقت تک مؤاخذہ نہ ہوگا ان پانچوں مراتب کو ایک شعر میں جمع کیا جاتا ہے۔
مراتب القصد خمس هاجس ذكروا
و خاطر فحديث النفس فاستمعا
یلیه هم فعزم کلها رفعت
سوى الاخير ففيه الاخذ قد وقعا
(روح المعانی ج ۳ جس : ۱۰۴)
عزم کے سلسلہ میں بعض محققین کی رائے یہ ہے کہ عزم علی المعصیة پر مواخذہ ہے جیسا کہ حدیث القاتل و لمقتول في النار میں عزم تل کو قتل کے برابر کا درجہ دیکر جہنم کی وعید ہے اسی پر ایک مسئلہ متفرع ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ اگر میں دائمی طور پر شراب چھوڑ دوں تو مجھے طلاق اور وہ شراب نہ پئے لیکن شراب پینے کا عزم رکھے تو بیوی پر طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی معلوم ہوا کہ یہاں پر عزم شرب شرب ہی کے درجہ میں ہے۔
البتہ عزم علی المعصیۃ میں صرف عزم کا گناہ ہو گا عمل بالجوارح کا گناہ نہ ہوگا البتہ اگر عزم ایسی چیز کا ہے جس کا تعلق ہی ایسی چیز ہے جو محض عزم سے پوری ہو جاتی ہو تو محض عزم ہی کا گناہ نہیں بلکہ پھر عمل بالجوارح کا بھی گناہ ہو گا جیسے کفر و غیرہ ، بزازیہ کا کلام پورا ہوا۔
Whether one intends sin or obedience, there are five stages. Hajis is that which comes to the mind and goes away. Then khatir is its flow in the mind. Then hadith al-nafs is that there is hesitation in the mind about doing the action or not. Then hamm is preferring the intention of the action. Then 'azm is strength and firmness in that intention. So hajis is such that there is no punishment for it by consensus, because it is not his action; it is something that came on its own, with no involvement of his power or action. Explanation: The author is making an exception from the second principle of those issues in which mere intention has no effect. Among these is hadith al-nafs, i.e., a thought of committing a sin comes to the heart and then goes away; as long as the servant does not utter it by tongue or actually commit it, there is no accountability for mere hadith al-nafs, as is known from Ruh al-Ma'ani and the hadith in Muslim. 'As for the conception of sins and blameworthy traits, since it does not cause the soul to be characterized by them, it is not punished as long as it does not exist in external actions. The Prophet (peace be upon him) indicated this when he said: 'Allah has forgiven my ummah for what they whisper to themselves, as long as they do not act upon it or speak.' That is, Allah does not punish my ummah for the conception of sin, but only for its action.' (Ruh al-Ma'ani vol. 3 p. 104). Abu Hurairah narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Allah has forgiven my ummah for what they whisper to themselves, as long as they do not speak or act upon it.' (Muslim vol. 1 p. 78). The five stages of intention: According to the level of the thought of obedience or sin that occurs in a person's soul, five stages are made, which we mention in order. (1) Hajis: something that comes to the soul and goes away, so it is called hajis. (2) Khatir: a thought comes to the mind, stays a little while, then disappears. (3) Hadith al-nafs: it comes and settles for a short while, so it is called hadith al-nafs because the soul remains engaged in that thought for a while. (4) Hamm: beyond hadith al-nafs, the intention to act starts but then weakens, so it is called hamm. (5) 'Azm: a thought comes to the heart, settles, and one firmly intends to do it, so it is called 'azm. In previous nations, the first three were forgiven, but the last two (hamm and 'azm) were punished. However, in the Shari'ah of Muhammad, this concession was granted: if it is hamm for good, it is recorded in the book of good deeds; but if it is hamm for evil, accountability does not occur until the servant acts by word or deed. These five stages are summarized in a poem: 'The stages of intention are five: hajis, khatir, then hadith al-nafs – listen – then hamm, then 'azm; all are lifted except the last, for in it punishment occurs.' (Ruh al-Ma'ani vol. 3 p. 104). Regarding 'azm: Some researchers hold that 'azm upon sin is punishable, as in the hadith 'the killer and the killed are in the Fire', where 'azm to kill is given the same rank as killing and is threatened with Hell. A derivative issue from this: if a man says to his wife, 'If I permanently leave wine, I am divorced', and he does not drink wine but intends to drink, then divorce does not occur on his wife. So it is known that here 'azm to drink is treated as actual drinking. However, in 'azm upon sin, the sin is only of the 'azm itself, not the sin of the limbs. But if the 'azm is for something that is completed by mere intention, then there is sin of both 'azm and action of the limbs, such as disbelief and the like. The words of Bazzaziyyah are complete.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents a qawida (legal maxim) regarding the five stages of intention (qasd) and their legal consequences. The author classifies the internal thoughts and intentions from mere passing thought (hajis) to firm resolve ('azm). The key ruling is that the first three stages (hajis, khatir, hadith al-nafs) are not punishable by consensus because they are not acts of the person. For hamm (wavering intention) of evil, the Hanafi school holds that it is not punished unless acted upon, while for 'azm (firm resolve) on sin, there is a dispute: some scholars hold it punishable, citing the hadith about the killer and the killed. The author then applies this to a practical case: a man who makes a conditional divorce based on quitting wine permanently but intends to drink — divorce does not occur because 'azm is not actual drinking, yet 'azm itself is sinful. The passage also notes that if the intention alone completes the act (like disbelief), then both intention and action are sinful. This analysis demonstrates the Hanafi principle of not punishing mere intentions until external action or speech, with nuances for 'azm.

Key Terms
ہاجس (hajis): A passing thought that comes to the mind and goes away without any deliberate consideration.
خاطر (khatir): A thought that lingers briefly in the mind but does not lead to intention.
حدیث النفس (hadith al-nafs): An inner speech or consideration of an action, with hesitation whether to do it or not.
ہم (hamm): An intention that starts but wavers; a beginning of resolve.
عزم ('azm): Firm resolve and strong intention to perform an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person firmly intends (azm) to commit a sin but does not act on it, what is the ruling?
A) No sin at all because it is only an intention.
B) It is sinful, but the full sin of the act is not incurred unless the act is completed by intention alone (e.g., disbelief).
C) It is punishable exactly as if the act were committed.
D) It is only sinful if the person speaks about it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes five stages of intention; only the last stage ('azm) incurs sin, and even then not the full punishment of the act unless the act is completed by intention alone.
