Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
6 min
The Five Levels of Intention and the Ruling on 'Azm
Defining five levels of intent and ruling on determination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five levels of intention and apply the rule that only 'azm (determination) incurs punishment, distinguishing between sin and worldly effects.

Core Idea
Only firm determination (عزم) to sin is punishable; lesser thoughts are excused.

This lesson unpacks a foundational Hanafi maxim on the gradation of internal states. The poetical couplet lists five levels of intention, declaring all but the last excused from legal accountability. We then explore the nuanced application of 'azm: it carries sin but does not always trigger worldly consequences, except when the act is completed by intent alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five levels
List the five levels from the couplet: hawajis, dhikr, khatir, hadith al-nafs, 'azm. Note that the first four are excused.
The levels are cumulative; only the last crosses into punishable territory.
2
Understand the exception
The phrase 'except the last, for in it the taking has occurred' means that 'azm is the only level where Allah holds the person accountable. Explain why 'azm is actionable.
The hadith equating determination to kill with actual killing supports this.
3
Distinguish sin from worldly effect
Clarify that 'azm upon sin is sinful in the afterlife, but it does not necessarily produce the same worldly ruling (e.g., talaq does not occur if the act is not actually done).
Worldly rulings depend on external action, not mere intent.
4
Apply to the furu case
Work through the conditional talaq scenario: the husband intends to drink but does not; talaq is not triggered. This shows that 'azm alone does not fulfill the condition.
The condition requires actual drinking, not merely intending it.
5
Note the exception
If the determined act is completed by mere intent (e.g., kufr), then 'azm incurs both sin and the worldly ruling. Explain the rationale.
Kufr is a state of belief; intention alone suffices to establish it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مراتب القصد خمس هاجس ذكروا
يليه هم فعزم كلها رفعت
و خاطر فحديث النفس فاستمعا
سوى الاخير ففيه الاخذ قد وقعا
(روح المعانی ج ۳ جس : ۱۰۴)
عزم کے سلسلہ میں بعض محققین کی رائے یہ ہے کہ عزم علی المعصیة پر مواخذہ ہے جیسا کہ حدیث القاتل و لمقتول في النار میں عزم تل کو قتل کے برابر کا درجہ دیکر جہنم کی وعید ہے اسی پر ایک مسئلہ متفرع ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ اگر میں دائمی طور پر شراب چھوڑ دوں تو مجھے طلاق اور وہ شراب نہ پئے لیکن شراب پینے کا عزم رکھے تو بیوی پر طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی معلوم ہوا کہ یہاں پر عزم شرب شرب ہی کے درجہ میں ہے۔
البتہ عزم علی المعصیۃ میں صرف عزم کا گناہ ہو گا عمل بالجوارح کا گناہ نہ ہوگا البتہ اگر عزم ایسی چیز کا ہے جس کا تعلق ہی ایسی چیز ہے جو محض عزم سے پوری ہو جاتی ہو تو محض عزم ہی کا گناہ نہیں بلکہ پھر عمل بالجوارح کا بھی گناہ ہو گا جیسے کفر و غیرہ ، بزازیہ کا کلام پورا ہوا۔
The levels of intention are five: (1) hawajis (passing thought), (2) dhikr (mention), (3) khatir (thought), (4) hadith al-nafs (self-talk), (5) 'azm (determination). All are excused except the last, for in it the taking has occurred. (Ruh al-Ma'ani vol.3 p.104) Regarding 'azm, some researchers opine that 'azm upon sin is punishable, as in the hadith 'the killer and the killed are in the Fire' where 'azm for killing is equal to killing and threatened with Hell. A derived case: if a man says to his wife, 'If I permanently leave wine, I am divorced,' and he does not drink wine but intends to drink it, then divorce does not occur. So here, 'azm to drink is in the level of drinking itself. However, 'azm upon sin is only sinful without the sin of limb action. But if the 'azm is for something that is completed by mere 'azm (like kufr), then both the sin of 'azm and limb action are incurred. The statement of al-Bazzaziyya ends.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental rule on the gradation of internal states. The couplet lists five levels: hawajis (passing thoughts), dhikr (mention), khatir (thought), hadith al-nafs (self-talk), and 'azm (determination). All except the last are excused from legal accountability. The author then discusses 'azm, citing a hadith that equates determined murder intent to murder in punishment. A furu' is given: if a husband makes talaq conditional on permanently leaving alcohol but does not drink but intends to, talaq does not occur. This shows 'azm does not always trigger worldly effects. However, if 'azm is for something achieved solely by intent (like kufr), both sin and worldly effect apply. This is a nuanced Hanafi position on intention's legal weight.

Key Terms
عزم (‘azm): Firm determination to commit an act; the only level of internal intent that incurs punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the legal status of 'azm (determination) to commit a sin?
A) It is completely excused like passing thoughts.
B) It is sinful but does not always trigger the worldly ruling of the act.
C) It always results in the same punishment as the act.
D) It is only sinful if the act is kufr.

Key Takeaway
Only firm determination ('azm) to sin is punishable, but it does not automatically produce worldly effects except when the act is completed by mere intent (like kufr).

Tamyez: The Second Condition for Valid Intention in Worship
Defining tamyeez as the second condition for valid intention in worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of tamyez, identify its branches (furu'), and apply the hadith of raf' al-qalam to explain why tamyeez is a condition for validity but not obligation.

Core Idea
Without discernment (tamyeez), no act of worship is valid – intention requires understanding.

This lesson defines tamyez (discernment) as the second condition for the validity of intention in worship, as stated by the author. The passage clarifies that a non-discerning child or an insane person cannot perform valid worship, though their acts in liability are treated as accidental. The hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' is cited to support the separation between conditions of obligation (aql and bulugh) and conditions of validity (tamyeez).

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The author states tamyeez as the second condition. Note that tamyeez is the ability to understand and intend meaningfully.
Tamyeez is a shart al-sihha, not shart al-wujub.
2
Note the furu' (branches)
The passage lists several applications: the intentional act of a child/insane is accidental for diya; wudu of intoxicated is nullified; prayer of intoxicated is invalid.
These branches illustrate how lack of tamyeez affects different areas of fiqh.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith of raf' al-qalam is given. Understand that it addresses obligation (taklif), not validity.
The hadith is a dalil for the lifting of obligation, but the passage uses it to show that tamyeez is separate from obligation.
4
Distinguish conditions of validity vs. obligation
Tamyeez is for validity; aql and bulugh are for obligation. A discerning child's worship is valid but not obligatory.
This distinction is crucial for issuing fatwas regarding children's worship.
5
Apply the rule
Use the furu' to see how the condition affects different scenarios, e.g., diya vs. prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثَّانِي: التَّمْيِيرُ فَلَا تَصِحُ عِبَادَةُ صَبِيٍّ غَيْرِ مُمَيِّنٍ، وَلَا مَجْنُونِ وَمِنْ فُرُوْعِهِ عَمْدُ الصَّبِيِّ وَ الْمَجْنُون خَطَأَ وَلكِنَّهُ أَعَمُّ مِنْ كَوَون الصَّبِيِّ مُمَيِّزاً أَوْ لَا، وَيَنْتَقِصُ وُضُوْء السَّكْرَانِ لِعَدَمِ تَمْيِزِهِ وَتَبْطُلُ صَلَاتُهُ بِالسُّكْرِ، كَمَا فِي شَرْحِ مَنْظُوْمَةِ إِبْنِ وَهْبَانَ.
وشرط افتراضهما عقل و بلوغ فلا تجب على مجنون و صبى لانهما عبادة محضة و ليسا مخاطبين بها.
و عمد الصبي والمجنون خطأ و فيه الدية على العاقلة.
عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال رفع القلم عن ثلاثة عن النائم حتى يستيقظ و عن الصبى حتى يحتلم و عن المجنون حتى يعقل.
و عمد الصبی و المجنون و المعتوه خطأ بخلاف السكران و المغمى عليه.
The second: discernment (tamyeez). Thus the worship of a non-discerning child and an insane person is not valid. And among its branches is that the intentional act of the child and the insane is accidental (khata), but it is general whether the child is discerning or not. And the wudu of an intoxicated person is nullified due to his lack of discernment, and his prayer is invalidated by intoxication, as in Sharh Manzumat Ibn Wahban. And the condition for their obligation is intellect and puberty, so it is not obligatory upon the insane and the child because they are pure worship and they are not addressed by it. And the intentional act of the child and the insane is accidental, and the blood money (diya) is upon the 'aqila. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he regains sanity.' And the intentional act of the child, the insane, and the feeble-minded is accidental, unlike the intoxicated and the unconscious.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage establishes tamyez (discernment, i.e., the ability to understand and intend meaningfully) as the second condition for the validity of intention in worship. Without it, worship is not valid. The author lists furu' (applications): the intentional act of a child or insane person is treated as accidental (khata) for the purpose of diya; the wudu and prayer of an intoxicated person are invalid due to lack of discernment. The hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' is cited as evidence that children (before puberty) and the insane are not legally responsible (mukallaf). However, the passage notes that the ruling of 'amd being khata applies to all children, discerning or not, in the context of financial liability. The condition of obligation ('aqil and baligh) is separate from the condition of validity (tamyeez).

Key Terms
تَمْيِيز (tamyeez): The intellectual capacity to understand basic concepts of worship and form a meaningful intention.
خَطَأ (khata): Accidental or mistaken act, as opposed to intentional (amd). In Hanafi fiqh, the intentional act of a child or insane is treated as khata for liability.
سُكْر (sukr): Intoxication; a state that negates tamyeez and thus invalidates worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the wudu of an intoxicated person?
A) It remains valid if he had proper intention before intoxication.
B) It is nullified due to lack of discernment.
C) It is valid only if he is a discerning child.
D) It is valid because intoxication is not a nullifier.

Key Takeaway
Tamyeez is a condition for the validity of worship, not for its obligation; a discerning child's worship is valid, and the hadith of raf' al-qalam only lifts obligation.

intermediate
10 min
Discernment as a Condition for Valid Intention
Qa'ida with furu‘ branches on tamyiz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the qa'ida regarding tamyiz as a condition for intention, identify its furu‘ branches, and apply the Hanafi distinction between the child/insane and the drunkard in legal responsibility.

Core Idea
Without discernment, intention is invalid; the child's deliberate act is error, while the drunkard bears full responsibility due to his own fault.

This lesson explores the second condition for the validity of intention (niyyah) in worship: discernment (tamyiz). The author of al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents a qa'ida that forms the basis for rulings on children, the insane, and drunkards. We will examine the furu‘ branches derived from this principle, including the treatment of intentional acts as error and the consequences for wudu and prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Qa'ida
The second condition for valid intention is discernment; without it, worship is invalid. This is the core principle.
Applies to all acts of worship that require niyyah.
2
Identify the First Branch
The intentional act of a child or insane person is treated as error (khatā') regarding liability, regardless of whether the child is discerning or not.
Based on the hadith of lifted pen (raf‘ al-qalam).
3
Identify the Second Branch
The drunkard's wudu is invalidated and his prayer becomes invalid due to lack of discernment, because he caused his own state.
Contrast with child/insane: drunkard is responsible because his loss of discernment is self-inflicted.
4
Consider the Dalil
The hadith 'raf‘ al-qalam' from Abu Dawud establishes that children and the insane are not legally responsible for worship or crimes.
This is the textual basis for treating their acts as error.
5
Note the Exception
The drunkard is distinguished because his lack of discernment results from his own choice; thus his acts are not treated as error and he bears full liability.
This exception is derived from the principle that one cannot benefit from one's own wrongdoing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثَّانِي: التَّمْيِيرُ فَلَا تَصِحُ عِبَادَةُ صَبِيٍّ غَيْرُ مُمَيِّنٍ، وَلَا مَجْنُونِ وَمِنْ فُرُوْعِهِ عَمْدُ الصَّبِيِّ وَ الْمَجْنُون خَطَأَ وَلكِنَّهُ أعَمُّ مِنْ كَوّن الصَّبِيِّ مُمَيِّزاً أولاً ، وَيَنْتَقِصُ وُضُوْء السَّكْرَانِ لِعَدَمِ تَمْيِيزِهِ وَتَبْطُلُ صَلَاتُهُ بِالسُّكْرِ، كَمَا فِي شَرْحِ مَنْظُوْمَةٍ إِبْنِ وَهْبَانَ. :ترجمه: دوسری شرط تمیز ہے غیر میز بچہ اور مجنون کی عبادت صحیح نہیں ہے اور اس کی جزئیات میں سے ہے کہ بچے اور مجنون کا عہد بھی خطا ہے لیکن یہ عام ہے کہ بچہ میز ہویانہ ہو اور نشہ آور کا وضوٹوٹ جاتا ہے تمیز نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اس کی نماز باطل ہے نشہ کی وجہ سے شرح منظومہ ابن و بیان میں ایسا ہی ہے۔ تشریح: دوسری شرط صحت نیت کے لئے تمیز کا ہونا ہے جس کے بغیر عبادت صحیح نہیں ہوتی ہے اور یہاں تمیز سے مراد شعور ہے اس وجہ سے کہا جاتا ہے کہ غیر ممیز بچے اور مجنون کی عبادت عدم شعور کی وجہ سے بیج نہ ہوگی۔ و شرط افتراضهما عقل و بلوغ و تحته في الشامية فلا تجب على مجنون و صبى لانهما عبادة محضة و ليسا مخاطبين بها . (شامی زکریاج ۳ س: ۱۷۳) اگر بچہ اور مجنون کسی کام کو عدا بھی کریں تب بھی وہ خطا کے درجہ میں ہو گا لیکن یہ حکم دیت کے سلسلہ میں ہے ورنہ تو نماز اگر چه ی میز پر لازم نہیں ہے لیکن درست ہے۔ و عمد الصبي والمجنون خطأ و فيه الدية على العاقلة نیز ابودا و وشریف کی حدیث ہے " عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال رفع القلم عن ثلاثة عن النائم حتى يستيقظ و عن الصبى حتى يحتلم و عن المجنون حتى يعقل " اس میں بچہ عام ہے ممیز ہو یا غیر ممیز ۔ نیز شامی میں ہے: و عمد الصبی و المجنون والمعتوه خطأ بخلاف السكران و المغمى و تحته في الشامية اى فى حكم الخطأ فى وجوب المال. (شامی ج ۱ ص:۲۳۹) عليه شروع کردی اور دور ان مسلوق نشہ ہو گیا جس سے مقتل ماؤف ہوگئی تو اس کا وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا اور نماز باطل ہو جائے گی وينقض وضوء السكران: اگر کسی نے شراب پی اور باوضو ہو کر اچھی طرح منہ صاف کر کے نماز پڑھنی عدم شعور کی وجہ سے۔ وفيها الاغماء و المجنون والغشى والسكر ..... إلى قوله والصحيح ما نقل عن شمس الأئمة الحلوانى انه اذا دخل في بعض مشيته تحرك كذا في الخلاصة (بند بين :۱۲)
The second: discernment. So the worship of a non-discerning child and an insane person is not valid. Among its branches: the intentional act of a child and an insane person is (considered) error, but it is general whether the child is discerning or not. The ablution of a drunkard is invalidated due to his lack of discernment, and his prayer becomes invalid due to drunkenness, as in Sharh Manzumah Ibn Wahban. Commentary [Urdu]... And the condition for obligation of both is intellect and puberty, and under it in al-Shamiyya: it is not obligatory on an insane person and a child because they are pure worship and they are not addressed by it. (Shami 3:173) If a child and an insane person intentionally do something, it is still in the category of error, but this ruling pertains to blood-money; otherwise, prayer, though not obligatory on a discerning child, is still valid. The intentional act of a child and an insane person is error, and blood-money is on the 'aqila. Also in Sunan Abi Dawud: 'The Prophet said: The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he regains sanity.' In this hadith, 'child' is general, whether discerning or not. Also in al-Shami: The intentional act of a child, an insane person, and a mentally deficient person is error, unlike the drunkard and the unconscious. And under it in al-Shamiyya: i.e., in the ruling of error regarding financial obligation. (Shami 1:239) He started... and during the journey he became drunk, so his target was killed; then his ablution is invalidated and his prayer becomes invalid. The ablution of the drunkard is invalidated: if someone drank wine, performed ablution, cleaned his mouth well, and started to pray, but during the prayer he became drunk and lost consciousness, so his ablution is invalidated and his prayer becomes invalid due to lack of consciousness. And in it (the texts): unconsciousness, insanity, fainting, drunkenness... until the statement: the correct view is what is transmitted from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani: if he enters into some of his will, it moves. Thus in al-Khulasa (section 12).
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage defines the second condition for the validity of intention (niyyah): discernment (tamyiz). The author states that worship from a non-discerning child or an insane person is invalid. From this principle are derived several branches: the intentional act of such persons is legally treated as error (khatā'), whether the child is discerning or not. The drunkard's condition is different—because he loses discernment through his own choice, his wudu is broken and his prayer invalidated. The passage cites the hadith of the lifted pen from Abi Dawud to show that children and the insane are not legally responsible. However, for blood-money (diyah), their deliberate actions are still considered as accidental errors, subjecting the 'āqila (tribal guarantors) to liability. A distinction is made between the drunkard and the insane/unconscious: the drunkard's acts are not treated as error because his lack of discernment is self-inflicted. The discussion ends with a verification from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani regarding the unconscious person.

Key Terms
التميير (al-tamyīz): The state of discernment or consciousness required for the validity of intention in worship.
عمد الصبي والمجنون خطأ (‘amd al-sabiyyi wa al-majnūni khaṭa’): The intentional act of a child or insane person is legally treated as an error (khatā’), meaning it carries the liability of accidental harm, not intentional crime.
رفع القلم (raf‘ al-qalam): The lifting of the pen: legal responsibility is removed for three categories: sleeper, child, and insane.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the intentional act of a drunkard who commits a crime while drunk?
A) It is treated as error (khatā') because he lacked discernment.
B) It is treated as intentional (amd) because he caused his own drunkenness.
C) It is neither error nor intentional; it is excused.
D) It is considered an accident with diyah on the 'aqila.

Key Takeaway
Discernment is a condition for valid intention; the child/insane are not responsible, while the drunkard is fully accountable because he caused his own lack of discernment.

Knowledge of the Intended Act and the Exception for Ambiguous Ihram
Explaining the exception to the rule of knowledge of intended act in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intention requires knowledge of the intended act, identify the exception for ambiguous ihram in Hajj, and explain the basis in the practice of ‘Alī (RA).

Core Idea
Intention requires knowing what act you intend, except in Hajj: ambiguous ihram is valid based on the Prophet's approval of ‘Alī.

This passage addresses the third condition for valid intention: knowledge of the intended act (al-‘ilm bi al-manwī). Generally, one must know the specific worship being performed — ignorance even of its obligation invalidates the act. However, Hajj has a unique exception: entering ihram without specifying whether for Hajj, ‘Umrah, or both is valid. This exception is established by the precedent of Sayyidunā ‘Alī (RA), who said, 'I intend what the Messenger of Allah intends,' and the Prophet approved. The lesson explores the rule, its exception, and the juristic method of abandoning qiyas for a textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
State the third condition: one must know the intended act (e.g., that it is prayer, fasting, etc.) and its specific type if applicable.
The general rule applies to all acts of worship except where specified otherwise.
2
Note the Exception
Recognize that for Hajj, an ambiguous ihram (al-iḥrām al-mubham) without specifying the type is valid.
This exception is explicit in the Hanafi texts from al-Qunyah and al-Shamiyya.
3
Examine the Dalil
The evidence is the action of ‘Alī (RA) who assumed ihram with the Prophet saying, 'What the Messenger of Allah intends, I intend,' and the Prophet approved it.
This is a textual evidence (naṣṣ) that overrides qiyas.
4
Understand the Juristic Principle
In Hanafi usul, a specific textual proof (dalīl naqlī) can override general qiyas. Here, the exception is established despite qiyas requiring specification.
This is an example of istihsan (juristic preference) based on a stronger evidence.
5
Apply the Ruling
If someone makes ambiguous ihram, it is valid. If they specify before starting rituals, that specification counts. If they begin actions (e.g., tawaf, sa‘y), it becomes fixed as ‘Umrah.
The practical consequence: the individual may later decide, but once actions commence, it is set.

الثَّالِثُ: العِلْمُ بِالْمَنْوِي فَمَنْ جَهل فرضيَّة الصَّلاةِ لَمْ تَصِحُ مِنْهُ، كَمَا قَدَّمْنَاهُ عَن القِنْيَةِ إِلَّا فِي الْحَجِّ فَإِنَّهُمْ صَرَّحُوا بصحة الإحْرَامِ الْمُنْهم؛ لأنَّ عَلِيًّا أَحْرَمَ بِمَا أَحْرَم بهِ النَّبِي الله وَصَحْحَهُ، فَإِنْ عَيْنَ حَمَّا أَوْ عُمْرَةَ صَحَ إِنْ كَانَ قَبْلَ الشَّرُوعِ فِي الأَفْعَالِ، وَإِنْ شَرَعَ تَعَيَّنَتْ عُمْرَةً. :ترجمه تیسری شرط منوی کا معلوم ہوتا ہے چنانچہ جو نماز ہی کی فرضیت سے ناواقف ہو اس کی نماز درست نہیں جیسا کہ ہم نے پہلے قنیہ کے حوالہ سے بیان کیا ہے جو حج کے چنانچہ فقہاء نے مبہم احرام کے صحیح ہونے کی مراحت فرمائی ہے اس لئے کہ حضرت علی نے وہی احرام باندھا جو نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے باندھا اور نبی اکرم صلی الہ علی علیہ وسلم نے اسے درست قرار دیا پھر اگرحج یا عمرہ متعین کیا تو صحیح ہے اگر وہ افعال شروع کرنے سے پہلے ہو اوراگر فعال شروع کر دیئے تو عمرہ متعین ہے۔ تشریح تیسری شرط صحت نیت کے لئے منوی کے عبادت ہونے کا علم ہوا گرمنوی کا علم نہ ہو تو عبادت درست ز ہوگی ٹا کسی کو فرضیت نماز ہی کا علم نہ ہو اور وہ نماز پڑھے تو اس کی نماز درست نہ ہوگی یہ مسئلہ اوپر کے مسئلہ پر ہی متفرع ہے۔ والشرط ان يعلم بقلبه اى صلاة يصلى (ہندین انس: ۶۵) ولابد من التعيين عند النية فلو جهل الفرضية لم يجز (شالى ج۲ : ۹۵ ) الإفى الحج بیاد پر مسئلہ گذرا تھا کہ منوی کا علم ہونا ضروری ہے آج کا مسئلہ اس سے مستقلی ہے قیاس اگر چہ اس کا متقاضی ہے کہ حج میں بھی منوی کے علم کے بغیر احرام درست نہ ہو لیکن حضرت علی کا واقعہ نفس کی شکل میں موجود ہے اس لئے ہم نے قیاس کو یہاں چھوڑ دیا چنانچہ اگر کسی نے بہم احرام باندھا ایران تجمیع ، یا افراد کی تعین نہیں کی تو بھی اس کا اتمام درست ہے پھر اگر افعال حج شروع کرنے سے پہلے تعین کر دی تو تعیین معتبر ہے اور اگر افعال شروع کر دئیے تو یا فعال نمرہ کے افعال ہوں گے دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ حضرت علی نے نبی اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے ساتھ حج ادا کیا تو میم احرام باندھا کہ جو رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا احترام ہے وہی میرا احترام ہے اور رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے
The third: knowledge of the intended (act). So whoever is ignorant of the obligation of prayer, his prayer is not valid, as we have previously mentioned from al-Qunyah, except in Hajj, for they have explicitly stated the validity of ambiguous (mubham) ihram, because ‘Alī assumed ihram with what the Prophet assumed ihram and he (the Prophet) approved it. Then if he specifies Hajj or ‘Umrah, it is valid if it is before commencing the actions, and if he commences (the actions), then it becomes specifically ‘Umrah. Commentary [Urdu]... The condition is that he knows in his heart which prayer he is praying. (Hindiya 65) And specification at the time of intention is necessary; so if he is ignorant of the obligation, it is not permissible. (Shami 2:95) The exception is in Hajj as the issue passed: knowledge of the intended is necessary. This issue is independent from it. Qiyas would demand that ihram without knowledge of the intended is invalid even in Hajj, but the incident of ‘Alī is present as a text, so we have abandoned qiyas here. Thus if someone assumes ambiguous ihram without specifying tamattu’, ifrād, or qirān, it is still valid. Then if he specifies before the actions, it is valid; but if he commences the actions, then the actions of ‘Umrah become fixed (as ‘Umrah). The proof is that ‘Alī assumed ihram with the Prophet saying, 'What the Messenger of Allah has intended, that is my intention,' and the Prophet approved it.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage explains the third condition of intention: knowledge of the intended act (al-‘ilm bi al-manwī). The general rule is that one must know what specific worship one is performing. If a person is ignorant of the very obligation of prayer (e.g., does not know it is fard), then his prayer is invalid. This is based on the texts from al-Qunyah and al-Shamiyya. However, there is a special exception for Hajj: an ambiguous (mubham) ihram is valid, even without specifying whether it is for Hajj, ‘Umrah, or both. This is established by the practice of Sayyidunā ‘Alī, who, when accompanying the Prophet, said, 'I intend what the Messenger of Allah intends,' and the Prophet approved his ihram. Consequently, if one makes an ambiguous ihram, it is valid. If before starting the rituals he specifies a particular type (tamattu’, ifrād, qirān), that specification is effective. But if he begins the actions (i.e., starts with ‘Umrah or Hajj rituals), then it becomes fixed as ‘Umrah (since the first actions correspond to ‘Umrah). This departure from qiyas is justified by the specific textual evidence (naṣṣ) from the Prophet’s approval. The passage emphasizes that this is an exception; in all other acts of worship, knowledge of the intended is strictly required.

Key Terms
العلم بالمنوي (al-‘ilm bil manwī): Knowledge of the specific act of worship one intends, including its nature (e.g., that it is prayer, fasting, etc.) and sometimes its specific type.
الإحرام المبهم (al-iḥrām al-mubham): Ambiguous ihram: entering the state of ihram without specifying whether it is for Hajj, ‘Umrah, or both.
تعيين النية (ta‘yīn al-niyyah): Specification of the intention: distinguishing the particular act (e.g., Zuhr prayer from ‘Asr, or Hajj from ‘Umrah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a person who assumes ihram without specifying whether for Hajj or ‘Umrah?
A) The ihram is invalid because intention requires specification.
B) The ihram is valid, but if he starts the actions, it becomes ‘Umrah.
C) The ihram is valid only if he specifies before the actions of ‘Umrah.
D) The ihram is valid only for Hajj by default.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of the intended act is a condition for valid intention, except in Hajj where ambiguous ihram is valid based on the prophetic precedent.

The Third Condition of Intention: Knowledge of the Intended Act
Explains the third condition of niyyah with its exception in Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of al-ilm bil-manwi to determine the validity of intention in worship and identify the exception for Hajj with its legal basis.

Core Idea
Intention requires knowing what you intend — except in Hajj, where ambiguous intent suffices by prophetic precedent.

This passage establishes that for an act of worship to be valid, the intention must include knowledge of the specific act and its legal status. This rule is applied strictly in prayer but relaxed in Hajj due to the example of Ali (RA). Understanding this nuance is crucial for issuing fatwas regarding the validity of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states: 'Knowledge of the intended act (al-ilm bil-manwi) is required in worship.' Recognize that this is a general condition for intention.
2
Recognize the default application
In prayer, ignorance of the obligatory nature (fardiyyah) invalidates the prayer. This shows the default strict application.
The source cites al-Qiniyah and al-Hindiyya.
3
Note the exception
Hajj is an exception: an ambiguous ihram (mubham) is valid even without specific knowledge of the type (Tamattu, Ifrad, Qiran).
4
Trace the dalil
The exception is based on the hadith of Ali (RA) who made an ambiguous ihram saying 'I make ihram as the Prophet made ihram' and the Prophet validated it.
This is a dalil naqli.
5
Resolve the apparent conflict
The exception does not mean knowledge is entirely waived; the obligation (fardiyyah) must still be known. Only the specific type may be ambiguous. Thus, the rule remains intact with a narrow exception.
The commentary clarifies that Ali knew Hajj was obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث: الْعِلْمُ بِالْمَنْوِي فَمَنْ جَهل فرضيَّة الصَّلاةِ لَمْ تَصِحُ مِنْهُ، كَمَا قَدَّمْنَاهُ عَن القِنْيَةِ إِلَّا فِي الْحَجِّ فَإِنَّهُمْ صَرَّحُوا بصحة الإحْرَامِ الْمُبْهَمِ؛ لأنَّ عَلِيًّا أَحْرَمَ بِمَا أَحْرَم بهِ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ وَصَحَّحَهُ، فَإِنْ عَيَّنَ حَجًّا أَوْ عُمْرَةَ صَحَ إِنْ كَانَ قَبْلَ الشَّرُوعِ فِي الأفْعَالِ، وَإِنْ شَرَعَ تَعَيَّنَتْ عُمْرَةً.
ترجمه: تیسری شرط منوی کا معلوم ہوتا ہے چنانچہ جو نماز ہی کی فرضیت سے ناواقف ہو اس کی نماز درست نہیں جیسا کہ ہم نے پہلے قنیہ کے حوالہ سے بیان کیا ہے سوائے حج کے چنانچہ فقہاء نے مبہم احرام کے صحیح ہونے کی تصریح فرمائی ہے اس لئے کہ حضرت علی نے وہی احرام باندھا جو نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے باندھا اور نبی اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اسے درست قرار دیا پھر اگر حج یا عمرہ متعین کیا تو صحیح ہے اگر وہ افعال شروع کرنے سے پہلے ہو اور اگر افعال شروع کر دیئے تو عمرہ متعین ہے۔
تشریح: تیسری شرط صحت نیت کے لئے منوی کے عبادت ہونے کا علم ہے اگر منوی کا علم نہ ہو تو عبادت درست نہ ہوگی جیسے کسی کو فرضیت نماز ہی کا علم نہ ہو اور وہ نماز پڑھے تو اس کی نماز درست نہ ہوگی یہ مسئلہ اوپر کے مسئلہ پر ہی متفرع ہے۔
والشرط ان يعلم بقلبه اى صلاة يصلى (ہندیہ ج ۱: ۶۵)
ولابد من التعيين عند النية فلو جهل الفرضية لم يجز (شامی ج ۲: ۹۵) إلا في الحج بیاد پر مسئلہ گذرا تھا کہ منوی کا علم ہونا ضروری ہے آج کا مسئلہ اس سے مستقلی ہے قیاس اگر چہ اس کا متقاضی ہے کہ حج میں بھی منوی کے علم کے بغیر احرام درست نہ ہو لیکن حضرت علی کا واقعہ نفس کی شکل میں موجود ہے اس لئے ہم نے قیاس کو یہاں چھوڑ دیا چنانچہ اگر کسی نے مبہم احرام باندھا بغیر تمتع یا افراد کی تعین نہیں کی تو بھی اس کا احرام درست ہے پھر اگر افعال حج شروع کرنے سے پہلے تعین کر دی تو تعیین معتبر ہے اور اگر افعال شروع کر دئیے تو وہ افعال عمرہ کے افعال ہوں گے دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ حضرت علی نے نبی اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے ساتھ حج ادا کیا تو مبہم احرام باندھا کہ جو رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا احرام ہے وہی میرا احرام ہے اور رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اسے درست قرار دیا لیکن حضرت علی کو حج کی فرضیت معلوم تھی صرف قرآن تمتع اور افراد وغیرہ کی نوعیت مجہول تھی تو العلم بالمنوی موجود تھا اس لئے العلم بالمنوی سے اس صورت کا استثنا درست معلوم نہیں ہوتا جبکہ مصنف کی مراد بظاہر یہی ہے کہ یشترط العلم بالمنوى في كل عبادة الا في الحج جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نفس العلم بالمنوی ہی سے حج کا استثنا کیا جارہا ہے۔
ان الحج يصح بمطلق النية بلا تعيين الفرضية بخلاف الصلاوة (شامی زکریا ج ۱۳ ص: ۴۵۷)
Third condition: knowledge of the intended act. Whoever is ignorant of the obligatory nature of prayer, his prayer is not valid, as we have previously mentioned from al-Qiniyah, except in Hajj, for they have explicitly stated the validity of ambiguous ihram because Ali (RA) assumed ihram with what the Prophet (PBUH) assumed and he validated it. Then if he specifies Hajj or Umrah, it is valid if before starting the actions. If he started, it becomes specifically Umrah. Translation: Third condition: the intended act must be known; so one who is unaware of the obligation of prayer, his prayer is invalid as we mentioned earlier from Qinyah. Except in Hajj, the jurists have stated the validity of ambiguous ihram because Ali assumed the same ihram as the Prophet and the Prophet validated it. Then if he specifies Hajj or Umrah, it is valid if before beginning actions, and if he began the actions, then it is specified as Umrah. Commentary: The third condition for the validity of intention is knowledge that the intended act is worship. If one does not know the intended act, the worship is invalid. For example, if someone does not know the obligation of prayer and prays, his prayer is invalid. This issue branches from the previous. And the condition is that he knows in his heart which prayer he prays (Hindiyya 1:65). And specification is necessary at the time of intention; if he is ignorant of the obligation, it is not permissible (Shami 2:95). Except in Hajj, as the issue passed earlier that knowledge of the intended act is necessary. The current issue is independent from it. By analogy, it would require that in Hajj too, ihram without knowledge is invalid, but the incident of Ali is present as a text, so we leave analogy here. So if someone assumes ambiguous ihram without specifying Tamattu or Ifrad, it is still valid. Then if he specifies before starting the actions, the specification is valid; if he starts the actions, they become actions of Umrah. The proof is that Ali performed Hajj with the Prophet and assumed ambiguous ihram, saying 'The ihram of the Prophet is my ihram.' The Prophet validated it. But Ali knew the obligation of Hajj; only the type (Qiran, Tamattu, Ifrad) was unknown, so knowledge of the intended act existed. Therefore, the exception of this case from knowledge of the intended act does not seem correct. The author's intention is apparently that knowledge of the intended act is required in every worship except in Hajj, indicating that the exception is from the very knowledge of the intended act. 'Verily Hajj is valid with absolute intention without specifying the obligation, unlike prayer' (Shami Zakariyya 13:457).
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage defines the third condition for valid intention: knowledge of the intended act (al-ilm bil-manwi). The author states that if a person is ignorant of the obligatory nature of prayer (fardiyyat al-salat), his prayer is invalid. This is based on the principle that intention requires knowledge of what is being intended. An exception is made for Hajj: an ambiguous ihram (mubham) is valid, based on the precedent of Ali (RA) who made an ambiguous ihram following the Prophet. The passage clarifies that the exception is specifically about ignorance of the type (e.g., Tamattu, Ifrad) not ignorance of the obligation itself, since Ali knew Hajj was obligatory. The author cites various sources: al-Qiniyah, al-Hidayah, al-Shami, and al-Hindiyya.

Key Terms
الْعِلْمُ بِالْمَنْوِي (al-ilm bil-manwi): Knowledge of the specific act being intended, including its legal status and category

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person prays without knowing that prayer is obligatory?
A) The prayer is valid because intention was still present
B) The prayer is invalid because knowledge of the intended act's obligation is a condition
C) The prayer is valid if he intended to pray
D) The prayer is makruh but valid

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of the intended act (al-ilm bil-manwi) is a condition for valid intention in worship, with a narrow exception for Hajj where only the type may be ambiguous, not the obligation.

The Fourth Condition of Intention: No Contradictory Act
Defines the fourth condition of intention and applies it to worship and apostasy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify what constitutes a contradictory act (munafi) and apply the Hanafi qawida regarding antecedent intention to determine the validity of an act of worship.

Core Idea
A valid intention must be free from contradictory acts between niyyah and action.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair lays down the fourth condition for the validity of intention: no contradictory act. The Hanafi school permits making intention before the takbir, but only if no act that contradicts the worship occurs in between. This qawida has practical implications for prayer, hajj, and even the companionship of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qawida
The passage states the rule: 'النِّيَّةُ الْمُتَقَدِّمَةُ عَلَى التَّحْرِيْمَةِ جَائِزَةٌ بِشَرْطِ أَنْ لا يَأْتِيَ بَعْدَهَا بِمُنَافٍ لَيْسَ مِنْهَا' (Intention preceding takbir is permissible on condition no contradictory act occurs).
This is a minor maxim (sughra) governing conditions of intention.
2
Define 'Munafi'
A contradictory act is any act that is not from the type of worship and is inconsistent with its nature. Acts that are part of the worship (like walking to the mosque) are not munafi.
Munafi is broader than just physical acts; it includes any act that contradicts the essence of the worship.
3
Apply to Worship
If a person makes intention for prayer then eats or plays before takbir, the intention is broken; prayer is invalid.
This applies to all acts of worship, not just prayer.
4
Apply to Apostasy
Apostasy during worship is a munafi that invalidates the act. Also, apostasy after being a companion of the Prophet invalidates that companionship if one dies upon it.
If one returns to Islam during the Prophet's lifetime, companionship is restored; after his death, there is consideration.
5
Note the Exception
The passage mentions that if an apostate returns to Islam during the Prophet's lifetime, the companionship is restored; after his death, there is a question (nazar).
This shows the qawida is applied contextually.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرَّابِعُ: أنْ لا يَأْتِي بِمُنَافٍ بَيْنَ النِّيَّةِ وَالْمَنْوِي قَالُوْا: إِنَّ النِّيَّةَ الْمُتَقَدِّمَةَ عَلَى التَّحْرِيْمَةِ جَائِزَةٌ بِشَرْطِ أَنْ لا يَأْتِيَ بَعْدَهَا بِمُنَافٍ لَيْسَ مِنْهَا، وَعَلَى هَذَا تَبْطُلُ الْعِبَادَةُ بِالْاِرْتِدَادِ فِي أَثْنَا ئِهَا، وَتَبْطُلُ صُحْبَةُ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ بِالزِّيَادَةِ إِذَامَاتَ عَلَيْهِ، فَإِنْ أَسْلَمَ بَعْدَهُ، فَإِنْ كَانَ فِي حَيَاتِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ، فَلَامَانِعُ مِنْ عَوْدِهَا، وَإِلَّا فَفِي عَوْدِهَا نَظْرٌ، كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ الْعِرَاقِيُّ.
ترجمه: چوتھی شرط یہ ہے کہ نیت اور منوی کے درمیان کوئی ایسا کام نہ کرے جو منافی ہو، فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ تحریمہ پر نیت متقدمہ جائز ہے اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ اس کے بعد کوئی ایسا کام نہ کرے جو منوی کے قبیل سے نہ ہو اور اسی بنا پر دوران عبادت ارتداد سے عبادت باطل ہو جاتی ہے اور نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی صحبت ارتداد سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے جبکہ اس پر انتقال ہو پھر اگر اس کے بعد ایمان لے آئے تو اگر آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی حیات مبارکہ ہو تو اس کے لوٹ جانے سے کوئی چیز رکاوٹ نہیں ہے ورنہ اس کے لوٹنے میں نظر ہے جیسا کہ عراقی نے ذکر کیا ہے۔
تشریح: چوتھی شرط یہ ہے کہ نیت اور منوی کے درمیان کوئی ایسا عمل نہ پایا جائے جو نیت کے منافی ہو اگر عبادت سے ہی متعلق ہو تو کوئی رکاوٹ نہیں جیسے گھر سے وضو کر کے نماز کی نیت سے مسجد گیا اور اسی نیت سے جا کر نماز پڑھی تو درست ہے اگر چہ اس کے گھر اور مسجد کے درمیان چلنے کا عمل بھی پایا گیا لیکن وہ منافی صلاۃ نہیں ہے اور اگر منافی صلاۃ ہو جیسے نیت صلاۃ اور تحریمہ کے درمیان کھیل کود یا کھانا پینا تو اس نیت سے نماز درست نہ ہوگی منافی عمل کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے۔
قالوا ان النية المتقدمة: نیت اور عبادت کے درمیان اگر کوئی منافی صلاۃ عمل نہ پایا جائے تو پیشگی نیت تحریمہ پر معتبر ہے اور منافی صلاۃ وہ عمل ہے کہ جس کا عبادت یا نماز سے کوئی تعلق نہ ہو۔
النية المتقدمة على التكبير كالقائمة عند التكبير اذا لم يوجد ما يقطع وهو عمل لا يليق بالصلاة. (ہندیہ ج ۱ ص: ۶۷)
و على هذا تبطل العبادة بالإرتداد: علامہ ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ اس اصول کی وجہ سے بند بھی
Fourth: that he does not bring something contradictory between the intention and the intended. They said: the intention preceding the takbir is permissible on condition that after it he does not bring something contradictory that is not from it. On this basis, worship is invalidated by apostasy during it, and the companionship of the Prophet (PBUH) is invalidated by apostasy if he dies upon it. Then if he becomes Muslim after that, if it was during his (PBUH) lifetime, there is no obstacle to its return; otherwise there is consideration in its return, as al-Iraqi mentioned. Translation: Fourth condition: no act contradictory between intention and intended. Jurists say that intention preceding takbir is permissible on condition that after it no act contrary to the worship occurs. On this basis, worship is invalidated by apostasy during it, and the companionship of the Prophet is invalidated by apostasy if one dies upon it. Then if he becomes Muslim after that, if it was during the Prophet's lifetime, there is no obstacle to its return; otherwise, there is consideration in its return, as al-Iraqi mentioned. Commentary: The fourth condition is that no act contradictory to the intention occurs between the intention and the intended. If the act is related to the worship, there is no problem, e.g., after making intention for prayer at home, one walks to the mosque—walking is not contradictory to prayer. But if the act is contradictory, like playing, eating, or drinking between intention and takbir, then the prayer is invalid. They said: the antecedent intention is valid if no contradictory act occurs; a contradictory act is one that is not suitable for prayer. (Hindiyya 1:67). On this basis, worship is invalidated by apostasy: Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says that due to this principle, [the worshiper] is also...
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth condition for the validity of intention: there must be no contradictory act (munafi) between the intention and the beginning of the worship. The intention can be made before the takbir, provided that between the intention and the takbir no act that is contradictory to the worship occurs. Acts that are related to the worship (like walking to the mosque) do not break the connection. The key application is apostasy during worship: if a person apostatizes during prayer, the prayer is invalid. Also, if a person apostatizes after being a companion of the Prophet, his companionship is invalidated if he dies upon apostasy; but if he returns to Islam during the Prophet's lifetime, the companionship is restored. After the Prophet's death, there is a question. The passage ends with a reference to Ibn Nujaym's discussion of this principle.

Key Terms
مُنَافٍ (munāfin): An act that contradicts the intended worship and is not from its type
النِّيَّةُ الْمُتَقَدِّمَةُ (an-niyyat al-mutaqaddima): Intention made before the opening takbir
الارتداد (al-irtidad): Apostasy, leaving the fold of Islam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Prayer is valid because the intention was already made
B) Prayer is invalid because eating is a contradictory act
C) Prayer is valid if the snack was small
D) Prayer is valid but makruh

Key Takeaway
A valid intention for worship requires that no act contradictory to that worship occurs between the intention and the commencement of the act.

Conditions for a Traveler's Intention to Stay (Niyyat al-Iqama)
Listing five conditions for a traveler's intention to stay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five conditions for a valid intention to stay according to the Hanafi school and apply the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to determine travel status.

Core Idea
Intention to stay for 15 days in a habitable place with independence changes a traveler to a resident.

This passage from Sharah al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair delineates the precise conditions under which a traveler's intention to stay (niyyat al-iqama) transforms him into a resident (muqim) in Hanafi law. These conditions operationalize the general maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions) by specifying what a valid intention requires. Understanding these conditions is essential for a mufti to correctly advise on travel concessions like qasr al-salah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first condition: no intent to leave
The traveler must not intend to depart from that place to another destination. Moving around within the same locality or wandering without a fixed destination does not invalidate the intention.
This condition ensures that the intention is for a fixed residence.
2
Understand the second condition: the place must be fit for residence
The location must have the capacity for settled life, e.g., basic amenities. Intending to stay on the sea or an uninhabited island is invalid unless provisions are arranged.
This excludes uninhabitable areas.
3
Understand the third condition: unity of location
The intention must be for a single locality. Moving within a distance less than the shar'i travel distance (masafat shar'iyya) does not break unity.
The entire town or city counts as one location.
4
Understand the fourth and fifth conditions: minimum 15 days and independence
The intended stay must be at least fifteen full days. Additionally, the person intending must be independent (mustaqill bi al-ra'y), not a dependent like a wife or slave. Dependents follow the intention of their guardian.
The commentator adds that a captive traveling with his captor is also a dependent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جائے اور اس بہتی سے کسی اور جگہ جانے کا ارادہ نہ ہو خواہ وہ ہستی میں ادھر ادھر چلتا رہے تو کوئی حرج نہیں۔ (۲) وہ جگہ اقامت کی صلاحیت بھی رکھتی ہو لہذا سمند یا کسی جزیروا غیرہ میں اقامت کی نیت غیر معتبر ہوگی بشر طیکہ سمندر با جزیرہ میں قیام وغیرہ کا انتظام نہ ہو۔ (۳) اتحاد موضع جس جگہ شہر نے کی نیت کرے وہ ایک ہی مقام ہو پھر خواہ وہاں سے مسافت شرعی سے کم ادھر ادھر جاتا ر ہے۔ (۴) مدت قیام کم از کم پندرہ یوم ہو اس سے کم نیت کی صورت میں مقیم نہ ہوگا ۔ (۵) استقلال بالرائے یعنی نیت کرنے والا مستقل بالرائے ہو متبوع ہو تابع نہ ہو لہذا بیوی کی نیت اقامت با غلام کی نیت اقامت معتبر نہ ہو گی۔ شارخ فرماتے ہیں تابعین میں وہ قیدی بھی ہیں جو قید کے ساتھ سفر کر رہا ہو درایہ میں ہے کسی مسلمان کو دشمن نے قید کر لیا اگر دشمن کا سفر مدت سفر کے برابر ہو تو قصر کرے ورنہ قصر نہ کرے اگر نہ جانتا ہو تو دریافت کر لے اگر دریافت کرنے کے باوجود نہ بتلائے تو دیکھے اگر دشمن مسافر ہو تو قصر کرے ورنہ نہیں خانیہ میں اس کے مثل ہے۔
He may go and wander around from that flowing [place] without intending to go elsewhere; there is no harm. (2) The place must also have the capacity for residence; therefore, intention to stay in the sea or on an island etc. is invalid, provided there is no arrangement for stay etc. in the sea or island. (3) Unity of location: the place he intends to stay is one location, even if he moves about a distance less than the shar'i distance. (4) Duration of stay: at least fifteen days; with less than that, he does not become a resident. (5) Independence of opinion: the one intending must be independent, a follower, not a dependent; therefore, the wife's intention to stay and the slave's intention to stay are not valid. The commentator says: Among dependents is also the prisoner who is traveling with his captor. In Durraya: If a Muslim is captured by an enemy, if the enemy's travel equals travel distance, he shortens; otherwise not. If he does not know, he should inquire. If after inquiry he is not told, then see: if the enemy is a traveler, he shortens; otherwise not. In Khaniyya it is similar.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage lists five conditions for a traveler’s intention to stay (niyyat al-iqama) to become effective in changing his status from traveler to resident. First, he must not intend to leave that place for another destination, even if he moves around within the area. Second, the place must be fit for settled life; intention to stay on a sea or uninhabited island is invalid unless basic amenities exist. Third, the intention must be for a single location; moving within less than shar'i travel distance does not violate unity. Fourth, the minimum period is fifteen full days; shorter intention leaves him a traveler. Fifth, the one intending must be independent (mustaqill bi al-ra'y), not a dependent like a wife or slave whose intention is not self-sufficient. The commentator adds that a captive traveling with his captor is considered dependent and follows the captor's travel rulings. This passage applies the general maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions) to the specific case of travel and residence.

Key Terms
نیت اقامت (niyyat al-iqama): Intention to stay in a place for at least 15 days with independence, making the traveler a resident.
مسافت شرعی (masafat shar'iyya): The legal distance for travel concessions, approximately three days journey or about 88 km.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for a valid niyyat al-iqama according to the Hanafi school?
A) Intending to stay for at least fifteen full days
B) The place must be suitable for residence
C) The intention must be made by an independent person (mustaqill bi al-ra'y)
D) The traveler must physically remain in one house without moving

Key Takeaway
A traveler's intention to stay must meet five conditions: no intent to leave, habitable place, single locality, minimum 15 days, and independence; the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' underlies these conditions.

Intention to Stay During Prayer and the Lahiq Exception
Ruling on a traveler who intends to stay during prayer, with lahiq exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to determine the ruling for a traveler who intends to stay during prayer, and identify the exception for the lahiq (latecomer) where his intention after the imam finishes is ineffective.

Core Idea
Intention during prayer can change a traveler's obligation, but once the imam finishes, the lahiq's obligation is fixed and cannot be altered.

This passage from Ashbah wa al-Nazair illustrates how the maxim 'matters are judged by intentions' governs a traveler's prayer. While a traveler who intends to stay during the prayer time must complete four rak'ahs, an exception arises for the lahiq (latecomer): his intention after the imam has finished does not affect his obligation. Understanding this nuance is crucial for a mufti when advising travelers in congregational settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recognize that a traveler who intends to stay during the prayer time—whether at the beginning, middle, or end—must complete the full four rak'ahs of a 4-rak'ah prayer. This applies whether he is alone, an imam, a follower, or a mudrik (one who catches the entire prayer with the imam).
The intention to stay changes his status from traveler to resident for that prayer.
2
Locate the Exception
Note that the lahiq (latecomer who joined after the first rak'ah) is excluded from this general rule if he intends to stay after the imam has completed his prayer (taslim). His intention to stay is ineffective.
The exception is based on the concept of istihkam al-fard (the obligation becoming firmly established).
3
Understand the Reasoning
The ruling is grounded in the Hanafi principle that once the imam finishes, the obligation of the lahiq becomes fixed (istahkama). An intention made after that point cannot change his traveler status.
This is a strict application of the maxim that timing matters for the effect of intention.
4
Apply the Maxim 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha'
The maxim is applied: intention (niyyah) is effective when it can still influence the act. Here, the lahiq's act of completing his prayer is already determined, so a later intention does not affect it.
This shows that the maxim is qualified by the stage of the act (before or after completion).
5
Note the Three Exceptional Cases
The commentary identifies three scenarios where the lahiq does complete four rak'ahs despite intending to stay after the imam finishes: 1) when the imam is a resident, 2) when the lahiq intends to stay before the imam finishes (and the imam is a traveler), and 3) another case mentioned indirectly (possibly when the lahiq catches the entire prayer with the imam).
These exceptions highlight that the general rule about lahiq only applies when both imam and follower are travelers and the intention occurs after taslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و إذا نوى المسافر: اگر مسافر نے وقت کے اندر دوران نماز اقامت کی نیت کر لی تو اس کی یہ نیت معتبر ہو گی اس پر چار رکعت پوری کر نا لا زم ہوگا خواہ نماز کے شروع میں نیت کرے یا درمیان میں یا آخر میں اور چاہے منفرد ہو یا مقتدی یا مدرک ہو یا مسبوق ہو سب کا حکم یکساں ہے۔ أَمَّا الَّلاحِقُ لَا يُتِمُّها بنيتها بعد فراغ إمامه لإسْتحْكامِ فَرْضِهِ بِفَرَاعَ إمَامِهِ، كَذَا فِي الخُلاصَةِ وَلَوْ نَوَى بِمَالِ التِّجَارَةِ الْخِدْمَةِ كَانَ لِلْخِدْمَةِ بِالنِّيَّةِ وَلَوْ كَانَ عَلَىٰ عَكْسِهِ لَمْ تُوكَّرْ كَمَا ذَكرَهُ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ: ترجمہ: اور بہر حال لاحق اپنے امام کی فراغت کے بعد اقامت کی نیت سے پوری نماز نہ پڑھی گا اس کے فرض کے امام کی فراغت کے بعد مستحکم ہو جانے کی وجہ سے خلاصہ میں اس طرح سے اگر مال تجارت میں خدمت کی نیت کی تو نیت سے خدمت کے لئے ہو جائے گا اور اس کے برعکس ہو تو نیت مؤثر نہ ہو گی زیلعی نے اسی طرح ذکر کیا ہے البتہ ودیعت میں خیانت کی نیت کرلے تو اس کا حکم صراحی نہیں دیکھا لیکن فتاوی ظہیر یہ میں احرام کی جنایت کے باب میں ہے اگر مودع نے تعدی کی پھر تعدی زائل ہو گئی اور نیت یہی ہے کہ پھر خیانت کرے گا تو تعدی زائل نہ ہوگی مقاومی ظہیر یہ کا کلام پورا ہوا ۔ تشریح : مذکورہ مسئلہ میں لاحق کی ایک صورت کا بیان ہے جو پہلے مسئلہ سے مختلف ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مقتدی لائق مسافر ہو اور امام بھی مسافر ہو اور امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد وہ مسافر لاحق مقتدی اقامت کی نیت کرلے تو اقامت کی نیت کرنے کی وجہ سے وہ لاحق مسافر جو مقتدی ہے اتمام نہیں کرے گا کیونکہ امام کے فارغ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کا فرض مستحکم ہو گیا۔ ولم یك لاحقاً و تحته قال الشامى اما اللاحق اذا ادرك اولی الصلوة و الامام مسافر الى قوله فلا يتغير في حق الامام (شامی زکریا ج ۲، ص: ۶۰۵) البتہ لاحق تین صورتوں میں اقامت کی نیت کی وجہ سے اتمام کرے گا (۲/۱ ۱ ) جب کہ امام مقیم ہو ( ۳) امام مسافر ہو اور امام کے فراغت سے پہلے لاحق مسافر اقامت کی نیت کر لے۔
And if the traveler: If a traveler intends to stay within the time during prayer, this intention is valid, and he must complete four rak'ahs, whether he intends at the beginning, middle, or end, and whether he is alone, a follower, a mudrik, or a masbuq; all have the same ruling. As for the lahiq, he does not complete it by intending to stay after the imam's completion, because his obligation becomes established by the imam's completion. Thus in al-Khulasa. And if he intends for trade goods to be for service, it becomes for service by intention, and if the opposite, it does not have effect, as al-Zayla'i mentioned. Translation: And anyway, the lahiq after his imam's completion will not complete his prayer by intention to stay, because his obligation becomes established after the imam's completion. Thus in al-Khulasa. And if he intends for trade goods to be for service, it becomes for service by intention, and if the opposite, the intention does not have effect, as al-Zayla'i mentioned. However, the ruling on intending betrayal in trust is not explicitly seen, but in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya in the chapter on crimes of ihram: if the depositary transgresses, then removes the transgression, and his intention is to return to it, the transgression does not cease. The words of al-Zahiriyya are complete. Explanation: In the mentioned issue, one case of the lahiq is described which is different from the previous issue: if the follower is a traveler and the imam is also a traveler, and after the imam finishes, that traveler lahiq intends to stay, then due to the intention to stay, that lahiq traveler follower will not complete, because his obligation became established by the imam's completion. And it is not lahiq? Under it al-Shami said: As for the lahiq when he catches the first part of the prayer and the imam is a traveler... up to his words: so it does not change regarding the imam. (Shami Zakariyya vol.2, p.605) However, the lahiq will complete by intention to stay in three cases: (1) when the imam is a resident, (2) the imam is a traveler and the lahiq traveler intends to stay before the imam's completion, (3) ...
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage first establishes a general rule: a traveler who intends to stay during the prayer time—whether at the beginning, middle, or end, and regardless of being an imam, follower, or latecomer—must complete the prayer as four rak'ahs because his intention to stay makes him a resident. The exception is the 'lahiq' (a latecomer who joined the imam after the first rak'ah and misses some rak'ahs). If the lahiq intends to stay after the imam has already completed his prayer, he does not need to complete his missed rak'ahs as four; instead, he completes as a traveler (qasr). The reason is that his obligation (fard) became firmly established (istahkama) at the moment the imam finished, and intention after that cannot change it. The commentary then clarifies that this exception applies only when both imam and follower are travelers. Three cases where the lahiq does complete four rak'ahs: 1) if the imam is a resident, 2) if the imam is a traveler but the lahiq intends to stay before the imam finishes, and 3) another case mentioned in the commentary. This discussion applies the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to the timing of intention relative to the imam's completion.

Key Terms
لاحق (lahiq): A latecomer in congregational prayer who missed one or more rak'ahs with the imam and completes them after the imam's taslim.
استحكام الفرض (istihkam al-fard): The obligation becoming firmly established and unchangeable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a lahiq (latecomer) traveler complete his prayer as four rak'ahs after intending to stay?
A) Only if he intends before the imam starts the prayer
B) If he intends after the imam has finished the prayer
C) If he intends before the imam finishes the prayer and the imam is a traveler
D) He never completes four rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
A traveler's intention to stay during prayer changes his obligation to four rak'ahs, but for the lahiq, intention after the imam finishes is ineffective due to istihkam al-fard.

Intention and Property Classification: Asymmetry in Hanafi Law
Ruling on intention and property categorization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to distinguish when intention alone changes the legal status of property for zakat purposes.

Core Idea
Intention alone can make trade goods personal, but not vice versa.

The Hanafi school holds that intention is powerful in determining the legal status of property, particularly regarding zakat. This lesson examines a key furu' of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha': the asymmetry between converting trade goods to personal use and personal property to trade.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its rank
Identify the major maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by their intentions) as a kubra (major) maxim governing many rulings.
This maxim is one of the five foundational maxims of Islamic law.
2
Identify the two cases from the furuat
Focus on the two opposite scenarios: intending trade goods for service, and intending personal property for trade.
The text presents both cases but only one is effective by mere intention.
3
Analyze why intention works in one direction but not the other
Understand the rationale: trade goods are defined by the initial intention to trade; a later intention to use personally suffices to exit the trade category. However, personal property needs an actual transaction to enter trade, because mere intention does not create market activity.
This asymmetry is grounded in the nature of trade requiring an offer or sale.
4
Connect to the broader principle of al-umur bi maqasidiha
Recognize that this ruling demonstrates how intention is a key determinant in legal categories, but its effect is limited by other considerations (e.g., need for a sale).
Intention alone is powerful but not omnipotent; it operates within the framework of the maxim's scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ نَوَى بِمَالِ التِّجَارَةِ الْخِدْمَةِ كَانَ لِلْخِدْمَةِ بِالنِّيَّةِ وَلَوْ كَانَ عَلَىٰ عَكْسِهِ لَمْ تُوكَّرْ كَمَا ذَكرَهُ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ: اور بہر حال اگر مال تجارت میں خدمت کی نیت کی تو نیت سے خدمت کے لئے ہو جائے گا اور اس کے برعکس ہو تو نیت مؤثر نہ ہو گی زیلعی نے اسی طرح ذکر کیا ہے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ مسئلہ میں لاحق کی ایک صورت کا بیان ہے جو پہلے مسئلہ سے مختلف ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مقتدی لائق مسافر ہو اور امام بھی مسافر ہو اور امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد وہ مسافر لاحق مقتدی اقامت کی نیت کرلے تو اقامت کی نیت کرنے کی وجہ سے وہ لاحق مسافر جو مقتدی ہے اتمام نہیں کرے گا کیونکہ امام کے فارغ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کا فرض مستحکم ہو گیا۔

And anyway, if he intends for trade goods to be for service, it becomes for service by intention, and if the opposite, the intention does not have effect, as al-Zayla'i mentioned.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of intention on property classification. According to the Hanafi school, if a person buys goods for trade (mal al-tijara) and later intends them for personal service (khidma), the mere intention changes their status: they become personal property, and the zakat obligation on trade goods ceases. However, the reverse is not true: if someone possesses personal property and intends to use it for trade, the intention alone does not make it trade goods; an actual sale or exchange is required. This is a furu' (application) of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha', showing that intention can transform legal status in one direction but not the other due to the nature of trade requiring market activity. The commentary that follows (about lahiq) seems to be a separate topic and is included in the previous lesson.

Key Terms
مال التجارة (mal al-tijara): Goods purchased with the intention of resale for profit, subject to zakat.
خدمة (khidma): Personal use or service, as opposed to trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The property remains trade goods until sold
B) The property becomes personal property by mere intention
C) The intention is ineffective; only physical use changes its status
D) Both parties must agree to the change

Key Takeaway
Intention alone can remove goods from the trade category, but cannot place personal goods into trade—an actual market action is required.

Intention in Trust: When Does Mental Betrayal Create Liability?
Passage on intention of betrayal in trust, citing a ruling from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to distinguish between cases where mere intention creates liability and where action is required, specifically in the chapter of wadi'a.

Core Idea
Mere intention to betray a trust does not create liability; only action does, except when prior transgression is coupled with persistent intent.

Does thinking about betraying a trust make you liable? The Hanafi school generally requires action, not mere thought. But what if you already acted and then stopped, but still intend to resume? This passage from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya refines the application of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' by showing that persistent intention can prevent the removal of liability when tied to a prior transgression.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
The passage asks whether mere intention of betrayal (niyyat al-khiyana) in a trust creates liability. Identify the unknown ruling from the author's statement.
The author says he did not find an explicit ruling on mere intention.
2
Examine the cited case from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya
The cited case: a depositary commits a transgression (ta'addi), then removes it, but intends to return. The ruling: the transgression does not cease. Understand the conditions: prior transgression, removal, and persistent intention.
This is from the chapter on crimes of ihram, but applied analogically to wadi'a.
3
Extract the relevant legal principle
The ruling shows that intention alone after a prior act prevents the removal of liability. Infer the broader principle: for liability in trusts, intention without action is insufficient, but intention alongside a prior action can maintain liability.
Refines the general principle that 'intention alone does not create liability'.
4
Apply the qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'
The maxim governs both furuat: (1) mere intention to betray → no liability (intention without action); (2) intention after transgression → liability persists (intention coupled with prior action). Note that the maxim is nuanced: intention matters only when manifested in action or linked to a prior transgression.
5
State the mufta bihi and hierarchy
The operative ruling: a depositary is not liable for mere intention to betray; action is required. The refinement from al-Zahiriyya (nawadir) confirms that once action occurs, persistent intention prevents the return to the original trusteeship.
This is consistent with the general Hanafi principle that an amin is not liable without ta'addi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ أَمَّا نِيَّةُ الْخِيَانَةِ فِي الْوَدِيْعَةِ، فَلَمْ أَرَهَا صريحةً، لكنْ فِي الْفَتَاوى الظَّهِيرِيَّةِ مِنْ جِنايَاتِ الإِحْرَامِ أَنَّ الْمُوْدَعَ إِذَا تَعَلَّى ثُمَّ أَزَالَ التَّعَدّى وَ مِنْ نِيَّتِهِ أَنْ يَعُودَ إِلَيْهِ لَا يَزُولُ التَّعَدّى إنتهى.:ترجمہ: البتہ ودیعت میں خیانت کی نیت کرلے تو اس کا حکم صراحی نہیں دیکھا لیکن فتاوی ظہیر یہ میں احرام کی جنایت کے باب میں ہے اگر مودع نے تعدی کی پھر تعدی زائل ہو گئی اور نیت یہی ہے کہ پھر خیانت کرے گا تو تعدی زائل نہ ہوگی مقاومی ظہیر یہ کا کلام پورا ہوا ۔
As for the intention of betrayal in a trust, I have not seen it explicitly, but in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya from the chapter on crimes of ihram: if the depositary transgressed, then removed the transgression, and his intention is to return to it, the transgression does not cease. End. Translation: However, if he intends betrayal in the trust, I have not seen its ruling explicitly, but in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya in the chapter on crimes of ihram: if the depositary transgressed, then removed the transgression, and his intention is to return to it, the transgression does not cease. The words of al-Zahiriyya are complete.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal effect of simply intending to betray a trust (wadi'a). The author states he did not find an explicit ruling on whether mere intention (niyya) without action constitutes betrayal (khiyana) that would make the depositary liable (daman). However, he cites al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, which provides a related case: if a depositary commits a transgression (ta'addi) by using the deposited item, then ceases the transgression, but still intends to return to it, the transgression is not considered removed and liability remains. This suggests that intention alone, when coupled with a prior act, prevents the removal of liability. The passage thus refines the application of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' by showing that intention in the context of trust requires more than mere thought; it typically requires an overt action to affect legal status.

Key Terms
وديعة (wadi'a): A trust or deposit; property left with someone for safekeeping.
نية الخيانة (niyyat al-khiyana): Intention to betray the trust by using or misappropriating the deposited property.
تعدي (ta'addi): Transgression; unauthorized use or handling of the deposit that violates the terms of trust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, intention alone does not create liability in a trust; however, a persistent intention after a prior transgression prevents the removal of liability, refining the application of 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'.

Intention of Betrayal in Trust: When Does It Impose Liability?
Refines the rule of intention in wadi'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that mere intention of betrayal in wadi'ah does not impose liability and distinguish cases where intention combined with an act creates liability.

Core Idea
In wadi'ah, intention alone is not enough; an overt act of transgression is required for liability.

The relationship between intention and liability in trust (wadi'ah) is subtle. While the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' teaches that acts are judged by intentions, this lesson refines that principle: in wadi'ah, a mere intention to betray, without any accompanying act, does not make the depositary liable. However, if the intention is coupled with an act of transgression (ta'addi), liability attaches even if the act temporarily ceases. This analysis from the Ashbah wa al-Nazair tradition helps the mufti navigate a common pitfall.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central question
The passage asks whether the mere intention (niyyah) of khianah (betrayal) in wadi'ah is effective in imposing liability (daman). Notice that no explicit ruling was initially found.
2
Analyze the cited case from al-Zahiriyyah
The case: a depositor wears a trust garment, then removes it with the intention to wear it again later. If the garment is stolen in the interim, the depositor is liable. This shows that intention with a prior act (wearing) creates a continuing effect.
The act (wearing) already occurred; the remaining intention sustains liability.
3
Distinguish intention with act from intention alone
The commentator clarifies that the effective element is the act of transgression itself. Mere intention without any act is not explicitly ruled upon, implying it does not impose liability.
4
Apply the refined qawida
Formulate the sub-maxim: 'In wadi'ah, intention alone is not effective; it must be accompanied by an act of transgression.' This refines the broader maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' for trust law.
5
Consider the mufti's application
When a questioner asks whether a depositary is liable if he merely thought about using the item but never did, the mufti should rule no liability. But if he used it even once, and later lost it, liability remains.

Source Text

And as for the intention of betrayal: Whether the intention of betrayal in a trust (wadi'ah) is effective or not, a clear ruling has not come into view. Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the rule regarding intention in wadi'ah. It discusses whether mere intention of khianah (betrayal) imposes liability. The author notes that no explicit ruling is found except in Fatawa Zahiriyya. The commentator analyzes a ruling from the first qa'ida: if a depositor wears the trust garment and then takes it off intending to wear again, he is not free from liability if it is lost. This indicates that intention combined with an act (wearing) makes intention effective. But if there is no act, mere intention may not impose liability. The passage clarifies that the effective element is the act of transgression, not just the intention. However, if intention remains after the act ceases, it can still affect liability. This lesson demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of distinguishing between intention alone and intention with action, refining the application of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' in trust law.

Key Terms
ودیعت (wadī'at): A trust deposit where the depositor gives an item to another for safekeeping without compensation.
خیانت (khiyānat): Breach of trust, betrayal, using or intending to use the entrusted item without permission.
تعدی (ta'addī): Transgression, exceeding the bounds of permission; an act that breaches the trust.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) As soon as the intention is formed in the heart
B) Only when the intention is expressed verbally
C) When the intention is accompanied by an overt act of transgression
D) When the owner of the item knows about the intention

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, mere intention to betray a trust does not impose liability; an overt act of transgression is required for liability to attach.
