Transferring Intention in Prayer (Niyyat al-Qalb)
Ruling on niyyat al-qalb (intention transfer) in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on niyyat al-qalb to determine the validity of prayer transfer, and identify the condition of commencing the second prayer with takbir.

Core Idea
Transferring intention in prayer requires beginning the second prayer; mere intention is insufficient.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary on Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents a specific ruling (far') on intention (niyyah) in prayer. It clarifies the distinction between simply abandoning a prayer (niyyat al-qat') and transferring to another prayer (niyyat al-qalb). Understanding this distinction is crucial for muftis and students to correctly advise on situations where a worshipper changes their mind during prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is transferring intention from one obligatory prayer to another (niyyat al-qalb). The Hanafi ruling is that this transfer is valid only when the second prayer is commenced with takbirat al-ihram.
This distinguishes it from mere termination.
2
List the conditions for valid transfer
Three conditions: (1) The second prayer must be different from the first (e.g., from Zuhr to 'Asr). (2) The transfer must be effected by commencing the second prayer with takbir. (3) The intention must not be verbalized.
If verbalized, the first prayer is invalidated absolutely, even without commencing the second.
3
Distinguish transfer from termination
Niyyat al-qat' (intention to cut off) ends the prayer without transferring to another. Niyyat al-qalb (transfer) requires both termination of the first and commencement of the second.
The text says they are 'close' but distinct.
4
Apply to examples
If after starting Zuhr one intends 'Asr and says takbir, Zuhr is invalidated. If after two rak'ahs of Zuhr one intends Zuhr again, the first Zuhr is not invalidated because the second prayer is not different.
The second must be a different prayer.
5
Note the effect of verbalization
If one verbally expresses the intention to change, the first prayer becomes void immediately, because speaking during prayer deliberately nullifies it.
This is a separate rule from the transfer itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَرْعٌ وَتَقْرُبُ مِنْ نِيَّةِ الْقَطْعِ نِيَّةُ الْقَلْبِ ، وَهِيَ نِيَّةُ نَقْلُ الصَّلَاةِ إِلَى أَخْرَى قَدَّمْنَا اللَّهُ لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا بِالشُّرُوْعِ بِالتَّحْرِيْمَةِ، لَا بِمُجَرَّدِ النّيَةِ، وَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ تَكُوْنَ الثَّانِيَةُ غَيْرَ الأَوْلَى كَانْ يُشْرَعَ فِي الْعَصْرِ بَعْدَ إِفْتِتَاحِ الظَّهْرِ ، فَيَفْسُدُ الظُّهْرَ، لَا الظَّهْرُ بَعْدَ رَكْعَتَي الظهر وَ شَرْطُهُ أَنْ لَّا يَتَلَفَّظَ بِالنِّيَّةِ ، فَإِنْ تَلَفْظَ بِهَا بَطَلَتِ الأوْلَى مُطْلَقاً، وَقَدْ ذَكَرْنَا تَفَارِيْعَهَا فِي مُفْسِدَاتِ الصَّلَاةِ مِنْ شَرْحِ الْكَنْزِ"۔ ترجمه: فرع او توڑنے کی نیت سے قریب قریب ہی نماز کو بدلنے کی نیت ہے اور وہ ایک نماز سے دوسری نماز کی طرف جانا ہے ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ ایسا تحریمہ کے ساتھ مشروع کرنے سے ہی ہو گا محض نیست سے ہوا اور یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ (انتقال) میں دوسری نماز پہلی نماز کی غیر ہو مثلا ظہر شروع کرنے کے بعد عصر کی طرف تھا۔ ہوا تو ظہر باطل ہو جائے گی ظہر کی دورکعت کے بعد ظہر ہی شروع کی تو ظہر باطل نہ ہوگی اور انقال کی شرط یہ ہے کہنا کو زبان سے نہ کہے اگر نیت زبان سے کی تو پہلی نماز ابطل ہو جائے گی اور ہم نے اس کی فروعات کو شرح کنز کی بابت مفسدات الصلوۃ میں بیان کیا ہے۔ تشریح نیست قطع یہ ہے کہ کسی نیست کو صرف ختم کر دیا جائے اور نیت قلب یہ ہے کہ ایک کوختم کر کے ہرے کی طرف انتقال بھی ہو ۔ ایک نماز سے دوسری نماز کی طرف منتقل ہونے کی بعض تفصیلات اس سے پہلے بھی گذر چکی ہیں اس جگہ یہ انت یا در کھنے کی ہے کہ جس نماز کی طرف منتقل ہوا جارہا ہے وہ نماز پہلی نماز سے الگ ہو مثلا ظہر سے عصر کی طرف منقل ہوا ہوا ایسا نہ ہو کہ وہ ظہر کی دورکعتوں کے بعد پھر ظہر کی نیت کرلے۔ نیز نیت کے تبدیل کرنے کی شرائط میں سے ایک شرط یہ بھی ہے کہ آدمی نیت کو زبان سے نہ بولے ورنہ پھر کی الناس کے مشابہ ہونے کی وجہ سے پہلی نماز مطلقاً باطل ہو جائے گی۔ ان هذا إذام لم يتلفظ بلسانه فان قال نوبت ان اصلى إلى آخره فسدت الأولى وصار مستانفاً للمونى ثانياً مطلقاً لان الكلام مفسد ( بحرج ۲،ص:۱۰)
A branch: Close to the intention of cutting off is the intention of the heart (niyyat al-qalb), which is the intention of transferring the prayer to another. We have previously mentioned that it is only by commencing with the takbirat al-ihram, not by mere intention. It is necessary that the second prayer be different from the first, such as starting the 'Asr after beginning Zuhr, then Zuhr is invalidated; but if it is Zuhr after two rak'ahs of Zuhr, it is not invalidated. Its condition is that he does not utter the intention verbally; if he does utter it, the first prayer is invalidated absolutely. And we have mentioned its details in the nullifiers of prayer from Sharh al-Kanz.
Translation: The branch: Close to the intention of breaking off is the intention of changing the prayer, which is to go from one prayer to another. We have already mentioned that this only occurs by commencing with the takbir, not by mere intention. It is also necessary that the second prayer be different from the first, e.g., after starting Zuhr, if he turns to 'Asr, then Zuhr is invalidated; if he starts Zuhr again after two rak'ahs of Zuhr, Zuhr is not invalidated. The condition of transfer is that he does not utter the intention with his tongue; if he utters it, the first prayer becomes void absolutely. We have explained its details in the nullifiers of prayer from Sharh al-Kanz.
Explanation: Niyyat al-qat' is to merely terminate an intention, and niyyat al-qalb is to terminate one and transfer to another. Some details of transferring from one prayer to another have already passed. Here the point is that the prayer to which he transfers must be separate from the first, e.g., transferring from Zuhr to 'Asr; it should not be that after two rak'ahs of Zuhr he intends Zuhr again. Also, one of the conditions of changing intention is that a person should not verbalize the intention; otherwise, due to resemblance to the speech of people, the first prayer becomes absolutely void. If he does not utter it with his tongue, and he says 'I intend to pray...' to the end, the first is invalidated and he becomes a beginner of the second prayer absolutely, because speech nullifies prayer.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (far') about a specific aspect of intention in prayer: the transfer of intention from one obligatory prayer to another (niyyat al-qalb). The author explains that this transfer is similar to completely abandoning intention (niyyat al-qat'), but with a key difference: transfer requires actually beginning the second prayer with takbir, not merely intending to change. The second prayer must be a different prayer (e.g., from Zuhr to 'Asr). If one intends to change after two rak'ahs of Zuhr but remains in Zuhr, the first prayer is not invalidated. Additionally, verbalizing the intention invalidates the first prayer absolutely, because speaking during prayer deliberately nullifies it. The author references more details in his commentary on the nullifiers of prayer from Sharh al-Kanz. This ruling illustrates the precision Hanafi fiqh demands in matters of niyyah, ensuring that the integrity of the prayer is maintained.

Key Terms
نِيَّةُ الْقَطْعِ (niyyat al-qat'): Intention to completely terminate the prayer without transferring to another
نِيَّةُ الْقَلْبِ (niyyat al-qalb): Intention to transfer from one prayer to another, requiring commencement of the new prayer
تَحْرِيْمَة (tahrimah): The takbirat al-ihram that initiates the prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi madhhab, when does the intention to transfer from Zuhr to 'Asr invalidate the Zuhr prayer?
A) As soon as the person decides to change
B) When he begins the 'Asr prayer with takbir
C) When he finishes the second rak'ah of Zuhr
D) When he verbally states the intention

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, transferring intention from one prayer to another (niyyat al-qalb) only takes effect when the second prayer is commenced with takbir; mere intention or verbalization does not suffice.

Hesitation in Intention: The Maxim and Its Application to Zakah on a Servant
Rulings on hesitation and lack of resolve in intention — the maxim and a zakat furu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'التَّرَدُّدُ فِي النِّيَّةِ مُنَافٍ لِلنِّيَّةِ' to determine that a servant bought for service with a hesitant intention to sell does not incur zakah.

Core Idea
If your original intention for an asset is not trade, hesitation to sell does not turn it into trade property.

This lesson unpacks a foundational Hanafi dabt (sub-maxim) regarding intention. The text from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents the ruling that hesitation (taraddud) contradicts intention (niyyah). Through the case of a servant bought for service, we see how conditional intention on the essence invalidates the intention, while conditional intention on the description does not. Understanding this distinction is crucial for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Maxim
Identify the Arabic text of the maxim and its plain meaning: hesitation in intention is contradictory to intention.
The maxim is a dabt (sub-maxim) under the broader qa'ida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
2
Distinguish Essence vs. Description
Grasp the key difference: hesitation in the asl (essence) means you are unsure whether to perform the act at all; hesitation in the wasf (description) means you are sure about the act but unsure about its category (e.g., nafil or fard).
Only hesitation in the essence invalidates intention.
3
Apply to the Servant Case
Work through the scenario: a man buys a servant for service but intends to sell if profit appears. The original intention is service, not trade.
The intention to sell conditionally is hesitation in description (whether to sell or not), not essence.
4
Derive the Zakah Ruling
Since the original intention is service, the servant is not a trade asset. The hesitant intention to sell does not change that, so no zakah is due.
This ruling is from Imam Muhammad as reported in al-Multaqat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَضْلٌ: وَمِنَ الْمُنَافِى التردد و عَدَمُ الْجَزْمِ فِي أصْلِهَا وَ فِي الْمُلْتَقَطِ": وَعَن محمد فِيْمَنْ إِشْتَرَىٰ خَادِمًا لِلْخِدْمَةِ، وَهُوَ يَنْوِى إِنْ أَصَابَ رِبْحاً بَاعَهُ لَا زَكَاةَ عَلَيْهِ.
ترجمه: فصل: اور اصل نیست میں تردد و عدم پختگی بھی (نیت کے منافی ہے اور ملفظ میں امام محمد سے منقول ہے اس شخص کے بارے میں جس نے خدمت کے لئے کوئی خادم خریدا اور وہ یہ نیت کرتا ہے کہ اگر اسے کوئی نفع لا تو وہ اسے فروخت کر دے گا تو اس پر زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: نیت کے معتبر ہونے کے لئے یہ ضروری ہے کہ جس طرح نیت اور منوی کے درمیان کوئی امر منافی جو اعراض عن النیہ پر دال ہو نہ پایا جائے اسی طرح اصل نیت میں اگر تر در ہو تو وہ نیت بھی غیر معتبر ہوگی بلکہ نیت کے اندر جزم و استحکام مطلوب ہے۔
گر کسی نے غلام خدمت کی نیت سے خریدا تھا اور نیت یہ کی کہ اگر نفع ہوا تو فروخت کر دوں گا تو اس پر زکوۃ نہیں کیونکہ اصل نیت خدمت کی ہے اور اگر فروخت کرنے کی پختہ نیت کر لی تب بھی تجارت کے لئے نہ ہوگا جب تک کہ عمل تجارت کا حق نہ ہو جیسا کہ اس کی تفضیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہے۔
قبال هشام سالت محمداً عن رجل اشترى جارية للخدمة و هو ينوى انه ان اصاب ربحا باعها فحال عليها الحول قال ليس فيها الزكوة ( تار تار خانیه ج ۲ ص ۲۴۱)
وَقَالُوا : لَوْ نَوَى يَوْمَ الشَّكْ أَنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ مِنْ شَعْبَانَ، فَلَيْسَ بِصَائِمٍ وَ إِنْ كَانَ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ كَانَ صَائِماً لَمْ تَصِحْ نِيَّتُهُ، وَلَوْ رَدَّدَ فِي الْوَصْفِ بأنْ نَّوى إِنْ كَانَ الْغَدُ مِنْ شَعْبَانَ فَنَفْلٌ وَإِلَّا فَعَنْ رَمَضَانَ صَحَتْ نِيَّتُهُ كَمَا بَيَّنَّاهُ فِي الصَّوْمِ. وَيَنْبَغِي عَلَىٰ هَذَا أَنَّهُ لَوْ كَانَتْ عَلَيْهِ فَائِنَةٌ، فَشَكَ أَنَّهُ قَضَا هَا أَوْلَا، فَقَضَاهَا ثُمَّ تَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهَا كَانَتْ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ لَّا تُجْزِيْهِ لِلشَّكَ وَ عَدَمِ الْجَزْمِ بِتَعْيِيْنِهَا. ترجمہ: اور فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر یوم اشک میں یہ نیت کی کہ اگر شعبان ہو تو و دوروزے سے نہیں اور اگر رمضان ہو تو وہ روزے سے ہے تو اس کی نیت صحیح نہیں اور اگر وصف میں تر در ہو بایں طور کہ وہ یہ نیت کرے کہ اگر کل شعبان ہو تو نفل روزہ ہے رو نہ تو رمضان کا روزہ ہے تو اس کی نیت صحیح ہے جیسا کہ کتاب الصوم میں ہم نے بیان کیا ہے اور اس پر محمول کرتے ہوئے ضروری ہے کہ اگر اس کے ذمہ چھٹی ہوئی نماز ہو اور اسے شک ہوا کہ اس نے وہ قضا کر لی یا نہیں پس اس نے وہ قضا کی پھر واضح ہوا کہ وہ اس کے ذمہ تھی تو وہ اس کے لئے کافی نہیں اس لئے کر تعیین نیت میں شک ہے جزم و پختگی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح کسی نے یوم الشک میں اس نیت سے روزہ رکھا کہ اگر آج شعبان ہی ہے تو وہ روزہ دار نہیں اور اگر رمضان ہے تو میں روزہ سے ہوں تو اس کی نیت صحیح نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اسے روزہ کے ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں تردد ہے۔ والمراد ان لا يرددفى النية بين كونه نفلا ان كان من شعبان و فرضاً ان كان من رمضان بل يجزم بنيته نفلا محضاً (شامی ج ۳ ص ۳۴۹)
Fasl: Among the contradictory [to intention] is hesitation and lack of resolve in the essence of the intention. And in al-Multaqat: From Muhammad regarding a person who bought a servant for service, while he intends that if he obtains profit he will sell it: no zakah is due on him.
Translation: Fasl: Hesitation and lack of firmness in the original intention is also contrary to intention. And in al-Multaqat it is narrated from Imam Muhammad about a person who bought a servant for service, and he intends that if he gets some profit, he will sell it. So no zakah is due on him.
Explanation: For the validity of intention, it is necessary that there be no contradictory matter indicating turning away from the intention, and similarly if there is hesitation in the original intention, that intention is invalid; rather, resolve and firmness are required in intention. If someone bought a slave for service with the intention that if profit comes, I will sell it, then no zakah is due because the original intention is service. Even if he firmly intends to sell, it does not become for trade until the action of trade actually occurs, as detailed previously.
[Hadith?] Qabal Hisham asked Muhammad about a man who bought a female servant for service and he intends that if he obtains profit, he will sell her; then a year passed. He said: No zakah is due on her. (Tatar Khaniya vol. 2 p. 241)
And they said: If on the day of doubt he intends: 'If it is from Sha'ban, then I am not fasting; and if it is from Ramadan, then I am fasting' — his intention is not valid. But if he hesitates in the description such that he intends: 'If tomorrow is from Sha'ban, then it is nafil; otherwise it is for Ramadan' — his intention is valid, as we explained in the book of fasting. And based on this, it should be that if there is a missed prayer upon him, and he doubts whether he has made it up or not, then he makes it up and then it becomes clear that it was still due upon him — it does not suffice him because of the doubt and lack of resolve in specifying it. Translation: And the jurists say: If on the day of doubt he intends: 'If it is Sha'ban, then I am not fasting; and if it is Ramadan, then I am fasting' — his intention is not valid. And if he hesitates in the description such that he intends: 'If tomorrow is from Sha'ban, then it is nafil; otherwise it is Ramadan's fast' — his intention is valid, as we explained in the book of fasting. And based on this, it is necessary that if there is a missed prayer upon him, and he doubts whether he has made it up or not, then he makes it up and then it becomes clear that it was upon him — it does not suffice because of the doubt and lack of resolve in specifying it. Explanation: If someone on the day of doubt fasts with the intention: 'If today is Sha'ban, then I am not fasting; and if it is Ramadan, then I am fasting' — his intention is not valid because he is in doubt about whether he is fasting or not. The intent is that he should not hesitate in the intention between it being nafil if from Sha'ban and fard if from Ramadan; rather, he should resolve his intention as purely nafil. (Shami vol. 3 p. 349)
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage (fasl) is a legal maxim with its applications: hesitation (taraddud) and lack of resolution (adam al-jazm) in the original intention invalidate the intention. The author provides three key furu': (1) Buying a servant for service with a conditional intention to sell if profit arises — no zakah is due on the servant because the original intention is for service, not trade. (2) Fasting on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk: 30th Shaban) — if one intends conditionally ('if it is Shaban, I am not fasting; if Ramadan, I am fasting'), the intention is invalid due to hesitation in the essence. However, if one intends conditionally on the description (nafil if Shaban, fard if Ramadan), the intention is valid because the resolve is firm: the fast is intended as either nafil or fard, but the person is definitely fasting. (3) Making up a missed prayer with doubt about whether it was already made up — the makeup is not valid because of lack of resolve in specifying which prayer is being made up. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that intention must be decisive; hesitation contradicts the very nature of niyyah.

Key Terms
التَّرَدُّدُ (al-taraddud): Hesitation or being in doubt regarding the intention, contradicting the required resolve
الْجَزْمُ (al-jazm): Resolve, firmness, certainty in intention
يَوْمُ الشَّكْ (yawm al-shakk): The 30th of Sha'ban when it is uncertain whether it is the last day of Sha'ban or the first of Ramadan

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the maxim in this lesson, what is the ruling on a servant bought for service with an intention to sell if profit appears?
A) Zakah is due because the intention to sell makes it trade property.
B) No zakah because the original intention is service.
C) Zakah is due only if the profit is realized.
D) No zakah because the servant is not zakahable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the original intention determines the legal status of an asset; conditional hesitation about selling does not transform it into trade property for zakah.

Hesitation in Intention: Application to Fasting on the Day of Doubt and Making Up Missed Prayers
Application of the maxim to fasting on the day of doubt and making up missed prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hesitation in the essence (asl) and hesitation in the description (wasf) and apply this distinction to determine the validity of fasting on yawm al-shakk and making up missed prayers.

Core Idea
Hesitation about whether you are performing the act at all invalidates the intention; hesitation about its specific ruling (nafil/fard) does not.

This lesson extends the same maxim to two practical furu': fasting on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk) and making up missed prayers with uncertainty. The text shows that a conditional intention that questions the very act of fasting is invalid, but one that only questions the category (nafil vs. fard) is valid. Similarly, making up a missed prayer with doubt about its obligation is not accepted because the intention lacks resolve in specifying the missed prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Cases
Note the two scenarios: (1) fasting on yawm al-shakk with a conditional intention; (2) making up a missed prayer with doubt about whether it was already made up.
Both cases involve hesitation in the intention.
2
Analyze the Intention in the First Case
Case 1: 'If it is Shaban, I am not fasting; if it is Ramadan, I am fasting.' This is hesitation in the essence: the person is unsure whether to fast at all. Hence the intention is invalid.
The person is not resolved to fast unconditionally.
3
Analyze the Intention in the Second Case
Case 2: 'If it is Shaban, then nafil; if it is Ramadan, then fard.' Here, the person is resolved to fast; the doubt is only about the description (nafil or fard). Therefore the intention is valid.
The firmness on the act of fasting is present.
4
Apply to the Missed Prayer
Case 3: A person has a missed prayer and doubts whether he already made it up. He then prays it again. If it becomes clear that it was still due, the makeup does not count because the intention lacked resolve in specifying which prayer was being made up.
The doubt about the obligation itself invalidates the intention.
5
Derive the General Rule
Hesitation in the essence (whether to perform the act) invalidates; hesitation in the description (type of act) does not.
This aligns with the maxim and its istithna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَضْلٌ: وَمِنَ الْمُنَافِى التردد و عَدَمُ الْجَزْمِ فِي أصْلِهَا وَ فِي الْمُلْتَقَطِ": وَعَن محمد فِيْمَنْ إِشْتَرَىٰ خَادِمًا لِلْخِدْمَةِ، وَهُوَ يَنْوِى إِنْ أَصَابَ رِبْحاً بَاعَهُ لَا زَكَاةَ عَلَيْهِ.
ترجمه: فصل: اور اصل نیست میں تردد و عدم پختگی بھی (نیت کے منافی ہے اور ملفظ میں امام محمد سے منقول ہے اس شخص کے بارے میں جس نے خدمت کے لئے کوئی خادم خریدا اور وہ یہ نیت کرتا ہے کہ اگر اسے کوئی نفع لا تو وہ اسے فروخت کر دے گا تو اس پر زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: نیت کے معتبر ہونے کے لئے یہ ضروری ہے کہ جس طرح نیت اور منوی کے درمیان کوئی امر منافی جو اعراض عن النیہ پر دال ہو نہ پایا جائے اسی طرح اصل نیت میں اگر تر در ہو تو وہ نیت بھی غیر معتبر ہوگی بلکہ نیت کے اندر جزم و استحکام مطلوب ہے۔
گر کسی نے غلام خدمت کی نیت سے خریدا تھا اور نیت یہ کی کہ اگر نفع ہوا تو فروخت کر دوں گا تو اس پر زکوۃ نہیں کیونکہ اصل نیت خدمت کی ہے اور اگر فروخت کرنے کی پختہ نیت کر لی تب بھی تجارت کے لئے نہ ہوگا جب تک کہ عمل تجارت کا حق نہ ہو جیسا کہ اس کی تفضیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہے۔
قبال هشام سالت محمداً عن رجل اشترى جارية للخدمة و هو ينوى انه ان اصاب ربحا باعها فحال عليها الحول قال ليس فيها الزكوة ( تار تار خانیه ج ۲ ص ۲۴۱)
وَقَالُوا : لَوْ نَوَى يَوْمَ الشَّكْ أَنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ مِنْ شَعْبَانَ، فَلَيْسَ بِصَائِمٍ وَ إِنْ كَانَ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ كَانَ صَائِماً لَمْ تَصِحْ نِيَّتُهُ، وَلَوْ رَدَّدَ فِي الْوَصْفِ بأنْ نَّوى إِنْ كَانَ الْغَدُ مِنْ شَعْبَانَ فَنَفْلٌ وَإِلَّا فَعَنْ رَمَضَانَ صَحَتْ نِيَّتُهُ كَمَا بَيَّنَّاهُ فِي الصَّوْمِ. وَيَنْبَغِي عَلَىٰ هَذَا أَنَّهُ لَوْ كَانَتْ عَلَيْهِ فَائِنَةٌ، فَشَكَ أَنَّهُ قَضَا هَا أَوْلَا، فَقَضَاهَا ثُمَّ تَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهَا كَانَتْ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ لَّا تُجْزِيْهِ لِلشَّكَ وَ عَدَمِ الْجَزْمِ بِتَعْيِيْنِهَا. ترجمہ: اور فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر یوم اشک میں یہ نیت کی کہ اگر شعبان ہو تو و دوروزے سے نہیں اور اگر رمضان ہو تو وہ روزے سے ہے تو اس کی نیت صحیح نہیں اور اگر وصف میں تر در ہو بایں طور کہ وہ یہ نیت کرے کہ اگر کل شعبان ہو تو نفل روزہ ہے رو نہ تو رمضان کا روزہ ہے تو اس کی نیت صحیح ہے جیسا کہ کتاب الصوم میں ہم نے بیان کیا ہے اور اس پر محمول کرتے ہوئے ضروری ہے کہ اگر اس کے ذمہ چھٹی ہوئی نماز ہو اور اسے شک ہوا کہ اس نے وہ قضا کر لی یا نہیں پس اس نے وہ قضا کی پھر واضح ہوا کہ وہ اس کے ذمہ تھی تو وہ اس کے لئے کافی نہیں اس لئے کر تعیین نیت میں شک ہے جزم و پختگی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح کسی نے یوم الشک میں اس نیت سے روزہ رکھا کہ اگر آج شعبان ہی ہے تو وہ روزہ دار نہیں اور اگر رمضان ہے تو میں روزہ سے ہوں تو اس کی نیت صحیح نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اسے روزہ کے ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں تردد ہے۔ والمراد ان لا يرددفى النية بين كونه نفلا ان كان من شعبان و فرضاً ان كان من رمضان بل يجزم بنيته نفلا محضاً (شامی ج ۳ ص ۳۴۹)
Fasl: Among the contradictory [to intention] is hesitation and lack of resolve in the essence of the intention. And in al-Multaqat: From Muhammad regarding a person who bought a servant for service, while he intends that if he obtains profit he will sell it: no zakah is due on him.
Translation: Fasl: Hesitation and lack of firmness in the original intention is also contrary to intention. And in al-Multaqat it is narrated from Imam Muhammad about a person who bought a servant for service, and he intends that if he gets some profit, he will sell it. So no zakah is due on him.
Explanation: For the validity of intention, it is necessary that there be no contradictory matter indicating turning away from the intention, and similarly if there is hesitation in the original intention, that intention is invalid; rather, resolve and firmness are required in intention. If someone bought a slave for service with the intention that if profit comes, I will sell it, then no zakah is due because the original intention is service. Even if he firmly intends to sell, it does not become for trade until the action of trade actually occurs, as detailed previously.
[Hadith?] Qabal Hisham asked Muhammad about a man who bought a female servant for service and he intends that if he obtains profit, he will sell her; then a year passed. He said: No zakah is due on her. (Tatar Khaniya vol. 2 p. 241)
And they said: If on the day of doubt he intends: 'If it is from Sha'ban, then I am not fasting; and if it is from Ramadan, then I am fasting' — his intention is not valid. But if he hesitates in the description such that he intends: 'If tomorrow is from Sha'ban, then it is nafil; otherwise it is for Ramadan' — his intention is valid, as we explained in the book of fasting. And based on this, it should be that if there is a missed prayer upon him, and he doubts whether he has made it up or not, then he makes it up and then it becomes clear that it was still due upon him — it does not suffice him because of the doubt and lack of resolve in specifying it. Translation: And the jurists say: If on the day of doubt he intends: 'If it is Sha'ban, then I am not fasting; and if it is Ramadan, then I am fasting' — his intention is not valid. And if he hesitates in the description such that he intends: 'If tomorrow is from Sha'ban, then it is nafil; otherwise it is Ramadan's fast' — his intention is valid, as we explained in the book of fasting. And based on this, it is necessary that if there is a missed prayer upon him, and he doubts whether he has made it up or not, then he makes it up and then it becomes clear that it was upon him — it does not suffice because of the doubt and lack of resolve in specifying it. Explanation: If someone on the day of doubt fasts with the intention: 'If today is Sha'ban, then I am not fasting; and if it is Ramadan, then I am fasting' — his intention is not valid because he is in doubt about whether he is fasting or not. The intent is that he should not hesitate in the intention between it being nafil if from Sha'ban and fard if from Ramadan; rather, he should resolve his intention as purely nafil. (Shami vol. 3 p. 349)
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage (fasl) is a legal maxim with its applications: hesitation (taraddud) and lack of resolution (adam al-jazm) in the original intention invalidate the intention. The author provides three key furu': (1) Buying a servant for service with a conditional intention to sell if profit arises — no zakah is due on the servant because the original intention is for service, not trade. (2) Fasting on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk: 30th Shaban) — if one intends conditionally ('if it is Shaban, I am not fasting; if Ramadan, I am fasting'), the intention is invalid due to hesitation in the essence. However, if one intends conditionally on the description (nafil if Shaban, fard if Ramadan), the intention is valid because the resolve is firm: the fast is intended as either nafil or fard, but the person is definitely fasting. (3) Making up a missed prayer with doubt about whether it was already made up — the makeup is not valid because of lack of resolve in specifying which prayer is being made up. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that intention must be decisive; hesitation contradicts the very nature of niyyah.

Key Terms
التَّرَدُّدُ (al-taraddud): Hesitation or being in doubt regarding the intention, contradicting the required resolve
الْجَزْمُ (al-jazm): Resolve, firmness, certainty in intention
يَوْمُ الشَّكْ (yawm al-shakk): The 30th of Sha'ban when it is uncertain whether it is the last day of Sha'ban or the first of Ramadan

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following intentions for fasting on yawm al-shakk is valid according to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) 'If it is Sha'ban, I am not fasting; if Ramadan, I am fasting.'
B) 'If it is Sha'ban, I intend nafil; if Ramadan, I intend fard.'
C) Both A and B are valid.
D) Neither A nor B is valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, hesitation in the essence of an intention invalidates the act, but hesitation in its description (nafil/fard) does not, as illustrated by fasting on the day of doubt.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
12 min
The Maxim of Certain Intention (Jazm) and Its Applications
Explaining the principle that intention must be certain and its applications in various acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim of certain intention (al-niyyah al-jazima) to concrete cases in zakah, fasting, and prayer, distinguishing between invalid indecisiveness on the essence and valid indecisiveness on the legal description.

Core Idea
Intention must be certain; doubt about the essence invalidates, but doubt about the description does not.

This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi usul principle through practical examples. You will see how the requirement of certain intention (jazm) works across different acts of worship, and how later jurists extended the same logic to prayer and missed obligations. Understanding this maxim will sharpen your ability to evaluate the validity of intentions in complex scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the Maxim
Articulate the Hanafi qawida: 'Certain and decisive intention (al-niyyah al-jazima) is a condition for the validity of worship.' This means that for an act of worship to be valid, the intention must be firm and free from doubt about the essential nature of the act.
The maxim is sughra (minor) and applies universally to ibadat.
2
Understand the Dabt (Restriction)
The sub-rule (dabt) states: 'If there is indecisiveness in the essence of the act, the intention is invalid; if indecisiveness is only in the description (wasf), the intention is valid.' This distinction is crucial for applying the maxim correctly.
The essence (asl) is the act itself (e.g., fasting). The description (wasf) is its legal category (e.g., obligatory vs. supererogatory).
3
Work Through the Furuat
Examine each case presented: (1) Buying a slave for service with conditional intent to sell – no zakat. (2) Fasting on yawm al-shakk with condition on essence – invalid. (3) Fasting on yawm al-shakk with condition on description – valid. (4) Performing a missed prayer with doubt about whether it was already made up – does not suffice. (5) Joining a congregation with conditional intention – valid if condition is on description.
For each case, identify whether the doubt concerns the essence or the description.
4
Identify the Istithna' (Exception)
The exception to the general rule is when the condition is about the description only. In that case, the intention remains valid because the act itself is certain. This is governed by the broader maxim 'Certainty is not overridden by doubt' (al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk).
The exception does not violate the maxim; it refines its application.
5
Apply the Maxim to a New Case
Given a new scenario (e.g., someone intends to give zakat but conditionally: 'If my income exceeds the nisab, this is zakat; otherwise it is sadaqah'), determine validity using the maxim. Here, the doubt is about the obligation (description), not the act of giving, so the intention is valid.
Always ask: Is the doubt about the essence of the act or its legal classification?

منقول ہے اس شخص کے بارے میں جس نے خدمت کے لئے کوئی خادم خریدا اور وہ یہ نیت کرتا ہے کہ اگر اسے کوئی نفع لا تو وہ اسے فروخت کر دے گا تو اس پر زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: نیت کے معتبر ہونے کے لئے یہ ضروری ہے کہ جس طرح نیت اور منوی کے درمیان کوئی امر منافی جو اعراض عن النیہ پر دال ہو نہ پایا جائے اسی طرح اصل نیت میں اگر تر در ہو تو وہ نیت بھی غیر معتبر ہوگی بلکہ نیت کے اندر جزم و استحکام مطلوب ہے۔

گر کسی نے غلام خدمت کی نیت سے خریدا تھا اور نیت یہ کی کہ اگر نفع ہوا تو فروخت کر دوں گا تو اس پر زکوۃ نہیں کیونکہ اصل نیت خدمت کی ہے اور اگر فروخت کرنے کی پختہ نیت کر لی تب بھی تجارت کے لئے نہ ہوگا جب تک کہ عمل تجارت کا حق نہ ہو جیسا کہ اس کی تفضیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہے۔

قَالَ هِشَامٌ: سَأَلْتُ مُحَمَّداً عَنْ رَجُلٍ اشْتَرَى جَارِيَةً لِلْخِدْمَةِ وَ هُوَ يَنْوِي أَنَّهُ إِنْ أَصَابَ رِبْحاً بَاعَهَا فَحَالَ عَلَيْهَا الْحَوْلُ قَالَ لَيْسَ فِيهَا الزَّكَاةُ ( تار تار خانیه ج ۲ ص ۲۴۱)

وَقَالُوا : لَوْ نَوَى يَوْمَ الشَّكِّ أَنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ مِنْ شَعْبَانَ، فَلَيْسَ بِصَائِمٍ وَ إِنْ كَانَ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ كَانَ صَائِماً لَمْ تَصِحَّ نِيَّتُهُ، وَلَوْ رَدَّدَ فِي الْوَصْفِ بِأَنْ نَّوَى إِنْ كَانَ الْغَدُ مِنْ شَعْبَانَ فَنَفْلٌ وَإِلَّا فَعَنْ رَمَضَانَ صَحَتْ نِيَّتُهُ كَمَا بَيَّنَّاهُ فِي الصَّوْمِ. وَيَنْبَغِي عَلَىٰ هَذَا أَنَّهُ لَوْ كَانَتْ عَلَيْهِ فَائِنَةٌ، فَشَكَّ أَنَّهُ قَضَا هَا أَوْلَا، فَقَضَاهَا ثُمَّ تَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهَا كَانَتْ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ لَّا تُجْزِيْهِ لِلشَّكَ وَ عَدَمِ الْجَزْمِ بِتَعْيِيْنِهَا. 
ترجمہ: اور فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر یوم اشک میں یہ نیت کی کہ اگر شعبان ہو تو وہ روزے سے نہیں اور اگر رمضان ہو تو وہ روزے سے ہے تو اس کی نیت صحیح نہیں اور اگر وصف میں تردد ہو بایں طور کہ وہ یہ نیت کرے کہ اگر کل شعبان ہو تو نفل روزہ ہے ورنہ تو رمضان کا روزہ ہے تو اس کی نیت صحیح ہے جیسا کہ کتاب الصوم میں ہم نے بیان کیا ہے اور اس پر محمول کرتے ہوئے ضروری ہے کہ اگر اس کے ذمہ چھٹی ہوئی نماز ہو اور اسے شک ہوا کہ اس نے وہ قضا کر لی یا نہیں پس اس نے وہ قضا کی پھر واضح ہوا کہ وہ اس کے ذمہ تھی تو وہ اس کے لئے کافی نہیں اس لئے کہ تعیین نیت میں شک ہے جزم و پختگی نہیں ہے۔ 
تشریح: کسی نے یوم الشک میں اس نیت سے روزہ رکھا کہ اگر آج شعبان ہی ہے تو وہ روزہ دار نہیں اور اگر رمضان ہے تو میں روزہ سے ہوں تو اس کی نیت صحیح نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اسے روزہ کے ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں تردد ہے۔ وَلَوْ رَدَّدَ فِي الْوَصْفِ: لیکن اگر کسی نے یوم الشک میں اس نیت سے روزہ رکھا کہ اگر شعبان کا ہے تو نفل ہے ورنہ رمضان کا ہے تو اس کی نیت صحیح ہوگی کیونکہ اسے محض وصف میں تردد ہے نہ کہ اصل صور میں ۔ 
وَلَوْ شَكٍّ فِي دَخُولِ وَقْتِ الْعِبَادَةِ فَأَتَى بِهَا فَبَانَ أَنَّهُ فَعَلَهَا فِي الْوَقْتِ لَمْ يُجْزِهِ أَخْذًا مِنْ قَوْلِهِمْ، كَمَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ: لَوْ صَلَّى الْفَرْضَ، وَعِنْدَهُ أَنَّ الْوَقْتَ لَمْ يَدْخُلْ فَظَهَرَ أَنَّهُ قَدْ دَخَلَ لَا يُجْزِئُهُ، انْتَهَى. وَ فِي خِزَانَةِ الْأَكْمَلِ : أَدْرَكَ الْقَوْمَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، وَلَا يَدْرِي أَنَّهَا الْمَكْتُوبَةُ أَوِ التَّرْوِيحَةُ يُكَبِّرُ وَ يَنْوِي الْمَكْتُوبَةَ عَلَى أَنَّهَا إِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ مَكْتُوبَةً يَقْضِيَهَا يَعْنِي الْعِشَاءَ، فَإِذَا هُوَ فِي الْعِشَاءِ صَحَّ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي التَّرْوِيحَةِ يَقَعُ نَفْلًا، انْتَهَى.
ترجمہ: اور اگر عبادت کا وقت داخل ہونے میں اسے شک ہو پھر بھی اس نے وہ ( عبادت ) پوری کر لی پھر واضح ہوا کہ اس نے وہ وقت میں ہی ادا کی ہے تو وہ اس کے لئے درست نہیں ہے اور یہ مسئلہ فقہاء کے اس قول سے ماخوذ ہے جو فتح القدیر میں ہے کہ اگر کسی نے فرض نماز پڑھی اور اس کا گمان یہ ہے کہ وقت داخل نہیں ہوا ہے پھر بعد میں واضح ہوا کہ وقت ہو گیا تھا تو وہ فرض نماز اس کے لئے کافی نہیں۔ اور خزانہ الاکمل میں ہے کہ اگر لوگوں کو نماز میں پایا لیکن اسے معلوم نہیں کہ یہ فرض نماز ہے یا تراویح ہے؟ تو وہ تکبیر کہے اور اس فرض کی نیت کر لے اس وضاحت کے ساتھ کہ اگر وہ فرض نہ ہوئی تو وہ اسے یعنی عشاء کو قضاء کرلے گا پھر معلوم ہوا کہ وہ عشاء ہی تھی تو صحیح ہے اور اگر یہ تراویح تھی تو وہ نفل ہو جائے گی ۔ انتہی
تشریح: کسی شخص کو نماز کے وقت کے دخول میں شک تھا اسی شک کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی بعد میں پتہ چلا کہ وہ وقت میں ہی پڑھی گئی ہے تو یہ نماز کافی نہ ہوگی اور اس کی نظیر فتح القدیر میں فقہاء کرام کا قول یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے فرض نماز پڑھی اور اس کے نزدیک ابھی وقت داخل نہیں ہوا تھا پھر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ وقت داخل ہو گیا تھا تو ان کا یہ نماز کافی نہ ہوگی۔
It is narrated about a person who purchased a servant for service and he intends that if it brings him profit he will sell it, then there is no zakat on it. Clarification: For intention to be valid, it is necessary that just as there should not be any contradictory matter between the intention and the intended object that indicates abandonment of the intention, similarly if there is indecisiveness in the original intention, that intention is also invalid; rather certainty and firmness are required in intention. If someone purchased a slave with the intention of service and intended that if profit occurs then I will sell it, then there is no zakat on it because the original intention is service, and even if he made a firm intention to sell, it would still not be for trade until the actual practice of trade occurs, as its detail has passed previously. Hisham said: I asked Muhammad about a man who purchased a slave-girl for service and he intends that if he makes a profit he will sell her, then a year passed over her; he said there is no zakat on her. And they said: If on the day of doubt he intended that if it is from Sha'ban then he is not fasting, and if it is from Ramadan then he is fasting, his intention is not valid; and if he was indecisive in the description by intending that if tomorrow is from Sha'ban then it is supererogatory, otherwise it is for Ramadan, his intention is valid, as we have explained in the Book of Fasting. And on this basis, if there is a missed prayer upon him and he doubted whether he had made it up or not, then he performed it, then it became clear that it was due upon him, then it will not suffice him due to the doubt and lack of certainty in its specification. Translation: And the jurists say... Clarification: Someone fasted on the day of doubt with this intention... And if he was indecisive in the description... And if there is doubt about the entry of the time of worship and he performed it, then it became clear that he did it within the time, it does not suffice him, taken from their statement, as in Fath al-Qadir: If he prayed the obligatory prayer while thinking that the time had not entered, then it appeared that it had entered, it does not suffice him. End quote. And in Khizanat al-Akmal: He found people in prayer and he does not know whether it is the obligatory or tarawih; he says takbir and intends the obligatory on the condition that if it is not obligatory he will make it up, meaning the 'isha, so if it is 'isha it is valid, and if it is tarawih it falls as supererogatory. End quote. Translation... Clarification: A person doubted the entry of the time of prayer and prayed with that doubt; later it became clear that he prayed within the time, this prayer is not sufficient...
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents a series of applications of the legal principle that intention (niyyah) must be certain (jazm) and free from indecisiveness (taraddud). It is a qawida with furuat: the maxim is that intention must be decisive and not conditional upon future contingencies unless the condition relates only to the legal description (wasf) of the act. The first application is from zakah: if someone buys a slave for service but intends to sell it if profit arises, no zakah is due because the primary intention is service and the conditional intention to sell is not certain. The second application concerns fasting on yawm al-shakk: if one intends conditionally that if it is Sha'ban he is not fasting and if Ramadan he is fasting, the intention is invalid because it is pendent on an unknown. However, if the condition concerns only the description (whether it is obligatory or supererogatory), then the intention is valid because the act of fasting itself is certain. The third application extends to a missed prayer performed with doubt about whether it was already made up: if one performs it with such doubt, it does not suffice even if it later appears that it was due, because the intention lacked certainty. The fourth application discusses joining a congregation without knowing whether it is fard or tarawih: if one intends the fard conditionally (i.e., if it is not the fard he will make it up), it is valid for either case because the intention is certain for the fard and the condition is on the description. All these examples illustrate the centrality of jazm in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention a person makes in the heart to perform a specific act of worship.
جزم (jazm): Certainty and decisiveness in intention without any doubt or condition.
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The 30th day of Sha'ban when there is doubt whether it is the last day of Sha'ban or the first day of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone buys a slave for service and intends that if a profit arises he will sell it, and a full year passes, is zakat due on the slave according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because the conditional intent to sell makes it a trade asset.
B) No, because the primary intention is service and the conditional intention is not certain.
C) Yes, because any intention of sale triggers zakat.
D) No, because slaves are never subject to zakat.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim on certain intention (al-niyyah al-jazima) distinguishes between indecisiveness on the essence (invalidates) and indecisiveness on the description (does not invalidate), with practical applications across acts of worship.

Doubt in Description (Wasf) Does Not Invalidate Intention
Ruling on doubt in description of an act with application to qada salat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-taraddud fi al-wasf la yubtil al-niyyah' to cases of intention in worship, distinguishing between doubt in the description and doubt in the act itself, and identify when the obligation is fulfilled.

Core Idea
Doubt in the description (wasf) of an act does not nullify the intention; only doubt in the act itself invalidates.

In this lesson, we examine a subtle but essential principle from the Hanafi tradition: doubt regarding the attribute or description of an act does not affect the validity of the intention. For example, when fasting on the doubtful day (yawm al-shakk), one may intend 'if it is Ramadan, then Ramadan; otherwise supererogatory.' The fast is valid, albeit disliked. We will explore the scope and applications of this qawida, including its implications for making up missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Identify the qawida text and its English meaning. The maxim is 'al-taraddud fi al-wasf la yubtil al-niyyah' (doubt in description does not nullify intention).
2
Identify its scope and condition
The qawida applies to acts of worship where intention is required, but only when both possible descriptions correspond to a valid act of worship. If one description corresponds to no valid act (e.g., not performing an act), the intention does not fulfill the obligation.
This nuance is critical for correct application.
3
Apply to the first furu': fasting on yawm al-shakk
The intention covers both Ramadan (wajib) and nafl (valid). Both are valid acts of fasting. The fast is valid but disliked (makruh) due to the doubt.
Source: passage states 'ma'a al-karahah'.
4
Apply to the second furu': qada prayer
The intention covers only one valid description (qada), the other (no act) is not a valid act of worship. Therefore, the prayer does not satisfy the missed wajib; the obligation remains.
Source: passage states 'la yajzi 'an al-wajib' (does not suffice for the wajib).
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in fasting, the intention is acceptable despite doubt; in qada prayer, the intention is not sufficient to fulfill the obligation. This distinction must be applied when issuing fatwa.
The mufta bihi is based on the analysis in Shami.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میرا روزہ افضل ہے ورنہ رمضان کا ہے تو اس کی نیت صحیح ہوگی کیونکہ اسے محض وصف میں تردد ہے نہ کہ کلی صورت میں۔ ولو ردد في الوصف: لیکن اگر کسی نے یوم الشک میں اس نیت سے روزہ رکھا کہ اگر یہ رمضان کا ہے تو رمضان کا اور اگر نہیں تو [؟] صائما مع الکراہة لو ردد في وصفها بان نوى ان کان من رمضان فعنه والا من [؟] وينبغي على هذا انه لو كانت عليه فائتة: لہذا ہم نے اوپر جوڑ کر کیا ہے کہ وصف میں شک ہو تو رہ تین نہیں ہے اس پر یہ مسئلہ بھی بنی ہونا چاہئے کہ کسی کے اوپر فائتہ نماز تھی اسے اس کے قضاء کرنے یا نہ کرنے میں اسی کے ساتھ اس نیت سے اس نے ادا کر لیا بعد میں واضح ہوا کہ وہ نماز اس کے ذمہ میں بھی تو شک اور عدم تمیز کی وجہ سے وہ نماز واجب آخر (شامی ج ۳ : ۳۵)
If my fasting is supererogatory otherwise it is Ramadan, then his intention is correct because he only doubts the description, not the entire act. And if he doubts the description: But if someone on the day of doubt fasts with this intention: if it is Ramadan then Ramadan, otherwise [something], he fasts with dislike. If he doubts its description such that he intends: if it is from Ramadan then it is Ramadan, otherwise from [something]. And it is befitting that if he had a missed prayer, then we have linked above that doubt in description does not negate [validity]. On this, this issue should also be based: someone had a missed prayer; in performing or not performing it, he performed it with that intention; later it became clear that that prayer was upon him; due to doubt and lack of distinction, that prayer does not suffice for the wajib. (Shami vol. 3: 35)
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents a qawida: doubt in the description (wasf) of an act—such as whether a fast is for Ramadan or a voluntary fast—does not invalidate the intention, because the doubt is only over an attribute, not over the essence of the act. The fast is valid but disliked (makruh). The same principle applies to qada prayers: if someone has a missed prayer and performs it with uncertainty whether it is qada or not, the prayer does not fulfill the obligation due to lack of certainty. The Hanafi position is that intention must be certain regarding the essential act; doubt in description is excused but disliked.

Key Terms
وصف (wasf): The specific attribute or description of an act (e.g., whether a fast is Ramadan or nafl, or a prayer is qada or ada).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on fasting on yawm al-shakk with the intention: 'If it is Ramadan, then Ramadan; otherwise, nafl' according to the Hanafi school?
A) The fast is invalid due to doubt.
B) The fast is valid but disliked (makruh).
C) The fast is valid and recommended.
D) The fast is invalid unless one specifies Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'doubt in description does not nullify intention' applies only when both possible descriptions correspond to valid acts of worship; in cases where one description is non-worship, the obligation is not fulfilled.

Doubt in Entry of Time Invalidates Worship (الشك في دخول الوقت)
Ruling: doubt in time invalidates worship; exception with conditional intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'Shakk fi al-waqt mubtil li al-ibadah' to new cases and identify the exception requiring conditional intention.

Core Idea
Doubt in the entry of time invalidates the worship; only a conditional intention can save it.

This lesson examines a critical qawida (legal maxim) from the Hanafi school: uncertainty about the starting time of a worship renders the act invalid, even if later proven to be within time. We will see the general rule and a nuanced exception from Khizanat al-Akmal involving conditional intention. This distinction is essential for muftis when giving fatwa on delayed prayers or joining congregations.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida and its scope
Articulate the maxim al-shakk fi dukhul al-waqt mubtil li al-ibadah and note that it applies to any time-bound worship, particularly prayer and fasting.
The scope is universal within ibadat.
2
Understand the rationale
Certainty (yaqin) of time is a condition for validity. Doubt precludes this certainty, making the act invalid even if later confirmed.
This is stricter than some other schools.
3
Examine the exception
In Khizanat al-Akmal, a person joining a congregation with uncertainty about whether it is fard or taraweeh can make a conditional intention (e.g., intending fard with the condition to qada if not). This provides sufficient specification to overcome doubt.
The exception requires an explicit conditional intention.
4
Distinguish between the two scenarios
Unconditional doubt (general rule) vs. conditional intention (exception). The latter is governed by the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'.
The exception does not undermine the rule; it operates under a different maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أَنَّ الْوَقْتَ لَمْ يَدْخُلْ فَظَهَرَ أَنَّهُ قَدْ دَخَلَ لَا يُجْزِتُهُ، إنْتَهَى وَ فِي خِزَانَةِ الْأَكْمَلِ : أَدْرَكَ الْقَوْمِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، وَلَا يَدْرِى أَنَّهَا الْمَكْتَوْبَةُ أَوِ بھی ہے اور معین فرض بھی ہے اور اگر تراویح ہو رہی تھی تو اس کی نماز نفل ہو جائے گی تراویح کی نماز نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ تراویح کا وقت عشاء کے بعد ہے اور اس نے ابھی عشاء ہی نہیں پڑھی اس پر لازم ہوگا کہ پہلے عشاء پڑھے اس کے بعد تروایح پڑھے۔
And if he doubts the entry of the time of worship and he performs it, then it becomes clear that he did it within the time, it does not suffice him, as per their statement, as in Fath al-Qadir: If he prayed a obligatory prayer while he thought that the time had not entered, then it appears that it had entered, it does not suffice him, end. And in Khizanat al-Akmal: He joined a congregation in prayer and does not know whether it is the obligatory or taraweeh; he says takbir and intends the obligatory with the condition that if it is not the obligatory he will make it up, meaning Isha. Then if it is Isha, it is valid; if it is taraweeh, it falls as nafl, end. Translation: ... Commentary: ... And in Khizanat al-Akmal: A man saw some people praying in congregation and he did not know whether it was obligatory or taraweeh; he says takbir and intends the obligatory, with the condition that if it is not obligatory he will make up Isha. He joins. Later it becomes known that it was Isha prayer, so his prayer is correct because here there is intention of the original prayer and also the specified obligatory. If it was taraweeh, his prayer becomes nafl, not taraweeh, because taraweeh time is after Isha and he has not yet prayed Isha; he must first pray Isha then taraweeh.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage states a clear rule: if one performs a worship while doubting whether its time has entered, and later discovers it was indeed within time, the worship is not valid. This is because certainty of time is a condition for validity; doubt precludes that certainty. The example from Fath al-Qadir illustrates: if one prays fard thinking time has not entered, but it actually had, the prayer does not count. However, the Khizanat al-Akmal case shows an exception: if one joins a congregation not knowing if it is fard or taraweeh, and he intends fard with a conditional intention (if not fard, then it is qada of Isha), then if it turns out to be Isha, it is valid because he had a clear intention for Isha (the fard) and an alternative plan. If it was taraweeh, it becomes nafl because taraweeh cannot be performed before Isha. This nuance underscores that while doubt in time generally invalidates, conditional intention with proper specification can salvage the act.

Key Terms
شك في الوقت (shakk fi al-waqt): Uncertainty about whether the obligatory time for a worship has begun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone prays Maghrib while doubting whether the time for Maghrib has entered, and later confirms it was within time, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid because it was performed in time.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The prayer is valid only if a conditional intention was made.
D) The prayer is valid but disliked.

Key Takeaway
Doubt in time invalidates worship; only a clear conditional intention can avert it.

Specifying General Oaths by Intention: Diyanatan Only
Qawida with furu' and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'تخصيص العام بالنية في الأيمان مقبول ديانة لا قضاء' to a new oath scenario and distinguish the diyanatan and qada'an rulings.

Core Idea
Intention specifies an oath only before Allah, not in court.

This lesson examines a key qawida from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair concerning oaths. When a person makes a general oath and later claims a specific intention, that intention is valid religiously (diyanatan) but not judicially (qada'an). This distinction protects the integrity of legal proceedings while honoring the individual's conscience. We will explore the rule, its application, and a scholarly disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida
Identify the exact Arabic text of the legal maxim from the source and its English translation.
The qawida is: تخصيص العام بالنية في الأيمان مقبول ديانة لا قضاء
2
Understand the diyanatan vs qada'an distinction
Define diyanatan (religious validity before Allah) and qada'an (judicial enforceability). The same act may have different rulings in the two realms.
Diyanatan relates to the swearer's accountability to Allah; qada'an relates to the judge's ruling based on external evidence.
3
Work through the furu' case
Apply the qawida to the example: if someone says 'Every woman I marry is divorced' and later claims he only meant women from a certain town.
Diyanatan: only women from that town are divorced; qada'an: all women are divorced because the literal general wording is enforced.
4
Examine the dispute with al-Khassaf
Al-Khassaf held that specification by intention is accepted judicially as well. Understand the opposing proof and the Hanafi response.
The Hanafi majority argues that accepting intention judicially would undermine the reliability of oaths and open doors to fraud.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and fatwa implications
The relied-upon position is the majority view: diyanatan only. A mufti should advise the swearer to follow his intention religiously, but a judge will enforce the literal meaning.
This rule is applied in all oath-related cases in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَاعِدَةٌ فِي الْأَيْمَانِ : تَخْصِيْصُ الْعَامُ بِالنِّيَّةِ مَقْبُولٌ دِيَانَةً، لَا فَضَاءٌ، وَعِنْدَ الْخَصَّافِ يَصِحُ قَضاءُ أَيْضًا فَلَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ امْرَأَةٍ أَتَزَوَّجُهَا فَهِيَ طَالِقٌ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: نَوَيْتُ مِنْ بَلْدَةِ كَذَا، لَمْ
A rule concerning oaths: Specifying the general by intention is accepted religiously (diyanatan), not judicially (qada'an). According to al-Khassaf, it is also valid judicially. So if he says: 'Every woman I marry is divorced,' then he says: 'I meant from a certain town,' [it is not accepted judicially]. The text cuts off.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage presents a qawida about oaths (ayman). When a person makes a general statement (like 'every woman I marry is divorced'), and later claims he intended only a specific group (e.g., women from a certain town), his specification is accepted diyanatan (in the religious sense, i.e., before Allah) but not qada'an (in a court of law). This means the oath is binding as per his intention in the sight of Allah, but a judge will enforce the literal general meaning. Al-Khassaf holds that it is accepted judicially as well, but the Hanafi position is the former. This rule protects the oath's enforceability while allowing the swearer to have a clear conscience if he had a specific intent.

Key Terms
ديانة (diyanatan): Religiously or before Allah; the ruling in the inner conscience.
قضاء (qada'an): Judicially; the ruling enforced by a judge.
تخصيص العام (takhsis al-'amm): Specification of a general term, limiting its application to a subset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only women from Baghdad are divorced upon marriage.
B) Any woman he marries is divorced, regardless of his intention.
C) The oath is invalid due to ambiguity.
D) He must repeat the oath with specification.

Key Takeaway
Specification of a general oath by intention is valid only before Allah (diyanatan), not in court (qada'an).

Effect of Insha'Allah on Intention and Pronouncements
A Hanafi subsidiary rule on conditioning with Insha'Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that saying 'Insha'Allah' does not invalidate intention-based acts but does invalidate verbal pronouncements like divorce and emancipation.

Core Idea
Insha'Allah after intention leaves it valid; after a verbal pronouncement, it nullifies.

This subsidiary rule from the Hanafi school draws a sharp line between acts that rely on internal intentions and those that rely on explicit verbal declarations. When a person says 'Insha'Allah' after making an intention for prayer or fasting, the intention remains intact. But if the same phrase is added to a pronouncement of divorce or emancipation, the pronouncement becomes void. Understanding this distinction is crucial for muftis issuing fatwas on conditional acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of acts
The source distinguishes between acts that relate to intentions (نىّات) like fasting and prayer, and acts that relate to verbal pronouncements (أقوال) like divorce and emancipation.
This is a key classification in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Apply the rule to each category
For intention-based acts, adding 'Insha'Allah' does NOT invalidate the intention. For pronouncement-based acts, it DOES invalidate the pronouncement.
The rationale is that verbal expressions require immediate effect, while intentions are internal and not subject to verbal conditions.
3
Understand the rationale
The source explains that 'Insha'Allah' is not a true exception clause but a request for divine assistance (istihsan). Therefore, it does not nullify intentions. However, for explicit verbal contracts, conditioning on Allah's will negates the immediate commitment required.
Refer to al-Shami commentary cited in the source.
4
Recognize the mufta bihi position
The correct and relied-upon Hanafi view is that intention-based acts are not invalidated by saying 'Insha'Allah'. This is the position for fatwa.
Any retraction from the act after the fact can invalidate it, but not the phrase itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَرْعُ: عَقْبَ النِّيَّةِ بِالْمَشِيْئَةِ، فَقَدَّمْنَا أَنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ كَالصَّوْمِ وَ الصَّلَاةِ لَمْ تَبْطُلْ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْأَقْوَالِ كَالطَّلَاقِ وَ الْعِتَاقِ بَطَلَ. ترجمه جزئیہ کسی نے نیت کے بعد انشاء اللہ کہ دیا تو ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ اگر وہ نیات سے متعلق ہو جسے روزہ اور نماز تو نیت باطل نہیں ہوگی اور اگر وہ اقوال سے متعلق ہو جیسے طلاق اور عتاق تو وہ باطل ہے تشریح ماقبل میں یہ اصول ذکر کیا گیا تھا کہ جملہ عقود و تصرفات جن کا مدار اقوال پر ہے انشاء اللہ ان پر اثر انداز ہوتا ہے اور جن کا مدار اقوال پر نہیں ہے بلکہ نیتوں پر ہے تو وہاں انشاء اللہ کا کچھ اثر نہیں ہوگا۔ ولا تبطل بالمشيئة بل بالرجوع عنها وتحته في الشامية أى استحساناً وهو الصحيح لأنها ليست في معنى حقيقة الاستثناء بل للإستعانة وطلب التوفيق. (شامی ج ۳، ص: ۳۴۵)
Subsidiary: Regarding conditioning an intention with the phrase 'Insha'Allah', we have already mentioned that if it is something related to intentions like fasting and prayer, the intention is not invalidated. And if it is something related to pronouncements like divorce and emancipation, it becomes invalid. Translation: If someone says 'Insha'Allah' after an intention, we have already said that if it pertains to intentions like fasting and prayer, the intention is not invalidated. And if it pertains to pronouncements like divorce and emancipation, it is invalid. Explanation: Previously, this principle was mentioned: all contracts and transactions that depend on pronouncements are affected by 'Insha'Allah', but those that depend on intentions, 'Insha'Allah' has no effect. And it is not invalidated by the phrase 'If Allah wills' but by retracting from it. And in Shami: it is istihsan and it is correct, because it is not really an exception but for seeking assistance and success.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This subsidiary rule differentiates between acts whose validity depends on intention (like prayer and fasting) and acts whose validity depends on explicit verbal pronouncements (like divorce and emancipation). Saying 'Insha'Allah' after an intention does not invalidate the intention, because the intention is an internal act of the heart not subject to verbal conditioning. However, after a verbal pronouncement like divorce, adding 'Insha'Allah' renders the pronouncement ineffective, because it implies a condition that negates the immediate effect. The preferred view in the Hanafi school, as stated in al-Shami, is that such a phrase is not a true exception but a request for divine assistance, so it does not invalidate intention-based acts. However, if one retracts the act, it becomes invalid.

Key Terms
انشاء اللہ (Insha'Allah): A phrase meaning 'if Allah wills', used to condition an act upon divine will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid
B) Invalid
C) Suspended
D) Subject to retraction

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, saying 'Insha'Allah' invalidates verbal pronouncements but not intentions.

Specifying General Oaths by Intention: The Qawida of Diyanatan vs. Qada'an
A legal maxim on the acceptance of specifying a general oath with intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'takhsis al-amm bi al-niyyah' to distinguish when specification by intention is accepted diyanatan versus qada'an, and identify the exception for coercion.

Core Idea
Specifying a general oath by intention is accepted between you and Allah, but not in court — unless a tyrant forces you.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi qawida on oaths: whether a person can limit a general oath by his inner intention. The maxim distinguishes between the realm of conscience (diyanatan) and the courtroom (qada'an). Through two furu' cases and an exception, we see how the Hanafi school balances textual generality with practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its two parts
Read the Arabic maxim and its translation. Note that it has two halves: diyanatan (accepted in conscience) and la qada'an (not accepted judicially).
The maxim is a sughra (minor) qawida specific to oaths.
2
Understand the diyanatan/qada'an distinction
Diyanatan means between the person and Allah – the court does not enforce it. Qada'an means judicially enforceable. The court goes by the apparent meaning.
This distinction recurs throughout Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply to the first furu' case
Consider the case: someone says 'Every woman I marry is divorced' then claims he intended only women from a specific city. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, his claim is not accepted in court.
The general wording binds him legally.
4
Apply to the second furu' case
Consider a usurper who, when the opponent swears a general oath, intends specific dirhams. Again, the intention does not limit the oath judicially.
Same principle applies.
5
Identify the istithna' and its rationale
The exception is coercion by a tyrant. In that case, following al-Khassaf's view, one may specify by intention to escape hardship. This is allowed by the maxim 'Harm must be removed'.
This is a dispensation, not the general rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَاعِدَةٌ فِي الْأَيْمَانِ : تَخْصِيْصُ الْعَامُ بِالنِّيَّةِ مَقْبُولٌ دِيَانَةً، لَا فَضَاءٌ، وَعِنْدَ الْخَصَّافِ يَصِحُ قَضاءُ أَيْضًا فَلَوْ قَالَ: كُلُّ امْرَأَةٍ أَتَزَوَّجُهَا فَهِيَ طَالِقٌ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: نَوَيْتُ مِنْ بَلْدَةِ كَذَا، لَمْ يَصِحْ فِي ظَاهِرِ الْمَذْهَبِ خِلَافاً لِلْخَصَّافِ وَ كَذَا مَنْ غَصَبَ دَرَاهِمَ إِنْسَانِ فَلَمَّا خَلْفَهُ الْخَصْمُ عَامَّا نَوَى خَاصًا وَ مَا قَالَهُ الْخَصَّافُ مَخْلَصٌ لِمَنْ حَلَّفَهُ ظَالِمٌ وَ وَالْفَتْوَىٰ عَلَىٰ ظَاهِرِ الْمَذْهَبِ فَمَنْ وَقَعَ فِي يَدِ الظُّلَمَةِ وَ ُأخِذَ بِقَوْلِ الْخَصَّافِ فَلَا بَأْسَ بِهِ كَذَا فِي الْوَالْوَ الْحِيَّة . ترجمه: قاعدہ ایمان کے بارے میں ۔ عام کو بذریعہ نیت خاص کرنا دیا یہ مقبول ہے قضاء نہیں اور اور خصاف کے نزدیک قضاء ( بھی ) درست ہے پس اگر یہ کہا کہ جس عورت سے میں شادی کروں اسے طلاق ہے پھر وہ یہ کہے کہ میری مرا فلاں شہر کی عورتوں کی تھی تو ظاہری مذہب کے مطابق صحیح نہیں ہے امام خصاف کا اس میں اختلاف ہے اس طرح کسی نے کسی آدمی کے درہم چھین لئے پھر جب فریق مخالف نے عام کی قسم دلوائی تو اس نے خاص کی نیت صحیح نہیں ہے ) اور خصاف نے جوفر مایا وہ تم پر تجات ہے اس شخص کے لئے جس کو کوئی ظالم حلف دے رہا ہو اور فتویٰ ظاہر مذہب پر ہے پس جو آدمی ظالموں کے ہاتھ پڑ جائے اور خصاف کے قول پر عمل کرے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے والو او لجیہ میں اس طرح ہے۔
A principle regarding oaths: Specifying a general term by intention is accepted in conscience (diyanatan), not in judiciary (qada'an). According to al-Khassaf, it is also valid judicially. So if someone says: 'Every woman I marry is divorced,' then he says: 'I intended from such-and-such city,' it is not valid in the apparent school, contrary to al-Khassaf. Similarly, if someone usurps another's dirhams, then when the opponent swore a general oath, he intended specific (dirhams). And what al-Khassaf said is a way out for one whom a tyrant makes to swear. And the fatwa is upon the apparent school. So whoever falls into the hands of oppressors and acts upon the statement of al-Khassaf, there is no harm. Thus in al-Walwajiyya.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This qa'idah addresses a critical issue in oaths: if a person makes a general oath (e.g., 'I will not speak to any man'), can he later claim that he intended only a specific group? According to Zahir al-Riwayah (the apparent school), such specification by intention is accepted only in matters of conscience (diyanatan), meaning between the person and Allah, but not in a court of law (qada'an). The judge will enforce the apparent meaning. However, Imam al-Khassaf held that it is also accepted judicially, provided the general term was uttered. This disagreement has practical consequences: if a tyrant forces a man to swear a general oath, the man may use al-Khassaf's ruling to escape hardship by intending a specific meaning, and this is permissible. The fatwa in normal cases follows the apparent school, but in situations of coercion, acting upon al-Khassaf's view is allowed. This is a nazirah (similar case) illustrating the application of the qa'idah.

Key Terms
دیانة (diyanatan): Acceptance in matters of conscience, not enforceable by court.
قضاء (qada'an): Judicially enforceable ruling.
خصاف (al-Khassaf): A Hanafi jurist known for his views on oaths and stratagems.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on specifying a general oath by intention in the apparent school (Zahir al-Riwayah)?
A) It is accepted both diyanatan and qada'an.
B) It is accepted diyanatan but not qada'an.
C) It is not accepted at all.
D) It is accepted qada'an only.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi jurisprudence, specifying a general oath by intention is accepted only between the person and Allah, not in court, unless coercion makes al-Khassaf's view applicable.

6 min
Qawida: Oath is According to the Intention of the Oppressed Oath-Taker or the Oppressive Oath-Imposer
States the maxim for whose intention matters in oaths: the swearer or the one imposing the oath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida to determine whose intention governs in an oath when coercion is involved, and identify the mufta bihi ruling from Hanafi fatwa practice.

Core Idea
The oath follows the intention of the oppressed, not the oppressor.

This lesson introduces a vital legal maxim (qawida) from Hanafi usul al-iftaa that addresses oath-taking under duress. The maxim protects the oppressed by shifting the interpretive authority: if the swearer is coerced, his true intention is honoured; if the imposer is the oppressor, his intention constrains the oath's enforceability. Muftis rely on this rule to issue just fatwas in cases of forced oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Distinguish between the oath-taker (halif) and the one imposing the oath (mustahlif). Determine who is the potential oppressor and who is the oppressed.
The oppressor is typically the one with power forcing the oath.
2
Assess the condition of oppression
Decide if the halif is truly oppressed (mazlum) or if the mustahlif is oppressive (zalim). In most forced-oath scenarios, the halif is oppressed and the mustahlif is oppressive.
The maxim covers both possibilities—but in practice they often coincide.
3
Apply the maxim
If the halif is mazlum, interpret the oath according to his intention. If the mustahlif is zalim, interpret the oath according to the mustahlif's intention—meaning his own understanding binds him, and the judge does not enforce an interpretation that harms the oppressed. The result is that the oppressed swearer's diyanatan intention is accepted.
The furuat clarify that the swearer's intention effectively governs when coercion is present.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
In Hanafi fatwa practice, the relied-upon view is that a coerced oath is not binding; the swearer's true intent is accepted. The mufti looks at the circumstances and gives the benefit of the doubt to the oppressed.
This aligns with the maxim's purpose of preventing injustice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَاعِدَةٌ فِيْهَا أَيْضاً : الْيَمِيْنُ عَلَى نِيَّةِ الْحَالِفِ إِنْ كَانَ مَظْلُوماً وَ عَلَى نِيَّةِ الْمُسْتَحْلِفِ إِنْ كَانَ ظَالِماً كَمَا فِي الْخُلَاصَةِ.
A rule also in it: The oath is according to the intention of the oath-taker if he is oppressed, and according to the intention of the one who imposes the oath if he is oppressive, as in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This is a standalone qawida (maxim) that regulates how oaths are interpreted in situations of duress or injustice. The rule distinguishes two scenarios: 1) If the person swearing (halif) is oppressed (mazlum) — meaning he is forced to swear by an oppressive party — his own inner intention is considered when interpreting the oath. For example, if a tyrant forces someone to swear 'By Allah, I have not taken your money' while he actually intends a different time or place, his true intention counts religiously, and he may be excused. 2) If the one imposing the oath (mustahlif) is the oppressor (zalim), then the intention of the imposer (the tyrant) is taken into account. This means if the tyrant had a specific understanding of the oath, that understanding becomes relevant in judicial consequences? Actually, the rule likely means that when the imposer is oppressive, the swearer's ambiguous words are interpreted against the oppressor (i.e., in favor of the oppressed), so the oppressed can use a general expression with a specific intention to escape the tyrant's injustice. The reference to al-Khulasa (a Hanafi fiqh work) indicates this is a well-established rule. Muftis use this rule to give relief to those coerced into oaths by unjust authorities.

Key Terms
الْحَالِف (al-halif): The person who takes the oath.
الْمُسْتَحْلِف (al-mustahlif): The person who imposes the oath on another, i.e., makes him swear.
مَظْلُوم (mazlum): The one being oppressed, i.e., forced to swear against his will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida, when must the intention of the oath-imposer (mustahlif) be considered?
A) When the oath-imposer is just and fair.
B) When the oath-imposer is oppressive (zalim).
C) When the oath-taker is willing.
D) Always, regardless of circumstances.

Key Takeaway
In oaths, the intention of the oppressed party is accepted diyanatan, preventing exploitation by oppressors.

Oaths Based on Words, Not Purposes
Maxim that oaths hinge on wording, not inner motives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-aymaan mabniyyah ala al-alfaz la al-aghrad' to determine whether an oath has been breached in a given scenario.

Core Idea
An oath is judged by its words, not the swearer's hidden purpose.

This lesson examines a foundational Hanafi maxim in the law of oaths: an oath is interpreted strictly according to its wording, not the swearer's inner motives. Understanding this rule is critical for muftis issuing fatwas on oath breaches. The maxim is supported by several illustrative cases from classical Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Identify the Arabic text of the maxim and note that it applies to all oaths in Hanafi fiqh (oaths by God, divorce, emancipation, etc.).
2
Work through the furuat (derived cases)
Analyze the examples from the text: swearing not to buy/sell for a specific amount and then transacting for a different amount. Determine breach based solely on wording.
3
Identify the key distinction
Note that the oath is broken only when the exact wording is violated, not when the purpose is achieved. For instance, swearing not to sell for ten and selling for eleven breaks the oath because eleven includes ten, but selling for nine does not.
4
Identify the istithna (exception)
Understand that intention can be considered if the word is capable of bearing the intended meaning. This is governed by the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' and does not contradict the main rule.
5
Summarize practical application for fatwa
A mufti must first ascertain the literal or customary meaning of the oath's wording before considering any claims about the swearer's intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَاعِدَةٌ فِيْهَا أَيْضًا: الأَيْمَانُ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى الأَلْفَاظِ لَا عَلَى الْأَعْرَاضِ، فَلَوْ اغْتَاظَ مِنْ إِنْسَانِ فَحَلَفَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَشْتَرِى لَهُ شِيْئًا بِفَلسٍ، فَاشْتَرَى لَهُ شَيْئًا بِمَاةٍ دِرْهَم لَمْ يَحْنَتْ وَلَوْ خَلَقَ لا يَبْعَة بِعَشْرَةٍ، فَبَاعَهُ بِاحَدَ عَشَرَ، أَوْ بِتِسْعَةٍ لَمْ يَحْتَ مَع أن غرفة الزيادة الكبر لا حنث بلا لفظ. وَلَوْ خَلَفَ لَا يَشْتَرِيهِ بِعَشْرٍ حَيْثُ وَ لَمَامُهُ فِي الْجَيْمِ الْجَامِع الصَّغِيرِ وَ شَرْحُهُ لِلْفَارْسِيّ. ترجمه : ایمان سے متعلق ہی قاعدہ ہے کہ ایمان الفاظ پرانی ہوتی ہیں اغراض و مقاصد پانی میں ہو کہ کو اگر کسی انسان سے غصہ ہو کر قسم کھائی کہ وہ اس کے لئے ایک پیسہ کی چیز نہیں خریدے گا پھر اس نے اس کے لئے سودرہم کی کوئی چیز خرید لی تو وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا اور اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ ( کوئی سامان ) اسے دیس میں بھی ہے پھر اس نے (وہ سامان) اسے گیارہ میں یا نو میں فروخت کر دیا تو وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا باوجود اس کے کہ اسکا مقصد زیادہ میں فروخت کرنا تھا لیکن بغیر لفظ کے وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا اور اگر اس نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ اسے دس میں نہیں رہے گا پھر اس نے گیارہ میں خرید لیا تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا اور اس کی پوری بحث تخصیص جامع صغیر اور علامہ فارس کی جوانکی شرح ہے اس میں ہے۔ تشریح نہین کا دار ومدار الفاظ کے عرفی معنی پر ہوتا ہے اور اگر عرف ہی نہ ہوتو حقیقی معنی کا مقاصد اور نیت پر یمین کا دارو مدار نہیں ہوتا ہاں البتہ اگر وہ لفظ جس معنی کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور حلف ای عملی کی نیند کرلے تو اس وقت نیت پر عدار ہو سکتا ہے۔ الإيمان مبنية على الألفاظ لا على الأغراض وتحته في رد المحتار أى على المقاصدو النيات احترز به عن القول ببنائها على النية (شامى جه س: am) فلو المحتاظ: ایمان کے سلسلہ میں جو قاعدہ ذکر کیا گیا کہ الايمان مبينة على الألفاظ لا على الأغراض" اس پر یہ مسئلہ متفرع ہے کہ اگرکی نے قصہ میں تم کھائی کہ میں تیرے لئے ایک ہی کو کوئی چیز میں خریدی ماری کے لئے سو درہم میں کوئی چیز خرید لی تو وہ حال نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ایمان کا مدار الفاظ پر ہے اور اسنے تم ایک ہی کانہ خریدنے کی کھائی تھی جیسا کہ شامی میں اس کی تصریح ہے۔
A rule in it as well: Oaths are built upon words, not upon purposes. For example, if someone got angry with a person and swore that he will not buy anything for him for a fils, and then bought something for a hundred dirhams, he does not break the oath. And if he swore that he will not sell it for ten, and then sold it for eleven or nine, he does not break the oath, even though his purpose was to sell for more — there is no breach without the word. And if he swore that he will not buy it for ten, and then bought it for eleven, he would break the oath. Its full discussion is in al-Jami' al-Saghir and its commentary by al-Farsi. Translation: Also a rule regarding oaths: Oaths are based on words, not on aims and purposes. For example, if someone became angry with a person and swore that he will not buy anything for him for one paisa, then he bought something for him for a hundred dirhams, he does not break the oath. And if someone swore that he will not sell an item for ten, then he sold it for eleven or nine, he does not break the oath, despite his purpose being to sell for more; but without the word he does not break. And if he swore that he will not buy it for ten, then bought it for eleven, he would break the oath. And its full discussion is in al-Jami' al-Saghir and its commentary by al-Farsi. Commentary: Oaths depend on the customary meaning of words. If there is no custom, then the literal meaning is used. Oaths do not depend on purposes and intention. However, if the word is capable of that meaning and he intends it, then it can be based on intention. 'Oaths are built upon words, not upon purposes' and under it in Radd al-Muhtar: i.e., upon purposes and intentions; he refrained from saying they are built upon intention. (Shami vol.5 p.?) So if someone swore in a story: 'I will not buy anything for you for one [unit]', then he bought something for a hundred dirhams, he does not break the oath because oaths depend on words, and he swore not to buy for one, not for a hundred, as is clarified in Shami.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental rule: oaths are interpreted based on the literal or customary meaning of the words used, not on the swearer's hidden purposes or motives. Several examples illustrate this: swearing not to buy for a small amount and buying for a large amount does not break the oath; swearing not to sell for a specific price and selling for a lower or higher price does not break the oath unless the wording explicitly includes that price. However, if the wording is specific (like 'I will not buy it for ten') and he buys for more (eleven), the oath is broken because the word 'for ten' is violated. The commentary in Radd al-Muhtar clarifies that this rule does not negate consideration of intention when the word can bear the intended meaning; it only rejects basing oaths solely on hidden motives.

Key Terms
الأيمان (al-aymaan): Oaths; solemn affirmations by God or divorce/emancipation.
الأغراض (al-aghraad): Purposes, aims, inner motives behind the oath.
حَنِثَ (hanitha): Broken the oath; liable for penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man swears, 'I will not give anything to Zaida for one dirham.' He later gives Zaida a gift worth 100 dirhams. According to this maxim, has he broken his oath?
A) Yes, because his purpose was not to give anything, and he gave a valuable gift.
B) Yes, because 100 dirhams includes one dirham.
C) No, because the oath specifically mentioned 'for one dirham', not any amount.
D) No, because the gift is not a sale.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'al-aymaan mabniyyah ala al-alfaz la al-aghrad' requires that oath breaches be determined solely by the literal or customary meaning of the wording, not the swearer's hidden purpose, with a limited exception when the word is ambiguous and intention is explicit.
