6 min
Oaths Are Based on Words, Not Intentions
Statement of maxim on oaths with examples and commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim that oaths are based on words, not intentions, to determine when an oath is broken in specific scenarios.

Core Idea
An oath is judged by its literal wording, not the swearer's inner objective.

In Hanafi law, the general rule 'matters are judged by intentions' (al-umur bi maqasidiha) applies broadly. However, in the chapter of oaths (al-ayman), a specific sub-maxim (dabt) takes precedence: oaths are determined by the words uttered, not by the swearer's customary objectives. This lesson unpacks that maxim, explains its three key applications, and clarifies when intention may still be considered.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Read the Arabic maxim 'الأَيْمَانُ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى الأَلْفَاظِ لَا عَلَى الْأَعْرَاضِ'. Understand that it is a sub-maxim (dabt) that restricts the general principle of intention.
2
Identify the scope
Note that this maxim governs the fiqh chapter of oaths (al-ayman). Outside this chapter, the general intention-based rule applies.
3
Apply to the first two furuat
For example: if one swears not to buy for a fils (a tiny amount), but buys for a huge sum, the oath is not broken because the wording specified 'fils', not the amount. Similarly, swearing not to sell for ten does not break if sold for eleven or nine; the wording is 'ten' exactly.
The key is strict correspondence of the uttered amount.
4
Apply to the third furu
If one swears not to buy for ten, and buys for eleven, the oath is broken because buying for eleven includes the price 'ten' plus one; the condition 'not for ten' is violated.
Any amount equal to or greater than the named price can trigger hanath if the wording implies 'for that amount or more'.
5
Recognize the exception
If the word used has a probable meaning (e.g., ambiguous) and the swearer intended that specific meaning, intention can be considered. This is the istithna' (exception).
This brings back the general rule of intention for ambiguous expressions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَاعِدَةٌ فِيْهَا أَيْضًا: الأَيْمَانُ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى الأَلْفَاظِ لَا عَلَى الْأَعْرَاضِ، فَلَوْ اغْتَاظَ مِنْ إِنْسَانٍ فَحَلَفَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَشْتَرِي لَهُ شَيْئًا بِفَلْسٍ، فَاشْتَرَى لَهُ شَيْئًا بِمِائَةِ دِرْهَمٍ لَمْ يَحْنَثْ. وَلَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يَبِيعُهُ بِعَشَرَةٍ، فَبَاعَهُ بِأَحَدَ عَشَرَ، أَوْ بِتِسْعَةٍ لَمْ يَحْنَثْ مَعَ أَنَّ غَرَضَهُ الزِّيَادَةَ الْكُبْرَى لَكِنْ لَا حِنْثَ بِلَا لَفْظٍ. وَلَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يَشْتَرِيهِ بِعَشْرٍ، فَاشْتَرَاهُ بِأَحَدَ عَشَرَ حَنِثَ. وَتَمَامُهُ فِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ وَشَرْحِهِ لِلْفَارِسِيِّ. 

ترجمه: ایمان سے متعلق ہی قاعدہ ہے کہ ایمان الفاظ پر مبنی ہوتی ہیں اغراض و مقاصد پر نہیں۔ پس اگر کسی انسان سے غصہ ہو کر قسم کھائی کہ وہ اس کے لئے ایک پیسہ کی چیز نہیں خریدے گا، پھر اس نے اس کے لئے سو درہم کی کوئی چیز خرید لی تو وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ (کوئی سامان) اسے دس میں نہیں بیچے گا، پھر اس نے (وہ سامان) اسے گیارہ میں یا نو میں فروخت کر دیا تو وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا، باوجود اس کے کہ اس کا مقصد زیادہ میں فروخت کرنا تھا، لیکن بغیر لفظ کے وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ اسے دس میں نہیں خریدے گا، پھر اس نے گیارہ میں خرید لیا تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کی پوری بحث جامع صغیر اور علامہ فارسی کی شرح میں ہے۔

تشریح: یمین کا دار و مدار الفاظ کے عرفی معنی پر ہوتا ہے، اور اگر عرف ہی نہ ہو تو حقیقی معنی پر۔ مقاصد اور نیت پر یمین کا دار و مدار نہیں ہوتا، ہاں البتہ اگر وہ لفظ جس معنی کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور حلف قَصَدَ ذٰلِکَ الْمَعْنَى فَتَصِحُّ نِیَّتُهُ۔

الإيمان مبنية على الألفاظ لا على الأغراض. وتحته في رد المحتار: أي على المقاصد والنيات. احترز به عن القول ببنائها على النية.

فلو احتاظ: اگر کسی نے غصہ میں قسم کھائی... الخ 

فَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ إِذَا حَلَفَ لَا يَشْتَرِي لِإِنْسَانٍ بِفَلْسٍ، فَإِذَا اشْتَرَى لَهُ شَيْئًا بِدِرْهَمٍ لَا يَحْنَثُ، وَإِنْ كَانَ الْغَرَضُ عُرْفًا أَنْ لَا يَشْتَرِيَ أَيْضًا بِدِرْهَمٍ وَلا غَيْرِهِ (شامی ج۵، ص:۵۲۹).

ولو حلف لا يبيعُه: اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ اپنا سامان دس درہم میں نہیں بیچے گا، پھر اس نے گیارہ میں یا نو میں فروخت کر دیا تو قسم کھانے والا حانث نہ ہوگا اگر چہ اس کی غرض مزید بڑھا کر بیچنے کی تھی لیکن قاعدہ گزر چکا ہے کہ یمین کا مدار لفظ پر ہے نہ کہ غرض و مقصد پر۔ ولا يحنث بالغرض بلا مسمى (شامی ج۵، ص:۵۲۹)

ولو حلف لا يشتريه: اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ اس سامان کو دس درہم میں نہیں خریدے گا، پھر گیارہ میں وہ چیز اس نے خرید لی تو حانث ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس نے دس اور زیادتی کے ساتھ خریدا ہے اور زیادتی حنث سے مانع نہیں ہوگی۔ ولو حلف لا يشريه بعشرة حنث باحد عشر .. لأن مراد المطلق (شامی ج۵، ص:۵۳۹)
A rule also concerning oaths: Oaths are based on words, not objectives. So if someone got angry at a person and swore that he would not buy anything for him for a fils, then bought something for him for a hundred dirhams, he does not break his oath. If he swore that he would not sell it for ten, then sold it for eleven or nine, he does not break his oath, even though his aim was a greater increase, but there is no breaking without [matching] the word. If he swore not to buy it for ten, then bought it for eleven, he breaks his oath. The complete discussion is in al-Jami' al-Saghir and its commentary by al-Farisi. Translation: A rule concerning oaths: oaths are based on words, not aims and objectives. So if... (Urdu translation of above). Explanation: An oath depends on the customary meaning of words, and if there is no custom, then on the literal meaning. It does not depend on aims and intentions. However, if the word has a probable meaning and the swearer intends that meaning, then his intention is valid. Oaths are based on words, not objectives. In Radd al-Mukhtar: i.e., on aims and intentions; it refrains from the opinion that they are based on intention. So if someone swore in anger... Know that if someone swears not to buy for a person for a fils, and then buys something for a dirham, he does not break his oath, even if the customary objective was also not to buy for a dirham or anything else (Shami 5:529). If he swore not to sell it: If someone swore not to sell his goods for ten dirhams, then sold it for eleven or nine, the swearer does not break his oath, even if his aim was to sell at a higher price; but the rule has passed that an oath depends on the word, not on aim and objective. And he does not break [the oath] by an objective without a name (Shami 5:529). If he swore not to buy it: If someone swore not to buy that item for ten dirhams, then he bought it for eleven, he breaks his oath because he bought it with ten and an increase, and an increase does not prevent breaking the oath. And if he swore not to buy it for ten, he breaks if [bought] for eleven, because the absolute purchase is intended (Shami 5:539).
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage presents a key Hanafi principle in the chapter of oaths (al-ayman): oaths are interpreted based on the literal wording used, not on the swearer's inner intention or customary objectives. This is an exception to the general maxim 'matters are judged by intentions' (al-umur bi maqasidiha) in the context of oaths. The text provides three examples: (1) If someone swears not to buy something for a fils (a small coin), but then buys it for a hundred dirhams, the oath is not broken because the wording specified 'a fils', not a large amount. (2) If someone swears not to sell for ten, but sells for eleven or nine, the oath is not broken because the wording specified exactly ten. (3) If someone swears not to buy for ten, and then buys for eleven, the oath is broken because buying for eleven includes the ten plus one. The reason is that when the swearer says 'not for ten,' it implies any price including ten; buying for eleven means he bought for ten and an extra one, so he fulfilled the condition. The commentary from Radd al-Mukhtar clarifies that this principle is specifically about oaths being based on explicit words to distinguish from the view that oaths are based on intention. However, there is a nuance: if the word has a probable meaning and the swearer intends that meaning, his intention is considered. But the default is that the customary or literal meaning applies.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): An oath or swearing by God or by divorce/emancipation, legally binding.
حنث (hanath): Breaking an oath; the state of having violated an oath, incurring expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man swears, 'I will not buy anything for Zaid for one dirham.' He then buys a book for Zaid for a thousand dirhams. According to the Hanafi maxim on oaths, what is the ruling?
A) He broke his oath because his intention was not to spend on Zaid.
B) He did not break his oath because the wording specified 'one dirham' and he spent a thousand.
C) He broke his oath because the amount is greater, so it counts as a purchase.
D) He is not liable because the oath was made in anger.

Key Takeaway
An oath is determined by its precise words, not the swearer's inner aim; this is a key exception to the general intention-based maxim in Hanafi law.

Oaths: Literal Wording over Hidden Intention
Explaining the rule that oaths are based on literal wording, not intent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that in oaths, literal wording (lafz) governs over hidden intention, and identify when and how this affects fatwa determination.

Core Idea
In oaths, the literal wording determines the ruling, not the secret intent.

In the Hanafi school, the principle 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' means actions are judged by intentions. However, in matters of oaths (yamin), this principle is restricted: the literal wording of the oath is the decisive factor. The hidden intention (gharad) does not override the plain meaning. This lesson examines a furu' on this rule, where the mufti must rely on the lafz rather than customary understanding. Let's see how it works.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida
Identify the maxim about oaths from the passage: in oaths, the literal wording (lafz) is followed, not the intention or customary meaning.
This is a furu' of the broader maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' but with an inversion: here lafz dominates.
2
Analyze furu' 1
A man swears not to buy for another with a fals (a coin). He buys with a dirham. The oath is not broken. Why? Because the lafz specified 'fals', and a dirham is not a fals, regardless of customary expectation.
The literal wording was the only binding element.
3
Analyze furu' 2
A man swears not to buy an item for ten dirhams. He buys for eleven. The oath is broken. Why? Because the lafz 'for ten' is understood as 'for ten or any amount', since the intent is absolute (muttalaq).
Buying for more is included under the general prohibition.
4
Extract the illa
The underlying reason is that oaths are tied to specific wordings, and those wordings are given literal effect unless a clear intention to the contrary is expressed. Customary understanding (urf) does not override the literal lafz.
This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
5
Apply to a new case
Given the rule, test a new scenario: A man swears not to enter Zayd's house for a dirham, but he enters for a dollar. Apply the rule to decide if the oath is broken.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاعلم انه إذا حلف لايشترى لانسان بفلس ...... فإذا إشترى له شيئاً بدرهم لا يحنث و إن كان الغرض عرفا ان لا يشترى أيضا بدرهم ولاغیره. ولو حلف لايشتريه: إذا اشترى بأكثر من ذلك حنث. ولو حلف لا يشريه بعشرة حنث بأحد عشر لأن مراد المشترى المطلقة.
Know that if one swears not to buy for a person with a fals [a coin]... then if he buys something for a dirham, he does not break his oath, even if the customary intent was not to buy even for a dirham or more. And if he swears not to buy it, and he buys it for more than that, he breaks his oath. And if he swears not to buy it for ten, and he buys it for eleven, he breaks his oath, because the buyer's intent is absolute.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage illustrates a specific qa'ida from the Hanafi school: in matters of oaths (yamin), the literal wording (lafz) is the determinant, not the hidden intention (gharad) or the customary understanding (urf). This is a furu' of the broader maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha', but here the rule is inverted: in oaths, the literal meaning is given priority unless there is a clear intention to the contrary. The first example: a man swears not to buy something for someone else for a fals (a small coin), but then buys it for a dirham – the oath is not broken because the literal wording specified 'fals', not 'dirham'. The second example: if one swears not to buy a specific item for ten dirhams, but then buys it for eleven, the oath is broken because buying for more is still included under the general prohibition. This shows that the wording 'for ten' means 'for ten or more', as the buyer's intent is absolute (muttalqa). This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, as found in al-Shami.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): An oath by Allah or by divorce/manumission to do or not do something.
لفظ (lafz): Literal wording or utterance.
غرض (gharad): Hidden intention or purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person swears, 'I will not buy this book for five dirhams,' and buys it for six dirhams, does he break his oath?
A) No, because he bought it for more than five.
B) Yes, because buying for six is still buying, and the wording 'for five' implies any amount.
C) No, because his intention was to not buy for five specifically.
D) Yes, only if he intended to break the oath.

Key Takeaway
The literal wording of an oath determines its legal effect; hidden intention does not override the lafz without a separate indication.

Calling by Name: Intention Determines Legal Effect
First branch: calling by name

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to determine whether calling a spouse or slave by a name that is also a legal term results in a legal consequence.

Core Idea
The same utterance can be a legal action or mere address — intention alone decides.

The first branch in the passage shows how the maxim works in its simplest form. A wife named Taliq or a slave named Hurrah is called by name. Whether divorce or manumission occurs depends entirely on what the speaker intended. This lesson unpacks that principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance and its potential meanings
The utterance 'Ya Taliq' can be a mere call or a divorce pronouncement. The word 'Taliq' is ambiguous.
The same ambiguity exists for 'Hurrah'.
2
Apply the maxim: intention is key
According to 'al-umur bi maqasidiha', the legal outcome hinges on the speaker's niyya. If he intended divorce/emancipation, it takes effect; if not, it is just a name.
If no intention (mutlaq), the relied-upon view is non-occurrence.
3
Consider the default rule when intention is unclear
In court, the judge cannot know the inner intention; the default is that the utterance does not count as talaq or itq unless evidence indicates otherwise.
This protects against frivolous litigation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع لو كان اسمها طالقا أو حرة، فناداها إن قصد الطلاق، أو العتق وقعا، أو النداء فلا، أو أطلق فالمعتمد عدمه. ولو كرر لفظ الطلاق، فإن قصد الاستيناف وقع الكل، أو التأكيد فواحدة ديانه، والكل قضاء، وكذا إذا أطلق. ولو قال أنت طالق واحدة في اثنتين فإن نوى مع اثنتين فثلاث دخل بها أو لا، وإلا فإن نوى و اثنتين فثلاث إن كان دخل بها وإلا فواحدة، كما إذا نوى الظرف أو أطلق. ولو نوى الضرب والحساب فكذلك، وكذا في الإقرار. ولو قال: أنت على مثل أمي، أو كأمي رجع إلى قصده لينكشف حكمه، فإن قال: أردت الكرامة فهو كما قال لأن التكريم بالتشبيه فاش في الكلام، وإن قال: أردت الظهار فهو ظهار، لأنه تشبيه بجميعها. وإن قال: أردت الطلاق فهو طلاق بائن، وإن لم تكن له نية، فليس بشيء عندهما، وقال محمد: هو ظهار، وإن عنى به التحريم لا غير، فعند أبي يوسف إيلاء وعند محمد ظهار.
Branches: If her name is Taliq or Hurrah, and he calls her, if he intended divorce or manumission, they take effect; if he intended mere calling, they do not; or if he was absolute (no intention), the relied-upon view is non-occurrence. And if he repeated the word 'talaq', if he intended fresh (initiation), all count; if he intended emphasis, then only one in conscience, but all in court; likewise if he was absolute. And if he said, 'You are divorced one in two', then if he intended 'with two', then three, whether he has consummated or not; otherwise if he intended 'and two', then three if consummated, otherwise one; just as if he intended the container (zarf) or was absolute. And if he intended multiplication and calculation, it is the same; similarly in acknowledgment. And if he said, 'You are like my mother' or 'like my mother', reference is made to his intent to uncover its ruling. If he said, 'I intended honor', then it is as he says, because honoring by similitude is common in speech. If he said, 'I intended zihar', then it is zihar, because it is a similitude of her entire body. If he said, 'I intended divorce', then it is a bain divorce. If he had no intention, then it is nothing according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: it is zihar. And if he meant prohibition only, then according to Abu Yusuf it is ila', and according to Muhammad it is zihar.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a collection of multiple furu' (branches) that illustrate the fundamental Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions). The first scenario: a wife named Taliq or a slave girl named Hurrah. When the husband/master calls her by that name, the legal effect depends solely on his intention. If he intended divorce or manumission, it takes effect. If he intended only to call her, it does not. If he had no specific intention (mutlaq), the relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is that nothing occurs. This shows that the same utterance can have different effects based on niyya. The second scenario: repetition of the word 'talaq'. If one says 'talaq' repeatedly intending to initiate separate divorces (istinaf), all count. If intending emphasis (ta'kid), only one divorce occurs diyanatan (in conscience), but qada'an (in court) all are enforced because the court cannot know the inner intention. This is a practical compromise. The third scenario: the phrase 'you are divorced one in two'. This contains the word 'fi' (in) which can mean 'with' (ma'a) or 'in' (zarf). The ruling varies based on intention: if he intends 'with two', then three divorces occur (one + two = three); if he intends 'and two' (waw), then three if consummated, else one; if he intends container (zarf) or is absolute, then one divorce. This is for a wife who has been consummated; if not, the rules of bain apply. The fourth scenario: saying 'you are like my mother' or 'like my mother'. This is a famous example of how intention determines whether it is zihar, divorce, or mere honor. The default presumption is that it is a form of honor (tikram) because similitudes for honor are common. But if the speaker clarifies his intent, it takes the corresponding ruling. The ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: if he only intended prohibition (tahrim), Abu Yusuf says it is ila' (an oath of abstinence), while Muhammad says it is zihar. The Hanafi school generally follows Abu Yusuf's view in this detail.

Key Terms
نيّة (niyya): The speaker's inner intention that determines the legal effect of an utterance.
طلاق (talāq): The husband's pronouncement of divorce, which can be effective or not based on intention.
عتق (itq): Manumission of a slave, also dependent on intention in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man has a slave-girl named 'Ḥurrah'. He calls her 'Yā Ḥurrah' intending only to get her attention. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling?
A) She is freed because the word 'Ḥurrah' means free woman.
B) She is not freed because the master did not intend manumission.
C) She is freed only if the master later admits intention.
D) The matter is ambiguous; a judge must decide.

Key Takeaway
When a word that could be a legal term is also a name, the speaker's intention determines whether a legal effect occurs.

Repetition of Talaq: Fresh vs Emphasis
Second branch: repetition of talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between repeating talaq for emphasis vs. initiating new divorces, and state the resulting ruling both diyanatan and qada'an.

Core Idea
Repeating 'talaq' can be one divorce emphasized or multiple divorces — inner intention differs from court enforcement.

When a husband repeats the word 'talaq' multiple times, the legal outcome depends on his intention. If he meant to emphasize one divorce, only one occurs in his conscience, but a court must enforce all utterances. This lesson explains the practical difference between diyanatan (inner) and qada'an (judicial) rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible intentions
The husband may intend either to confirm a single divorce (emphasis) or to pronounce separate divorces (istinaf).
The word 'talaq' is ambiguous when repeated.
2
Apply the maxim diyanatan
According to 'al-umur bi maqasidiha', if he intended emphasis, only one divorce is effective in his conscience before Allah.
This is because the second utterance was not a new divorce.
3
Apply the qada' rule
In court, the judge cannot know the inner intention. The external words are taken at face value: all repetitions count as separate divorces.
This is a practical necessity to avoid perjury and to maintain legal certainty.
4
Determine the result when intention is unknown
If the husband is silent about his intention (mutlaq), the ruling follows the same pattern: diyanatan one divorce, qada'an all repetitions count.
This is the relied-upon position.

اِسْتِينَاف (istīnāf): To start anew; here, to initiate a fresh divorce rather than emphasize a previous one.
تَأْكِيد (ta'kīd): Emphasis or confirmation, not a new action.

A) Two divorces are enforced.

C) The court must ask his intention.
D) The utterance is invalid because ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
Intention governs the inner reality of repeated talaq, but the court enforces all utterances to maintain legal certainty.

Intention in Ila' and Zihar: The Case of 'Like My Mother'
Fourth branch: 'like my mother' and similar utterances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the utterance 'anti 'ala mithli ummi' into different legal categories (zihar, divorce, ila', honor) based on the speaker's intention, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
The same phrase can be honor, zihar, divorce, or ila' — intention alone determines which ruling applies.

The last branch in the passage presents a multifaceted scenario: a husband says to his wife 'You are like my mother' or 'like my mother'. This utterance can be purely honorific, a declaration of zihar, a divorce, or an oath of ila' (abstinence). The Hanafi school gives decisive weight to the husband's stated intention. Additionally, there is an internal Hanafi dispute when he intends mere prohibition (tahrim): Abu Yusuf considers it ila', while Muhammad considers it zihar. This lesson unpacks the logic of each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the possible intentions
The husband may have intended honor (karamah), zihar (similitude to a mahram), divorce (talaq), or mere prohibition (tahrim without specifying).
Each intention leads to a different legal consequence.
2
Apply the maxim: his stated intention is accepted
If he claims he intended honor, it is accepted because such similitudes are common in speech. If he claims zihar or divorce, it is taken as such.
The default presumption, if no intention is stated, is honor (so nothing occurs according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
3
Analyze the dispute on 'tahrim' intention
If he intended only prohibition (i.e., to make her haram like his mother through oath), Abu Yusuf says it is ila' (an oath to abstain), while Muhammad says it is zihar (because the similitude is explicit).
The relied-upon view in the school is Abu Yusuf's (ila').
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If it is ila', the husband must either resume relations within four months or face divorce by the judge. If it is zihar, he must perform expiation (kaffarah) before resuming relations.
The consequences for the couple are very different.

تحريم (tahrim): Merely intending to make something forbidden, without specifying the legal mechanism.

A husband says 'You are like my mother' and later says he intended only to make her forbidden to him (tahrim) without specifying further. According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling?
A) It is zihar.
B) It is ila'.
C) It is a bain divorce.
D) It is nothing; the intention is not sufficient.

Key Takeaway
When a husband uses a simile that could be honor, zihar, divorce, or ila', his stated intention determines the ruling, with the default being honor.

8 min
Intention in Ambiguous Divorce Utterances: The 'fi' Case
Analysis of 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for interpreting 'fi' in talaq phrases and identify the ikhtilaf with Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
When a husband says 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn', his intention determines the number of divorces.

Ambiguous words in divorce require careful investigation of the speaker's intention. This lesson focuses on the phrase 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn' where the word 'fi' can mean 'with', 'and', or 'in'. Understanding how the Hanafi school resolves this ambiguity is essential for a mufti when issuing fatwas on talaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous phrase
The husband says 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn'. The word 'fi' is ambiguous—it could mean 'with' (ma‘a), 'and' (waw), 'in' (zarf), or 'multiplication' (darb).
The ruling changes drastically based on the intended meaning.
2
Determine the husband's intention
Ask the husband what he intended. If he intended 'with two' (مع اثنتين), the result is three divorces regardless of consummation. If he intended 'and two' (واثنتين), it is three divorces if consummated, otherwise one ba'in divorce.
If he had no specific intention, the default is 'in' (zarf), yielding three divorces.
3
Apply the rule for multiplication intention
If he intended multiplication (ضرب) and calculation (حساب), the apparent madhhab (Abu Hanifa) says one divorce. Imam Zufar says two divorces, which Ibn Hammam preferred.
The mufti should follow the tarjih: two divorces according to the stronger view.
4
Consider the wife's status
These rulings apply to a consummated wife (madkhul biha). For a non-consummated wife, the first divorce makes her ba'in, and subsequent pronouncements are void.
This is an exception mentioned at the start of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و كذا أطلق القط طلاق کے تکرار میں اگر نہ استناف کا ارادہ ہے اور نہ تاکید کا تو اس صورت میں تھی طلاق واقع ہوں گی کذا کے لفظ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تین طلاق واقع ہوں گی یہ سب صورتیں یہ خولہ عورت کے بارے میں ہے ورنہ غیر مدخولہ پہلی طلاق سے باسکے ہو جائے گی دوسری اور تیسری طلاق لغو قرار پائے گی۔
وَلَوْ قَالَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ وَاحِدَةٌ فِي ثِنْتَيْنِ فَإِنْ نَوَىٰ مَعَ ثِنْتَيْنِ فَثَلَاثِ، دَخَلَ بِهَا أَوْلَا، وَإِلَّا فَإِنْ نَوَى وَ ثِنْتَيْنِ فَتَلْتُ إِنْ كَانَ دَخَلَ بِهَا وَ إِلَّا فَوَاحِدَةٌ، كَمَا إِذَا نَوَى الطَّرْفَ أَوْ أَطْلَقَ، وَلَوْ نَوَى الضَّرْبَ وَالْحِسَابَ فَكَذَلِكَ، وَ كَذَا فِي الإِقْرَارِ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر کہا تجھے ایک طلاق دو میں پس اگر نیت کی دو کے ساتھ تو تین واقع ہوگی ذخول ہوا ہو یا نہ ہوا ہورنہ ایک جیسے اگر ظرف کی نیت کی ہو یا مطلق کہا ہوا گر ضرب و حساب مراد ہوتب بھی یہی حکم ہے اور اسی طرح اقرار میں بھی ۔ تشریح : اگر کوئی شخص اپنی بیوی سے انت طالق واحدۃ فی نشتین کے تو یہاں فی والا اور مع دونوں کا احتال رکھتا ہے اب اگر مع کے معنی لئے تو ہیوی مدخول بہا ہو یا غیر مدخول بہا دونوں صورتوں میں طلاق مغلظہ واقع ہو جائے گی اور اگر واؤ کے معنی مراد لئے توبیوی کے مدخولہ ہونے کی صورت میں تینوں طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور غیر مدخول ہونے کی صورت میں ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی اس ضمن میں دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ظرف کی نیت کی یا نیت کو مطلق رکھا تو مدخولہ اور غیر مدخولہ ہر ایک پر سیاری طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی تو ظاہر مذہب کے مطابق ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی اور امام زفر کے نزدیک دو طلاق واقع ہوں گی علامہ ابن ہمام نے امام زیر کے قول کو تر جیح دی ہے۔
وَلَوْ قَالَ: أَنْتَ عَلى مِثْلَ أُمِّي، أَوْ كَامّى رَجَعَ إِلى قَصْدِهِ لِيَنْكَشِفَ حُكْمُهُ، فَإِنْ قَالَ: أردت الكرامَةَ، فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ لأن التكريم بالتشبِيْهِ فَاش فِي الْكَلَامِ وَ إِنْ قَالَ أَرَتُ الطَّهَارَ فَهُوَ ظِهَارٌ ، لأَنَّهُ تَشْبِيْة بِجَمِيعِهَا. وَإِنْ قَالَ : أَرَدْتُ الطَّلَاقِ، فَهُوَ طَلَاقَ بَائِنٌ، وَ إِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ لَهُ نِيَّةٌ، فَلَيْسَ بِشَيْ عِنْدَهُمَا، وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ: هُوَ ظِهَارٌ، وَ إِنْ عَنِى بِهِ التَّحْرِيْمَ لَا غَيْرَ ، فَعِنْدَ أَبي يُوْسُفَ إِيْلَاء وَ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ ظِهَارٌ .

تا کہ تنقیح کے بعد حکم لگایا جا سکے اگر قائل کہتا ہے کہ میری مراد اس جملہ سے تعظیم و تکریم ہے تو سبحان اللہ کیونکہ یہ الفاظ تشریح: اگر سی نے اپنی بیوی سے انت علی مثل امی کہا یا کامی تو قاتل سے معلوم کیا جائے گا کہ مقصد کیا ہے تو ظہار کا تھا تو ظہار ہی ہوگا کیونکہ ظہار تو نام ہی ہے اپنی بیوی کو ماں یا ماں کی طرح محرمات موجدہ میں سے کسی کے تعظیم و تکریم میں تشبیہ کے لئے مستعمل ہوتے ہیں اس کی نیت پر ہی فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا اور اگر متکلم یہ کہے کہ میرا مقصد ساتھ تشبیہ دینے کا اور یہاں پورے بدن کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی گئی ہے۔
کے نزدیک ایلاء اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ظہار پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر متکلم کہے کہ میرا مقصد طلاق تھا تو طلاق بائن مراد ہوگی اور مطلق رکھتا ہے کچھ نیت نہیں ہے تو امام یوسف
وَلَوْ قَالَ أَنْتَ عَلَيَّ حَرَامٌ كَأَمِّي، وَنَوَى ظِهَاراً، أَوْ طَلَاقَا فَهُوَ عَلَى مَا نَوَى، وَ إِنْ لَمْ يَنْوِ، فَعَلى قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ إِبْلَاءٌ، وَعَلَى قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ ظِهَارٌ. وَ مِنْهَا لَوْ قَرَأَ الْجُنُبُ قُرْآنًا، فَإِنْ قصَدَ الثَّلَاوَةَ حَرُمَ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ الذِّكْرَ فَلَا وَلَوْ قَرَأَ الْفَاتِحَةُ فِي صَلَاتِهِ عَلَى الْجَنَازَةِ، إِنْ فَصَدَ الدُّعَاءَ وَ الثَّناءَ لَمْ يَكْرَهُ ، وَ إِنْ قَصَدَ التَّلَاوَةَ كَرِهَ عَطَسَ الْخَطِيْبُ، فَقَالَ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، إِنْ قَصَدَ الْخُطْبَة صَحَّتْ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ الْحَمْدَ لِلْعُطَاسِ لَمْ تَصِحْ ذَبَحَ فَعَطَسَ، فَسَدَتَ وَ إِلَّا فَلَا. وَقَالَ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، فَكَذلِكَ ذَكَرَ الْمُصَلَّى آيَةً، أَوْ ذِكْراً، وَقَصَدَ بِهِ جَوَابَ الْمُتَكَلِّمِ
ترجمه : اور اگر کہا انت علی حرام کامی اور نیت ظہار کی یا طلاق کی ہو تو وہ اس کی نیت کے مطابق ہے اور اگر اس نے کوئی بھی نیت نہ کی تو ابو یوسف کے قول کے مطابق ایلاء اور امام محمد کے قول کے مطابق ظہار ہے اور ان ہی جزئیات میں سے ہے کہ اگر نبی نے قرآن پڑھا تو اگر وہ تلاوت کا ارادہ کرے تو حرام ہے اور اگر ذکر کا ارادہ ہو تو حرام نہیں اور اگر نماز جنازہ میں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھی تو اگر دعا وثناء کا ارادہ ہو تو مکر وہ نہیں اور اگر تلاوت کا ارادہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے خطیب کو چھینک آئی اس پر اس نے کہا الحمدللہ تو اگر خطبہ کا ارادہ کیا تو خطبہ درست ہے اور اگر اس نے چھینک پر اللہ کی تعریف کا ارادہ کیا تو خطبہ درست نہیں ذبح کرتے وقت چھینک آئی اور اس نے الحمد للہ کہا تو بھی یہی تفصیل ہے نماز کی
حالت میں اس نے کوئی آیت پڑھی یا ذ کر کیا اور اس سے متکلم کا جواب دینا مقصود ہے تو نماز فاسد ہے ورنہ نہیں۔
And like that, absolvic the repetition of talaq if neither the intention of renewal nor emphasis, then in that case three talaqs occur. It is known from the word 'kadha' that three talaqs occur. All these cases are about a khula woman; otherwise for a non-consummated woman, the first talaq makes her separate, the second and third are void. And if he said: 'You are divorced one in two', then if he intended 'with two', then three occur whether he consummated or not; otherwise if he intended 'and two', then three if he consummated, otherwise one. Similarly if he intended 'in' or absolute, and if he intended 'multiplication and calculation', similarly. And likewise in acknowledgment. Translation: And if he said: 'You are divorced one in two', then if he intended 'with two', then three occur whether consummated or not; otherwise if he intended 'and two', then three if consummated, otherwise one. Similarly if he intended 'in' or absolute, and if he intended 'multiplication and calculation', similarly. And likewise in acknowledgment. Explanation: If a person says to his wife 'you are divorced one in two', here the word 'fi' can mean both 'with' and 'in'. Now if he takes the meaning of 'with' then whether the wife is consummated or not, a severe talaq occurs. If he intends the meaning of 'and' then if the wife is consummated, three talaqs occur, and if not consummated, one ba'in talaq occurs. Within this, the second issue: if he intended 'in' or kept the intention absolute, then for both consummated and non-consummated, three talaqs occur. Third issue: if he intended multiplication and calculation, then according to the apparent madhhab one talaq occurs, and according to Imam Zufar two talaqs occur. Allama Ibn Hammam preferred the view of Imam Zufar. And if he said: 'You are like my mother' or 'like her', recourse is made to his intent to uncover its ruling. If he said: 'I intended honor', then it is as he said because honor through simile is common in speech. If he said: 'I intended zihar', then it is zihar because it is a simile with all of her. If he said: 'I intended talaq', then it is ba'in talaq. If he had no intention, then it is nothing according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?). Muhammad said: it is zihar. And if he meant prohibition only, then according to Abu Yusuf it is ila, and according to Muhammad it is zihar. Translation: And if he said: 'You are upon me unlawful like my mother', and he intended zihar or talaq, then it is according to his intention. If he did not intend, then according to Abu Yusuf it is ila, and according to Muhammad it is zihar. And from these issues: if a junub reads Quran, if he intended recitation, it is haram; if he intended dhikr, then not. And if he recited Fatiha in the funeral prayer, if he intended supplication and praise, it is not disliked; if he intended recitation, it is disliked. The khateeb sneezed and said 'alhamdulillah'; if he intended the khutbah, it is valid; if he intended praise for the sneeze, it is not valid. While slaughtering he sneezed and said 'alhamdulillah' similarly. The one in prayer recited a verse or dhikr and intended to answer the speaker, then the prayer is invalid; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir applies the grand legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are by intentions) to specific cases in family law and worship. The author presents several scenarios where ambiguous words uttered by a husband or worshipper are interpreted according to the speaker's intention. The first set of cases involves the phrase 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn.' The word 'fi' can mean 'with' (ma'a) or 'in' (zarf). If the husband intended 'with two', three divorces occur regardless of consummation. If he intended 'and' (waw), then three divorces only if consummated; otherwise one ba'in divorce. If he made no specific intention or intended 'in' (zarf), three divorces occur. If he intended multiplication (darb) and calculation (hisab), the apparent madhhab (Abu Hanifa) says one divorce, but Imam Zufar says two. The second set deals with 'anti 'ala mithli ummi' or 'ka-ummi'. The husband's intention determines whether it is zihar, talaq, ila, or mere honorific. If he intended honor, it is taken as such. If he intended zihar, it is zihar (a form of divorce-like prohibition). If he intended talaq, it is a ba'in talaq. If he intended only prohibition, Abu Yusuf rules it as ila (an oath of abstinence), while Muhammad rules it as zihar. The third set extends the principle to acts of worship: a junub may read Quran if intending dhikr, not recitation; reciting Fatiha in janazah prayer is disliked if intended as recitation but not if as supplication; a khateeb's sneeze response is valid only if intended as part of the khutbah; and a prayer is invalid if the worshipper intends to answer someone with a verse or dhikr. These examples illustrate that intention is central in Hanafi fiqh for distinguishing between different legal categories.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The conscious intention in the heart that distinguishes between different legal categories of an utterance.
طلاق (talaq): Divorce; the dissolution of marriage by the husband's pronouncement.
ظرف (zarf): Adverb of place/time; in this context, 'in' meaning the divorce is placed within two.
ضرب (darb): Multiplication; used here as a possible interpretation of 'fi'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn' with the intention of 'and two' (waw). The wife is non-consummated. How many divorces occur?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
When 'fi' is ambiguous, the husband's intention determines the number of divorces; with no intention, three divorces occur.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
Intention in Zihar and Ila: The 'Ka-Ummi' Cases
Analysis of 'anti 'ala mithli ummi' and 'anti 'alayya haramun ka-ummi'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between zihar, talaq, ila, and honorific based on the husband's intention when saying 'anti 'ala mithli ummi' or 'anti 'alayya haramun ka-ummi'.

Core Idea
When a husband says 'you are like my mother' or 'unlawful like my mother', his intention alone determines the legal category.

Phrases likening a wife to a mahram woman are ambiguous and can be interpreted as zihar, talaq, ila, or mere honorific. This lesson examines how the Hanafi school resolves these cases by inquiring into the husband's intention. It also highlights the internal ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding no intention and prohibition-only intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance
The husband says either 'anti 'ala mithli ummi', 'anti ka-ummi', or 'anti 'alayya haramun ka-ummi'. All are ambiguous.
The ruling depends on what the husband intended.
2
Ask the husband's intention
If he says he intended honor (ikram), it is accepted and no legal effect. If he says zihar, it is zihar. If he says talaq, it is ba'in talaq.
If he says he intended only prohibition (tahrim), there is ikhtilaf.
3
Apply the ikhtilaf for no intention
If he has no intention at all, for 'anti 'ala mithli ummi', Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it is nothing, while Muhammad says it is zihar.
For 'anti 'alayya haramun ka-ummi', if no intention, Abu Yusuf says ila, Muhammad says zihar.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The text does not give a definitive tarjih, but the context suggests following Abu Yusuf for ila/zihar distinction. The mufti should investigate the husband's likely intent.
In practice, the mufta bihi often follows Abu Yusuf for ila and Muhammad for zihar, but careful inquiry is needed.

Source Text

وَلَوْ قَالَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ وَاحِدَةٌ فِي ثِنْتَيْنِ فَإِنْ نَوَىٰ مَعَ ثِنْتَيْنِ فَثَلَاثِ، دَخَلَ بِهَا أَوْلَا، وَإِلَّا فَإِنْ نَوَى وَ ثِنْتَيْنِ فَتَلْتُ إِنْ كَانَ دَخَلَ بِهَا وَ إِلَّا فَوَاحِدَةٌ، كَمَا إِذَا نَوَى الطَّرْفَ أَوْ أَطْلَقَ، وَلَوْ نَوَى الضَّرْبَ وَالْحِسَابَ فَكَذَلِكَ، وَ كَذَا فِي الإِقْرَارِ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر کہا تجھے ایک طلاق دو میں پس اگر نیت کی دو کے ساتھ تو تین واقع ہوگی ذخول ہوا ہو یا نہ ہوا ہورنہ ایک جیسے اگر ظرف کی نیت کی ہو یا مطلق کہا ہوا گر ضرب و حساب مراد ہوتب بھی یہی حکم ہے اور اسی طرح اقرار میں بھی ۔ تشریح : اگر کوئی شخص اپنی بیوی سے انت طالق واحدۃ فی نشتین کے تو یہاں فی والا اور مع دونوں کا احتال رکھتا ہے اب اگر مع کے معنی لئے تو ہیوی مدخول بہا ہو یا غیر مدخول بہا دونوں صورتوں میں طلاق مغلظہ واقع ہو جائے گی اور اگر واؤ کے معنی مراد لئے توبیوی کے مدخولہ ہونے کی صورت میں تینوں طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور غیر مدخول ہونے کی صورت میں ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی اس ضمن میں دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ظرف کی نیت کی یا نیت کو مطلق رکھا تو مدخولہ اور غیر مدخولہ ہر ایک پر سیاری طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی تو ظاہر مذہب کے مطابق ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی اور امام زفر کے نزدیک دو طلاق واقع ہوں گی علامہ ابن ہمام نے امام زیر کے قول کو تر جیح دی ہے۔
وَلَوْ قَالَ: أَنْتَ عَلى مِثْلَ أُمِّي، أَوْ كَامّى رَجَعَ إِلى قَصْدِهِ لِيَنْكَشِفَ حُكْمُهُ، فَإِنْ قَالَ: أردت الكرامَةَ، فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ لأن التكريم بالتشبِيْهِ فَاش فِي الْكَلَامِ وَ إِنْ قَالَ أَرَتُ الطَّهَارَ فَهُوَ ظِهَارٌ ، لأَنَّهُ تَشْبِيْة بِجَمِيعِهَا. وَإِنْ قَالَ : أَرَدْتُ الطَّلَاقِ، فَهُوَ طَلَاقَ بَائِنٌ، وَ إِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ لَهُ نِيَّةٌ، فَلَيْسَ بِشَيْ عِنْدَهُمَا، وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ: هُوَ ظِهَارٌ، وَ إِنْ عَنِى بِهِ التَّحْرِيْمَ لَا غَيْرَ ، فَعِنْدَ أَبي يُوْسُفَ إِيْلَاء وَ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ ظِهَارٌ .

تا کہ تنقیح کے بعد حکم لگایا جا سکے اگر قائل کہتا ہے کہ میری مراد اس جملہ سے تعظیم و تکریم ہے تو سبحان اللہ کیونکہ یہ الفاظ تشریح: اگر سی نے اپنی بیوی سے انت علی مثل امی کہا یا کامی تو قاتل سے معلوم کیا جائے گا کہ مقصد کیا ہے تو ظہار کا تھا تو ظہار ہی ہوگا کیونکہ ظہار تو نام ہی ہے اپنی بیوی کو ماں یا ماں کی طرح محرمات موجدہ میں سے کسی کے تعظیم و تکریم میں تشبیہ کے لئے مستعمل ہوتے ہیں اس کی نیت پر ہی فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا اور اگر متکلم یہ کہے کہ میرا مقصد ساتھ تشبیہ دینے کا اور یہاں پورے بدن کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی گئی ہے۔
کے نزدیک ایلاء اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ظہار پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر متکلم کہے کہ میرا مقصد طلاق تھا تو طلاق بائن مراد ہوگی اور مطلق رکھتا ہے کچھ نیت نہیں ہے تو امام یوسف
وَلَوْ قَالَ أَنْتَ عَلَيَّ حَرَامٌ كَأَمِّي، وَنَوَى ظِهَاراً، أَوْ طَلَاقَا فَهُوَ عَلَى مَا نَوَى، وَ إِنْ لَمْ يَنْوِ، فَعَلى قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ إِبْلَاءٌ، وَعَلَى قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ ظِهَارٌ. وَ مِنْهَا لَوْ قَرَأَ الْجُنُبُ قُرْآنًا، فَإِنْ قصَدَ الثَّلَاوَةَ حَرُمَ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ الذِّكْرَ فَلَا وَلَوْ قَرَأَ الْفَاتِحَةُ فِي صَلَاتِهِ عَلَى الْجَنَازَةِ، إِنْ فَصَدَ الدُّعَاءَ وَ الثَّناءَ لَمْ يَكْرَهُ ، وَ إِنْ قَصَدَ التَّلَاوَةَ كَرِهَ عَطَسَ الْخَطِيْبُ، فَقَالَ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، إِنْ قَصَدَ الْخُطْبَة صَحَّتْ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ الْحَمْدَ لِلْعُطَاسِ لَمْ تَصِحْ ذَبَحَ فَعَطَسَ، فَسَدَتَ وَ إِلَّا فَلَا. وَقَالَ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، فَكَذلِكَ ذَكَرَ الْمُصَلَّى آيَةً، أَوْ ذِكْراً، وَقَصَدَ بِهِ جَوَابَ الْمُتَكَلِّمِ
ترجمه : اور اگر کہا انت علی حرام کامی اور نیت ظہار کی یا طلاق کی ہو تو وہ اس کی نیت کے مطابق ہے اور اگر اس نے کوئی بھی نیت نہ کی تو ابو یوسف کے قول کے مطابق ایلاء اور امام محمد کے قول کے مطابق ظہار ہے اور ان ہی جزئیات میں سے ہے کہ اگر نبی نے قرآن پڑھا تو اگر وہ تلاوت کا ارادہ کرے تو حرام ہے اور اگر ذکر کا ارادہ ہو تو حرام نہیں اور اگر نماز جنازہ میں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھی تو اگر دعا وثناء کا ارادہ ہو تو مکر وہ نہیں اور اگر تلاوت کا ارادہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے خطیب کو چھینک آئی اس پر اس نے کہا الحمدللہ تو اگر خطبہ کا ارادہ کیا تو خطبہ درست ہے اور اگر اس نے چھینک پر اللہ کی تعریف کا ارادہ کیا تو خطبہ درست نہیں ذبح کرتے وقت چھینک آئی اور اس نے الحمد للہ کہا تو بھی یہی تفصیل ہے نماز کی
حالت میں اس نے کوئی آیت پڑھی یا ذ کر کیا اور اس سے متکلم کا جواب دینا مقصود ہے تو نماز فاسد ہے ورنہ نہیں۔
And like that, absolvic the repetition of talaq if neither the intention of renewal nor emphasis, then in that case three talaqs occur. It is known from the word 'kadha' that three talaqs occur. All these cases are about a khula woman; otherwise for a non-consummated woman, the first talaq makes her separate, the second and third are void. And if he said: 'You are divorced one in two', then if he intended 'with two', then three occur whether he consummated or not; otherwise if he intended 'and two', then three if he consummated, otherwise one. Similarly if he intended 'in' or absolute, and if he intended 'multiplication and calculation', similarly. And likewise in acknowledgment. Translation: And if he said: 'You are divorced one in two', then if he intended 'with two', then three occur whether consummated or not; otherwise if he intended 'and two', then three if consummated, otherwise one. Similarly if he intended 'in' or absolute, and if he intended 'multiplication and calculation', similarly. And likewise in acknowledgment. Explanation: If a person says to his wife 'you are divorced one in two', here the word 'fi' can mean both 'with' and 'in'. Now if he takes the meaning of 'with' then whether the wife is consummated or not, a severe talaq occurs. If he intends the meaning of 'and' then if the wife is consummated, three talaqs occur, and if not consummated, one ba'in talaq occurs. Within this, the second issue: if he intended 'in' or kept the intention absolute, then for both consummated and non-consummated, three talaqs occur. Third issue: if he intended multiplication and calculation, then according to the apparent madhhab one talaq occurs, and according to Imam Zufar two talaqs occur. Allama Ibn Hammam preferred the view of Imam Zufar. And if he said: 'You are like my mother' or 'like her', recourse is made to his intent to uncover its ruling. If he said: 'I intended honor', then it is as he said because honor through simile is common in speech. If he said: 'I intended zihar', then it is zihar because it is a simile with all of her. If he said: 'I intended talaq', then it is ba'in talaq. If he had no intention, then it is nothing according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?). Muhammad said: it is zihar. And if he meant prohibition only, then according to Abu Yusuf it is ila, and according to Muhammad it is zihar. Translation: And if he said: 'You are upon me unlawful like my mother', and he intended zihar or talaq, then it is according to his intention. If he did not intend, then according to Abu Yusuf it is ila, and according to Muhammad it is zihar. And from these issues: if a junub reads Quran, if he intended recitation, it is haram; if he intended dhikr, then not. And if he recited Fatiha in the funeral prayer, if he intended supplication and praise, it is not disliked; if he intended recitation, it is disliked. The khateeb sneezed and said 'alhamdulillah'; if he intended the khutbah, it is valid; if he intended praise for the sneeze, it is not valid. While slaughtering he sneezed and said 'alhamdulillah' similarly. The one in prayer recited a verse or dhikr and intended to answer the speaker, then the prayer is invalid; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir applies the grand legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are by intentions) to specific cases in family law and worship. The author presents several scenarios where ambiguous words uttered by a husband or worshipper are interpreted according to the speaker's intention. The first set of cases involves the phrase 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn.' The word 'fi' can mean 'with' (ma'a) or 'in' (zarf). If the husband intended 'with two', three divorces occur regardless of consummation. If he intended 'and' (waw), then three divorces only if consummated; otherwise one ba'in divorce. If he made no specific intention or intended 'in' (zarf), three divorces occur. If he intended multiplication (darb) and calculation (hisab), the apparent madhhab (Abu Hanifa) says one divorce, but Imam Zufar says two. The second set deals with 'anti 'ala mithli ummi' or 'ka-ummi'. The husband's intention determines whether it is zihar, talaq, ila, or mere honorific. If he intended honor, it is taken as such. If he intended zihar, it is zihar (a form of divorce-like prohibition). If he intended talaq, it is a ba'in talaq. If he intended only prohibition, Abu Yusuf rules it as ila (an oath of abstinence), while Muhammad rules it as zihar. The third set extends the principle to acts of worship: a junub may read Quran if intending dhikr, not recitation; reciting Fatiha in janazah prayer is disliked if intended as recitation but not if as supplication; a khateeb's sneeze response is valid only if intended as part of the khutbah; and a prayer is invalid if the worshipper intends to answer someone with a verse or dhikr. These examples illustrate that intention is central in Hanafi fiqh for distinguishing between different legal categories.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A husband likening his wife to a mahram woman, which results in a prohibition requiring kaffarah before resumption.
إيلاء (ila): An oath by the husband to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for four months or more, leading to automatic divorce if not resumed.
نية (niyyah): The conscious intention in the heart that distinguishes between different legal categories of an utterance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says 'anti 'ala mithli ummi' and later says he intended talaq. What is the ruling?
A) It is zihar.
B) It is ba'in talaq.
C) It is nothing.
D) It is ila.

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous phrases like 'ka-ummi', the husband's intention is decisive; without intention, the ruling varies among Hanafi imams.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
beginner
7 min
Intention in Acts of Worship: Junub, Janazah, Khutbah, and Prayer
Ibadat furuat applying the maxim of intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim of intention to distinguish between permissible and impermissible actions in acts of worship where the same verbal act can have different legal effects.

Core Idea
The same recitation can be haram or halal depending on whether one intends tilawah or dhikr.

The maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' extends beyond family law into ibadat. This lesson examines four cases: a junub reading Quran, reciting Fatiha in janazah prayer, a khateeb responding to a sneeze, and a worshiper answering someone during prayer. In each, the intention transforms the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the intention
The act is a verbal utterance that could serve two purposes (e.g., recitation vs. dhikr). The intention determines which category it falls into.
2
Apply the ruling for junub reading Quran
If a junub intends recitation (tilawah), it is haram. If he intends dhikr (remembrance), it is permissible.
The same words are either forbidden or permissible based on intent.
3
Apply the ruling for reciting Fatiha in janazah prayer
If he intends it as supplication and praise (du‘a’ wa thana'), it is not disliked. If he intends it as recitation (tilawah), it is disliked (makruh).
The difference is subtle; intent changes the ruling from makruh to not makruh.
4
Apply the ruling for khateeb sneezing
If the khateeb says 'alhamdulillah' intending it as part of the khutbah, the khutbah is valid. If he intends praise for the sneeze, the khutbah is invalid.
The same words can break the khutbah if the wrong intention is present.
5
Apply the ruling for a worshiper answering someone
If a worshiper during prayer recites a verse or dhikr intending to answer someone, the prayer is invalid. If he did not intend to answer, it remains valid.
Intent to communicate with others nullifies the prayer.

Source Text

و كذا أطلق القط طلاق کے تکرار میں اگر نہ استناف کا ارادہ ہے اور نہ تاکید کا تو اس صورت میں تھی طلاق واقع ہوں گی کذا کے لفظ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تین طلاق واقع ہوں گی یہ سب صورتیں یہ خولہ عورت کے بارے میں ہے ورنہ غیر مدخولہ پہلی طلاق سے باسکے ہو جائے گی دوسری اور تیسری طلاق لغو قرار پائے گی۔
وَلَوْ قَالَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ وَاحِدَةٌ فِي ثِنْتَيْنِ فَإِنْ نَوَىٰ مَعَ ثِنْتَيْنِ فَثَلَاثِ، دَخَلَ بِهَا أَوْلَا، وَإِلَّا فَإِنْ نَوَى وَ ثِنْتَيْنِ فَتَلْتُ إِنْ كَانَ دَخَلَ بِهَا وَ إِلَّا فَوَاحِدَةٌ، كَمَا إِذَا نَوَى الطَّرْفَ أَوْ أَطْلَقَ، وَلَوْ نَوَى الضَّرْبَ وَالْحِسَابَ فَكَذَلِكَ، وَ كَذَا فِي الإِقْرَارِ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر کہا تجھے ایک طلاق دو میں پس اگر نیت کی دو کے ساتھ تو تین واقع ہوگی ذخول ہوا ہو یا نہ ہوا ہورنہ ایک جیسے اگر ظرف کی نیت کی ہو یا مطلق کہا ہوا گر ضرب و حساب مراد ہوتب بھی یہی حکم ہے اور اسی طرح اقرار میں بھی ۔ تشریح : اگر کوئی شخص اپنی بیوی سے انت طالق واحدۃ فی نشتین کے تو یہاں فی والا اور مع دونوں کا احتال رکھتا ہے اب اگر مع کے معنی لئے تو ہیوی مدخول بہا ہو یا غیر مدخول بہا دونوں صورتوں میں طلاق مغلظہ واقع ہو جائے گی اور اگر واؤ کے معنی مراد لئے توبیوی کے مدخولہ ہونے کی صورت میں تینوں طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور غیر مدخول ہونے کی صورت میں ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی اس ضمن میں دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ظرف کی نیت کی یا نیت کو مطلق رکھا تو مدخولہ اور غیر مدخولہ ہر ایک پر سیاری طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی تو ظاہر مذہب کے مطابق ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی اور امام زفر کے نزدیک دو طلاق واقع ہوں گی علامہ ابن ہمام نے امام زیر کے قول کو تر جیح دی ہے۔
وَلَوْ قَالَ: أَنْتَ عَلى مِثْلَ أُمِّي، أَوْ كَامّى رَجَعَ إِلى قَصْدِهِ لِيَنْكَشِفَ حُكْمُهُ، فَإِنْ قَالَ: أردت الكرامَةَ، فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ لأن التكريم بالتشبِيْهِ فَاش فِي الْكَلَامِ وَ إِنْ قَالَ أَرَتُ الطَّهَارَ فَهُوَ ظِهَارٌ ، لأَنَّهُ تَشْبِيْة بِجَمِيعِهَا. وَإِنْ قَالَ : أَرَدْتُ الطَّلَاقِ، فَهُوَ طَلَاقَ بَائِنٌ، وَ إِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ لَهُ نِيَّةٌ، فَلَيْسَ بِشَيْ عِنْدَهُمَا، وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ: هُوَ ظِهَارٌ، وَ إِنْ عَنِى بِهِ التَّحْرِيْمَ لَا غَيْرَ ، فَعِنْدَ أَبي يُوْسُفَ إِيْلَاء وَ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ ظِهَارٌ .

تا کہ تنقیح کے بعد حکم لگایا جا سکے اگر قائل کہتا ہے کہ میری مراد اس جملہ سے تعظیم و تکریم ہے تو سبحان اللہ کیونکہ یہ الفاظ تشریح: اگر سی نے اپنی بیوی سے انت علی مثل امی کہا یا کامی تو قاتل سے معلوم کیا جائے گا کہ مقصد کیا ہے تو ظہار کا تھا تو ظہار ہی ہوگا کیونکہ ظہار تو نام ہی ہے اپنی بیوی کو ماں یا ماں کی طرح محرمات موجدہ میں سے کسی کے تعظیم و تکریم میں تشبیہ کے لئے مستعمل ہوتے ہیں اس کی نیت پر ہی فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا اور اگر متکلم یہ کہے کہ میرا مقصد ساتھ تشبیہ دینے کا اور یہاں پورے بدن کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی گئی ہے۔
کے نزدیک ایلاء اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ظہار پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر متکلم کہے کہ میرا مقصد طلاق تھا تو طلاق بائن مراد ہوگی اور مطلق رکھتا ہے کچھ نیت نہیں ہے تو امام یوسف
وَلَوْ قَالَ أَنْتَ عَلَيَّ حَرَامٌ كَأَمِّي، وَنَوَى ظِهَاراً، أَوْ طَلَاقَا فَهُوَ عَلَى مَا نَوَى، وَ إِنْ لَمْ يَنْوِ، فَعَلى قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ إِبْلَاءٌ، وَعَلَى قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ ظِهَارٌ. وَ مِنْهَا لَوْ قَرَأَ الْجُنُبُ قُرْآنًا، فَإِنْ قصَدَ الثَّلَاوَةَ حَرُمَ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ الذِّكْرَ فَلَا وَلَوْ قَرَأَ الْفَاتِحَةُ فِي صَلَاتِهِ عَلَى الْجَنَازَةِ، إِنْ فَصَدَ الدُّعَاءَ وَ الثَّناءَ لَمْ يَكْرَهُ ، وَ إِنْ قَصَدَ التَّلَاوَةَ كَرِهَ عَطَسَ الْخَطِيْبُ، فَقَالَ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، إِنْ قَصَدَ الْخُطْبَة صَحَّتْ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ الْحَمْدَ لِلْعُطَاسِ لَمْ تَصِحْ ذَبَحَ فَعَطَسَ، فَسَدَتَ وَ إِلَّا فَلَا. وَقَالَ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، فَكَذلِكَ ذَكَرَ الْمُصَلَّى آيَةً، أَوْ ذِكْراً، وَقَصَدَ بِهِ جَوَابَ الْمُتَكَلِّمِ
ترجمه : اور اگر کہا انت علی حرام کامی اور نیت ظہار کی یا طلاق کی ہو تو وہ اس کی نیت کے مطابق ہے اور اگر اس نے کوئی بھی نیت نہ کی تو ابو یوسف کے قول کے مطابق ایلاء اور امام محمد کے قول کے مطابق ظہار ہے اور ان ہی جزئیات میں سے ہے کہ اگر نبی نے قرآن پڑھا تو اگر وہ تلاوت کا ارادہ کرے تو حرام ہے اور اگر ذکر کا ارادہ ہو تو حرام نہیں اور اگر نماز جنازہ میں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھی تو اگر دعا وثناء کا ارادہ ہو تو مکر وہ نہیں اور اگر تلاوت کا ارادہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے خطیب کو چھینک آئی اس پر اس نے کہا الحمدللہ تو اگر خطبہ کا ارادہ کیا تو خطبہ درست ہے اور اگر اس نے چھینک پر اللہ کی تعریف کا ارادہ کیا تو خطبہ درست نہیں ذبح کرتے وقت چھینک آئی اور اس نے الحمد للہ کہا تو بھی یہی تفصیل ہے نماز کی
حالت میں اس نے کوئی آیت پڑھی یا ذ کر کیا اور اس سے متکلم کا جواب دینا مقصود ہے تو نماز فاسد ہے ورنہ نہیں۔
And like that, absolvic the repetition of talaq if neither the intention of renewal nor emphasis, then in that case three talaqs occur. It is known from the word 'kadha' that three talaqs occur. All these cases are about a khula woman; otherwise for a non-consummated woman, the first talaq makes her separate, the second and third are void. And if he said: 'You are divorced one in two', then if he intended 'with two', then three occur whether he consummated or not; otherwise if he intended 'and two', then three if he consummated, otherwise one. Similarly if he intended 'in' or absolute, and if he intended 'multiplication and calculation', similarly. And likewise in acknowledgment. Translation: And if he said: 'You are divorced one in two', then if he intended 'with two', then three occur whether consummated or not; otherwise if he intended 'and two', then three if consummated, otherwise one. Similarly if he intended 'in' or absolute, and if he intended 'multiplication and calculation', similarly. And likewise in acknowledgment. Explanation: If a person says to his wife 'you are divorced one in two', here the word 'fi' can mean both 'with' and 'in'. Now if he takes the meaning of 'with' then whether the wife is consummated or not, a severe talaq occurs. If he intends the meaning of 'and' then if the wife is consummated, three talaqs occur, and if not consummated, one ba'in talaq occurs. Within this, the second issue: if he intended 'in' or kept the intention absolute, then for both consummated and non-consummated, three talaqs occur. Third issue: if he intended multiplication and calculation, then according to the apparent madhhab one talaq occurs, and according to Imam Zufar two talaqs occur. Allama Ibn Hammam preferred the view of Imam Zufar. And if he said: 'You are like my mother' or 'like her', recourse is made to his intent to uncover its ruling. If he said: 'I intended honor', then it is as he said because honor through simile is common in speech. If he said: 'I intended zihar', then it is zihar because it is a simile with all of her. If he said: 'I intended talaq', then it is ba'in talaq. If he had no intention, then it is nothing according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?). Muhammad said: it is zihar. And if he meant prohibition only, then according to Abu Yusuf it is ila, and according to Muhammad it is zihar. Translation: And if he said: 'You are upon me unlawful like my mother', and he intended zihar or talaq, then it is according to his intention. If he did not intend, then according to Abu Yusuf it is ila, and according to Muhammad it is zihar. And from these issues: if a junub reads Quran, if he intended recitation, it is haram; if he intended dhikr, then not. And if he recited Fatiha in the funeral prayer, if he intended supplication and praise, it is not disliked; if he intended recitation, it is disliked. The khateeb sneezed and said 'alhamdulillah'; if he intended the khutbah, it is valid; if he intended praise for the sneeze, it is not valid. While slaughtering he sneezed and said 'alhamdulillah' similarly. The one in prayer recited a verse or dhikr and intended to answer the speaker, then the prayer is invalid; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir applies the grand legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are by intentions) to specific cases in family law and worship. The author presents several scenarios where ambiguous words uttered by a husband or worshipper are interpreted according to the speaker's intention. The first set of cases involves the phrase 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn.' The word 'fi' can mean 'with' (ma'a) or 'in' (zarf). If the husband intended 'with two', three divorces occur regardless of consummation. If he intended 'and' (waw), then three divorces only if consummated; otherwise one ba'in divorce. If he made no specific intention or intended 'in' (zarf), three divorces occur. If he intended multiplication (darb) and calculation (hisab), the apparent madhhab (Abu Hanifa) says one divorce, but Imam Zufar says two. The second set deals with 'anti 'ala mithli ummi' or 'ka-ummi'. The husband's intention determines whether it is zihar, talaq, ila, or mere honorific. If he intended honor, it is taken as such. If he intended zihar, it is zihar (a form of divorce-like prohibition). If he intended talaq, it is a ba'in talaq. If he intended only prohibition, Abu Yusuf rules it as ila (an oath of abstinence), while Muhammad rules it as zihar. The third set extends the principle to acts of worship: a junub may read Quran if intending dhikr, not recitation; reciting Fatiha in janazah prayer is disliked if intended as recitation but not if as supplication; a khateeb's sneeze response is valid only if intended as part of the khutbah; and a prayer is invalid if the worshipper intends to answer someone with a verse or dhikr. These examples illustrate that intention is central in Hanafi fiqh for distinguishing between different legal categories.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The conscious intention in the heart that distinguishes between different legal categories of an utterance.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah).
تلاوة (tilawah): Recitation of Quran with the intention of fulfilling the act of recitation.
ذكر (dhikr): Remembrance of Allah, including reciting Quran with the intention of remembrance rather than tilawah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A khateeb sneezes during the Friday khutbah and says 'alhamdulillah' intending it as part of the khutbah. Is the khutbah valid?
A) Yes, the khutbah is valid.
B) No, the khutbah is invalid.
C) It is makruh but valid.
D) The khutbah is valid only if he repeats the phrase.

Key Takeaway
In acts of worship, intention determines whether an utterance is permissible, disliked, or invalidating.

Applying al-Umur bi-Maqasidiha to Ambiguous Divorce Expressions
Application of al-umur bi-maqasidiha to ambiguous divorce-like expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim al-umur bi-maqasidiha to the phrase 'anti 'alayya haramun ka'ummi' and state the mufta bihi position when intention is absent.

Core Idea
Intention decides the ruling; without it, the Hanafi school prefers zihar over ila'.

The Islamic legal maxim al-umur bi-maqasidiha (actions are judged by intentions) resolves ambiguity in marital speech. When a husband says 'anti 'alayya haramun ka'ummi,' his intention determines whether it is zihar, talaq, or ila'. This passage from Sharah al-Ashbah applies the maxim and then addresses the internal Hanafi difference when intention is absent, showing how later scholarship chose the operative position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ambiguous Statement
The phrase 'anti 'alayya haramun ka'ummi' is legally ambiguous—it can be interpreted as zihar, talaq, or ila'.
2
Apply the Maxim al-Umur bi-Maqasidiha
If the speaker has an intention, the ruling follows that intention: if he intended zihar, it is zihar; if talaq, it is talaq; if ila', it is ila'.
This is the primary rule from the maxim.
3
Address Absence of Intention
When no intention is declared or known, the ruling is based on linguistic defaults. Here, Abu Yusuf holds it is ila', and Muhammad holds it is zihar.
Internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Ila' requires a four-month waiting period and leads to divorce if not revoked; zihar requires expiation (kaffarah) before resuming relations. The practical difference is significant.
5
Identify the Mufta Bihi
Later Hanafi scholars have preferred Imam Muhammad's view, so the operative ruling is that it is zihar when intention is absent.
This is the position used in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ أَنْتَ عَلَيَّ حَرَامٌ كَأَمِّي، وَنَوَى ظِهَاراً، أَوْ طَلَاقاً، فَهُوَ عَلَى مَا نَوَى، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْوِ، فَعَلَى قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوسُفَ إِيلَاءٌ، وَعَلَى قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ ظِهَارٌ.
And if he said, 'You are forbidden to me like my mother,' and he intended zihar or talaq, then it is according to what he intended. And if he did not intend, then according to Abu Yusuf it is ila', and according to Muhammad it is zihar.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the application of the maxim 'Actions are judged by intentions.' It presents a case where a husband says to his wife, 'You are forbidden to me like my mother.' The legal effect depends on his intention: if he intends zihar (declaring his wife like his mother), it is zihar; if he intends talaq (divorce), it is talaq. If he has no specific intention, there is an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. Abu Yusuf considers it ila' (a vow to abstain from intercourse), while Muhammad considers it zihar. This demonstrates that when wording is ambiguous, the default interpretation may differ among mujtahids. In practice, the mufti asks the questioner about his intention; if no intention is claimed, the mufti follows the stronger view in the school, which is typically Muhammad's position (zihar) in this case.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A declaration that one's wife is like one's mother, requiring expiation before resuming marital relations.
إيلاء (ila'): A vow to abstain from sexual relations with one's wife for four months or more.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, if a man says 'anti 'alayya haramun ka'ummi' without intention, it is:
A) Ila' as per Abu Yusuf
B) Zihar as per Muhammad
C) Talaq because of the word 'haram'
D) Invalid because intention is necessary

Key Takeaway
When a man says 'anti 'alayya haramun ka'ummi,' intention decides the ruling; without intention, the Hanafi mufta bihi is zihar, requiring expiation.

Junub Reciting Quran: Intention Determines the Ruling
Application of a maxim to a furu' case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to distinguish between tilawah (forbidden) and dhikr (permissible) for a junub, and state the mufta bihi for fatwa.

Core Idea
For a junub, the same Quranic words can be haram or permissible based solely on intention.

This passage presents a classic furu' case illustrating the foundational maxim 'Actions are judged by intentions.' It shows how the same act—reciting Quranic words—can be either forbidden or permissible depending solely on the niyyah. As a mufti, understanding this application is critical for issuing correct fatwas regarding ritual purity and recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing qawida
Recognize that this case is an application of the major maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (الأمور بمقاصدها).
This is one of the five major legal maxims in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Identify the act and the two intentions
The act is reciting Quranic words while in a state of janabah. The two possible intentions are tilawah (formal recitation) and dhikr (remembrance).
Tilawah is recitation for the sake of the words themselves; dhikr is using the words for remembrance of Allah.
3
Derive the ruling for each intention
Apply the maxim: if the intention is tilawah, the act is haram because it disrespects the Quran. If the intention is dhikr, it is permissible because the act becomes general remembrance.
The same words are recited, but the niyyah changes the legal category.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and note the practical consequence
The mufta bihi ruling: a junub may recite Quranic verses as dhikr (e.g., Bismillah, Alhamdulillah) but not with the specific intention of tilawah. This distinction prevents undue hardship while maintaining respect for the Quran.
In practice, a mufti should inquire about the questioner's intention if ambiguous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا لَوْ قَرَأَ الْجُنُبُ قُرْآنًا، فَإِنْ قَصَدَ التِّلَاوَةَ حَرُمَ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ الذِّكْرَ فَلَا.
And among them [the examples]: if a person in a state of janabah recites the Quran, then if he intended recitation (tilawah), it is forbidden; and if he intended dhikr, it is not [forbidden].
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is another application of the maxim 'Actions are judged by intentions.' It addresses a person in a state of major ritual impurity (junub). The act of reciting Quran is the same, but the ruling changes based on intention. If he intends to recite the Quran as a formal tilawah (recitation), it is forbidden (haram) because it is disrespectful to touch or recite Quran in that state. However, if he intends it as general dhikr (remembrance of Allah), such as saying 'Alhamdulillah' or 'Bismillah', it is permissible. This distinction prevents undue hardship while maintaining respect for the Quran.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
تلاوة (tilawah): Recitation of the Quran with the intention of worship through the words themselves.
ذكر (dhikr): Remembrance of Allah using any words, including Quranic phrases.
الأمور بمقاصدها (al-umur bi-maqasidiha): A major legal maxim: the legal classification of actions depends on the intention behind them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, if a junub recites the Quran with the intention of tilawah, what is the ruling?
A) Haram
B) Permissible
C) Makruh
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
The same Quranic words can be either haram or permissible for a junub, depending solely on the intention—tilawah or dhikr.

Intention Transforms the Ruling: Reciting Fatiha in Janazah
Ruling on reciting Fatiha in janazah with intention of dua vs tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that intention (niyyah) determines the ruling of an act in ibadat, specifically differentiating between dua and tilawah in janazah prayer.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, intention can transform the same act from permissible to disliked.

This lesson examines a precise application of the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions). We will analyze a ruling from the Ashbah wa al-Nazair concerning reciting Al-Fatiha in the funeral prayer. The same act of recitation is ruled not disliked when intended as supplication but disliked when intended as formal recitation. Understanding this distinction is key to mastering how intention shapes fiqh rulings in ibadat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is reciting Al-Fatiha in salat al-janazah. Note that janazah prayer is primarily for supplication (dua), not recitation (tilawah).
2
Identify the two possible intentions
The source text specifies 'qasada al-dua wa al-thana' (intention of supplication and praise) vs. 'qasada al-tilawah' (intention of recitation as Quran).
3
Note the ruling for each intention
With intention of dua, it is not makruh. With intention of tilawah, it is makruh (disliked).
4
Extract the underlying principle
The ruling depends on intention because the nature of the act changes. This is a furu' (branch) of the qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
5
Generalize the principle
This principle applies across ibadat: the same physical action can have different rulings based on intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَرَأَ الْفَاتِحَةَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ عَلَى الْجَنَازَةِ، إِنْ قَصَدَ الدُّعَاءَ وَالثَّنَاءَ لَمْ يَكْرَهْ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ التِّلَاوَةَ كَرِهَ.
And if he recited Al-Fatiha in his prayer over the deceased, if he intended supplication and praise, it is not disliked; and if he intended recitation (tilawah), it is disliked.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage applies the same principle to the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). Reciting Surat al-Fatiha in the janazah prayer is generally done as a supplication (dua) for the deceased. The ruling depends on intention: if the worshipper intends it as dua and praise of Allah (thana), it is not disliked (makruh) because that is the purpose of the prayer. But if he intends it as formal tilawah (recitation of the Quran as such), it becomes makruh, because the janazah prayer is not primarily a prayer for recitation but for supplication. This shows how the same action can be recommended or disliked based on intention.

Key Terms
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer performed over a deceased Muslim.
نية (niyyah): Intention, a key factor in determining the ruling of an act in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, reciting Al-Fatiha in janazah prayer is makruh in which case?
A) Intention of dua and praise
B) Intention of tilawah
C) Intention of salah
D) Reciting loudly

Key Takeaway
Intention determines the ruling of reciting Al-Fatiha in janazah prayer: if intended as supplication, it is not disliked; if intended as Quranic recitation, it is disliked.
